\c 00
\t Senufo Supyire Project
\p
\co Senufo Supyire Cultural Background: The Senufo Supyire people are typically
farmers, living in close community with one another.  Everything is done in
community:  from farming, working the fields, to cooking rotations, to meetings, to
village decisions, to naming a child, to building a new village hut, to making tea -
there are few things in life here that is not done in fellowship of others.  A Senufo
Supyire proverb is "One finger alone cannot lift a pebble" ... "One hand cannot wash
itself."  Oftentimes, priority is placed on the relationship and not on a task or need of
an individual.  Much effort is placed in maintaining relationship, and in avoiding
breaking a relationship.  The Supyire people are typically animistic, African Traditional
Religion, and seek power in life through sacrifices to their intermediaries: spirits, or
fetishes.  While striving for power, daily life is spent struggling to meet their
everyday basic needs.  The power they are seeking is for provision in this life and for
the life after.
\p
\co Islam and Christianity Influence on Supyire Culture:  There are both Islam and
Christianity influences present within Supyire culture.  However, it appears that
even with the presence of these, they are typically only a veneer covering their
deeper traditional beliefs.  It is very common within the Supyire culture to participate
in the practices of multiple religions concurrently, synchronizing them or adding the
practice of Islam or Christianity to their current traditional beliefs and practices.  For
example, on one day, we witnessed a sacrifice to an animistic god with the
participation of our village friends.  These same friends then went to the mosque
and celebrated the Islamic religious holidays.  Also, it is apparent that geography and
location of each village is a factor in determining the level of Islamic or Christian
influence.  As there are several towns along the main paved road between the
capital and a second large city, these towns have drastically greater Christian and
Islamic influences.  There are more western-style buildings for worship as well as
greater communication available with telephone cabines, easier radio access, and a
constant flow of travellers.  However, the further away one travels from this main
road, the less Christian and Islamic influence is present.  There is a much greater
animistic present in the village where we spent the most time, only 12 km away
from the paved road, than in the main town where we lived.
\p             
\co Redemptive Themes:  
\co (1) Relationship.  Through belief in Jesus Christ, there can be a good relationship
between man and God.   
\co (a)  Problem:  When God created the world, there was a good relationship between
man and God.  This relationship between man and God was broken by the sins of
man.  Man is now cursed and will one day die and be judged by God.  Those who are
not on God's road, will be thrown into an a fire that cannot be extinguished.
\co (b) - Hope, Pointing to a solution:  There can be a good relationship between man
and God, through belief and trust in God.  There is someone coming, sent from God,
who will take the penalty for man's sin.  He will restore the relaitonship between
man and God.  He will save people from the fire that cannot be extinguished by
believing in Him.
\co (c) - Solution:  Jesus.  God's Son, Jesus, comes to save people.  He has been sent
by God to restore the relationship between man and God.  He suffered and died for
the sins of man.  He rose three days later and then ascended into heaven to be with
God.  Those who believe in Jesus, those who leave their old road and take Jesus'
road, can have a good relationship with God and be saved from the fire that never
ends, and be given life forever with God.
\co (d) Response:  The theme will call people to belief in Jesus.  It should call people to
be baptized to show that they have left their old road and taken Jesus' road.  God will
forgive their sins, restoring relationship with them, and offering them life forever
with Him.  The story set should show would those who are on Jesus' road, who are
in a restored relationship with God, should do:  be obedient to God, study His Words,
be in community with other believers, go and tell others.
\p
\co (2) Power and Provision:  Intertwined with the theme of relationship, is a subtheme
of power and provision.  God is the all-powerful victorious God who provides for the
needs of those that are in relationship with Him, that are on His road.
\co (a) Problem:  God created a world in which man was well taken care of and provided
for by Him.  However, as sin entered, the fallen world was a world full of evil and full
of hardship.  A world in which humans will one day die and face judgement and
anger from God.
\co (b) Hope, Pointing to Solution:  The story set shows that God can use His power to
provide for the needs of those who have a relationship with Him.  God has power
over nature, over sickness, over evil spirits.  God has power to give wisdom to
people and direct daily actions in a way the provides for them.  God is powerful, over
all other beings and things on earth.  God is a God who cares for the needs of His
people.  God will one day send a king, someone who will reign forever, be powerful,
and bring peace to people.
\co (c) Solution:  God's ultimate power and provision for those who follow Him was the
sending of His Son, Jesus.  Jesus and God are one.  Jesus has the power of God. 
Jesus died and rose again, conquering death.  Those who believe in Jesus have
access to God's Power through the coming of His Spirit.  Ultimately, God's power is
passed on to believers through victory over death and eternal life with God.
\co (d) Response:  This subtheme should call people to belief in Jesus, recognizing Jesus
as God's Son and as the all-powerful provider because He has provided a way to gain
eternal life with God, power over death, provision for this life and after.
\p

\p
\co Comment on availability of scripture in mother-tongue language:  An SIL team has
been working on the translation of the NT.  There has been an electronic draft of the
NT available for use and reference during this project. The NT was printed as of Oct
08 and distributed Dec08. There is also a draft in progress of Genesis, parts of
Exodus, and Ruth.
\p
\co There has been an SIL presence in the ethno-center of the Supyire people for 20+
years.  Outside of the NT draft, several products have been written regarding the
Senufo Supyire culture and language.  Michael Jemphrey‚Äôs thesis, ‚ÄúThrough the
shedding of blood‚Äù, and the Supyire - Lexique Pro Dictionary by Robert Carlson
proved to be valuable resources during language and culture study and research.
\p    
\co The Story crafter we have been working with is a believer named Sitapha.  He also
works as a night guard and office worker for SIL, and is often a worship leader at the
church we attend.  He and his family live in the same town where we live.  = SS.
\p
\co The backtranslator for the project is a young educated man who came back from
college in Bamako to work as a head master of a school in the city nearest to our
town.  He is not a Christian; however, he openly discusses the beliefs and culture
around him.  = BK.
\p
\co Typical Testing Groups Throughout Story Set:
\co Language Helper in Village:  This was our first testing group for all stories.  Our
village language helper (for language learning) is a 25 yr old male, has some
education and spent some time in the nearby city, but has lived the most recent
part of his life in the village.  He has recently become a bptzd believer.
\co Group of Women in Village:  This group varies, and sometimes is combined with the
testing session with our language helper.  These women are highly oral learners,
most are uneducated, all are UNS.  They primarily practice animism.
\co Group of Men in Nearby Village:  This is a testing group of between 5-10 men who
are predominately animistic or African Traditional Religion, all are UNS.  Some do
practice Islam as well.  This group has varied in attendance, but has had a
consistant group of 4-5 hearing most stories.
\co Day Guard friend:  This is a young educated male who works as a day guard in our
town.  He is a UNS.  He has told us that this is the first time he has heard these
stories.
\co Woman Friends at Boutique:  These are two women who work at a local store in
town.  They are both UNS.  The two of them often rotate work duties at the store,
however, at least one is usually available for story testing.
\co Phone booth friend:  A woman friend of ours who is readily available for testing as
she works at a phone cabine here in town.  She is married into a Muslim family;
however, she has attended church here in town a few times.  Many of the stories,
she is hearing for the first time.  She was a testing respondent primarily as a source
for story retellability and not for worldview probing questions, as she has the most
Christian influence of our test groups.
\p

\c 01
\t Creation - New
\co Supyire
\p
\co Redemptive Theme:  This initial story shows God's power over all by creating all
things.  The story shows God's provision for man and good relationship with man in
the beginning.
\co Basic Biblical concepts :  God is maker of all heaven and earth.
\co Cohesion / Background:  This initial story sets the stage prior to a problem.  The
story also sets up the future problem by introducing the one tree that gives
knowledge of good and bad that man and woman were not to eat of.
\co Worldview / Selection Issues :  As most Supyire believe in a Creator God, this story
should serve as a bridge.  
\p
\co Story crafter's name or initials: SS
\co Backtranslator's name or initials: BK  
\co Resources Used:  "La Bible - Parole De Vie" French Bible, Bambara (Trade language)
Bible, Supyire Draft of Genesis
\p
\co BT file revised 10/21/08
\co Audio Revised 10/17/08
\p
\tst General Testing Comments:  Tst3 = One gentleman, day guard, NGo.  This was the first
time working with our friend.  Some of the details of the creation of the things on earth
were omitted, potentially because of this first time working with him, not knowing what to
expect, and performance error.  See specific line number for further detail.
\p
\tst General Testing Comments:  Tst2 = Group of men and one woman at a boutique in
town.   The retelling of the story has gone well the several times this new version has
been tested.  Sometimes a few of the details of what was created when gets out of order
chronologically.  The details of how the man and woman were made are retold well.  The
simplification of the part in which God placed them in a garden, and told them they could
eat of the fruit of all the trees except one ... this part was clear, understood, and retold
well.  It was emphasized and the connection between this and the Fall story was made
well.  It was also understood that life in the garden was good - there was a lot to eat
there.    Overall, the testing sessions and retellability went well.
\p
\tst Tst3 (retest):  Upon editing and revising, the story was tested again, both for retellability
and to probe a few issues further.  See comments below.
\tst Tst5 - Tested a few further probing issues with friend at phone booth.  
\p
\ln 01.01
\bt This is something that happened which is also true.
\anc 2Ti.03:16 , Psa.119:142 (New Century Version) "...your teachings are true";
Psa.119:160 (NIV) "all your words are true"; Jhn.17:17 "your word is truth".
\cn MM:  This is a typical introduction to our stories.  This seems to be a culturally
appropriate way to introduce a story and to set this story apart as a true story rather
than a fable or cultural story that may be untrue.
\ln 01.02
\bt Before the beginning of the {world}, {God} was there.
\anc Jhn.01:01 - 2 ; 1Ti.01:17
\cn MM:  Here is the first reference to the key term God.  This term is used throughout the
story set and will not be bracketed in future references.
\tst Tst3: Before the world existed, what do you think was there?  God.  God only.  People
here think that God created the world and put people on it.  People think God created the
earth, animals, trees, people.
\tst Tst3: The initial line of the story, line 02 was omitted in the retelling.  He made an initial
statement to say "God gave these words about the world.  God created the world."  The
word he used here in the retelling is the word that is inclusive of the earth, heavens,
land, water, animals, and all things on the earth.  It may be a good idea to simply add
this statement after or in conjunction with the current line 02.  "Before the world, God
was there.  God created the world."  Line 01.02b added.
\ln 01.02b
\bt God created {KT: create} the world.
\anc Gen.01:01
\ln 01.03
\bt God created the heavens [KT: {above}], created the {earth}, and
created the water.
\old Then God created the earth and [created] the water, and created the above.
\anc Gen.01:01 , Gen.01:02 , Gen.01:09 - 10 , Job.38:08 -11 , TW: The heavens and the
earth is the Hebrew way of speaking of all that existed. It is an idiom made up of two
opposites, like the expression ìgood and evil,î and in this context it means the universe,
or everything in the universe, and not just the earth and the sky.  Therefore, water was
included in this.
\cn MM:  The word for "earth" here, which is the same word used in the Supyire draft,
means literally dirt or ground.  It does not include water. Therefore, when it says God
made the heavens and earth, it is not clear that He put the water on earth.  It is made
explicit for this reason.
\ln 01.04a
\bt Darkness covered the world.  
\old And let all the kinds of trees to rise on the earth.
\anc Gen.01:02
\tst Tst3(retest):  In final retelling, he states, "Darkness was there."  We discussed this
concept further with individuals and they explained it as the whole world was in
darkness.  The whole world was dark.  As this expression is understood, it will not be
changed.
\ln 01.04b
\bt And God said, "Light come."  And the light came.  
\anc Gen.01:03
\ln 01.04c
\old When God saw the light, he said, "It is good."
\anc Gen.01:04
\tst Tst2:  Why does God say "It is good" when He sees the light?  It was dark all over
before.  Now it's light.  Everything becomes clear and bright.  It is a good thing for
everyone to have light.
\tst Tst3:  In multiple testing sessions, as well as this one, this line was omitted.  This line
may be cut from the story set as it is difficult to retell.
\tst Based on retellings, this line has been deleted.  
\ln 01.05
\bt God said, "All kinds of grass, all kinds of trees, grow on the earth."  
\old And created light and [created] the darkness
\anc Gen.01:11 - 12
\ln 01.06a
\bt God created the sun, created the moon, and created the stars.  
\old And created the moon and the sun, and [created] the stars.  And created all the animals.
\anc Gen.01:14 - 18
\ln 01.06b
\bt God created all the birds, the fish, the field animals, and all the
animals.  
\anc Gen.01:21 - 22 , Gen.01:24 -25
\tst Tst3:  In the retelling, he chronologically mixed up the creation of the grass and things
on the earth with the calling of the light to come.  He omitted the details of the creation
of the animals, birds, etc.. and simply said "all things on earth."  He also  left out the
creation of the sun, moon, and stars.  However, in the multiple other re-tellings these
details were included.  Being the first time working with Tst3, these omissions were most
likely performance error and do not warrant a change in story text.
\ln 01.06c
\bt And God looked at the world and said, "It is good."
\anc Gen.01:10 , Gen.01:12 , Gen.01:18 , Gen.01:21 , Gen.01:25
\tst Why did God look at the world and say "IT's good."?  God knows that His work is good.  
\tst Tst2:  Why did God say "It is good" after he looked at the world?  Because He put the
light there.  He made the birds, the animals, the fish, the grass, the trees - all of this is
good.
\ln 01.07
\bt One day, He took the mud and built it into a human being [MM gave it
the shape of a person], and blew breathing-air into his nose.
\anc Gen.02:07
\cn MM:  The term used and backtranslated here as "mud" is the same term used in the
Senufo draft of Genesis.
\tst Tst2:  Why does God make man?  He wanted people on the earth.  Also, it's like, I am
sitting here alone - that's not good for me.  I want you to come and be here with me -
when you are here, it's good for me.  (companionship is good).
\tst Tst2:  How does God blow air into the man's nose?  God blew air into him to give him
life.  He blew air into him so that the man could start respiration.
\ln 01.08
\bt And it became a person.  His name was Adam.
\old And it became a person.  He named him Adam.
\anc Gen.02:07 , Gen.02:20 , as in TN in Gen.03:20 states, "As mentioned in the note on
3:17a, the Hebrew word 'aDam can be translated as ‚Äúman‚Äù or as the name ‚ÄúAdam‚Äù.  
English translations of Genesis vary somewhat as to when they transition from
translating the Hebrew word "Adam" as "man" to translating it with the name "Adam".
\tst Why did God make man?  To do His work.  To work.   
\tst tst3:  He omitted the name of the man in retelling, which was unusual.  This has been
retold in every other retelling.  So, we will not make any changes based on this one time
event.
\ln 01.09
\bt Then He let him in a garden he had created
\old And [MM: God] let him [MM: the man] in the {garden}.
\anc Gen.02:15
\tst Tst2:  What is in a garden (chee-ckworray)?  Lots of trees.  Trees are everywhere.  Like
a plantation or garden (plantation and jardin in French).  It is a really good place.
\tst Tst2:  Why does God let the man in the garden?  There are lots of trees there - fruits are
there.  They can eat all the fruit except one tree.  It's good that the man is in the garden
because there is food to eat.
\ln 01.10
\bt There were all kinds of trees in that garden.  Their fruits were pretty.
\anc Gen.02:09
\tst Was God good to the man?  Yes.  Why?  Life was good in the garden.  There was lots to
eat there.
\tst Tst3:  In retelling, Line 10 was omitted and it jumped straight from putting man in the
garden, to God telling man he could eat of all the fruits of all the trees except one. 
However, this line has been retold in every other retelling.  It emphasizes the goodness
of the garden and shows the care in which God went to to place the man in a good
environment.  This line will not be cut, also based on the fact that the explicit statement
that "life is good in the garden" in Line 20 may be deleted.
\ln 00.11
\bt Then God said to Adam, "You can eat all the fruit except one tree"
\old And told Adam that he can eat all the fruits in the garden, but there is one tree he should
not eat the fruit of.  He will die the day he eats it.
\anc Gen.02:16 - 17
\tst Tst2:  Why is there one tree that the man cannot eat the fruit of?  He will die if he eats
it.  But this is a question that the man (one of the test group men) asked himself, "Why
would God say he could not eat of that fruit?")  They said that the answer to this question
was not told in this story.  They did not further comment on what they thought a possible
answer might be.  Also, as far as learnability is concerned, our language helper has now
heard this version of the story several times, and retells it often (often times he corrects
me if I get something out of order or my Supyire is not absolutely correct).  So it is
learnable.
\tst Tst3:  Why is there one tree that the man cannot eat the fruit of?  God told the man he
could eat all the fruit of all the tree, except that one.  Why would God say that he could
not eat the fruit of that tree?  God gave them all the other fruit of all the other trees to
eat, but that one is His tree.  It's His tree.  He gave them everything.  They could have
everything, but that one tree was His.  Why do you think the man will die if he eats that
fruit?  God said he would die.  Why do you think this is?  God said if they ate the fruit of
that tree they would die.  People would die and all people would be finished.  God did not
want people to be finished, but He created them and would kill them if they ate the fruit
of that tree.
\tst Tst3:  Is the fruit of the tree poisonous?  Yes.  If they eat it they will die.  Who made the
tree?  God made the tree.  Why would God make a tree with poisonous fruit on it?  God
made the trees.  The trees are good.  Some trees just have poisonous things on them
that people cannot eat.  People should trust God's words, but everybody does not trust
God's words.  He tells them not to eat the fruit of that tree, if they trust Him, they will not
eat it.
\tst Tst3 (retest):  Talk to me about the trees in the garden.  God created them all for them
to eat of.  God is their boss, their leader.  He gave them an entire garden of trees to eat
from.
\tst Tst3 (retest):  This one tree is there that they cannot eat from.  Why?  He wanted them
to know that he was their God, their chief.  He blessed them and gave them the entire
garden.  He wanted them to fear and respect Him because He is God.  That tree would
kill them.
\tst Tst3 (retest):  Why would He not want them to eat from this tree?  Because it was God's
will for them to not eat the fruit of that tree.  If they ate the fruit of that tree, they would
die.
\ln 01.12a
\bt If you eat the fruit of that tree, you will know good and know bad {KT:
sin}.
\anc Gen.02:17 , Gen.02:09 , TN states, " That is, ‚Äúthe tree whose fruit causes people who eat
it to know good and evil‚Äù
\tst Tst3(retest):  Why does God not want them to know good and know bad?  Because he
does not want them to know, it is not good for God if they know good and bad.  God told
them not to eat the fruit of this tree, he told them not to because he doesn't want them
to know things, to be scared, and to die.  God helped them.  He gave them an entire
garden to eat from, but this one tree was His tree.  You came on your motorcycle. If you
told me not to touch it, I would not because you told me to.  Does this make someone's
insides bad?  Does this make God bad?  No.  It is just what God told them to do.  It was
His tree and He told them not to eat of it.
\tst Tst3 (retest) : in retelling, this new added line was retold.  
\tst Tst5:  What kinds of things do you think he might know about that would be bad?  They
will know death, suffering, tiredness.  Bad is when their work is bad or they have
accidents.  Or they are bad.  It could be when you wake up without food and water,
when you don't have food to eat at meals.
\ln 01.12b
\bt If you eat the fruit of that tree, you will die.
\old You will die the day you eat them.
\old There were these two trees in the garden.  One was the tree of knowing good and
knowing bad.  The other one was the tree of life.
\tst How did the man know not to eat the fruit of one tree?  God told him.  
\anc Gen.02:17
\cn In testing, it was still misunderstood and unclear.  The trees are confusing, their names
are confusing.  We have simplified this part of the story.  The point is clear that they can
eat of all the trees in the garden, except for one tree.
\old 02.13
\old And asked him not to eat the fruit of the tree of knowing good and bad.  He will die when
he eats it.
\old Gen.02:16 - 17
\cn Line 13 has been deleted.
\ln 01.14
\old And let him to take care of the garden.
\anc Gen.02:15
\tst What kind of things will he do in the garden?  He is the guardian of the garden.  He will
take care of it.  He will farm. 
\ln 01.15
\bt One day, God said, "It is not good to let Adam alone.  I am going to
make him a helper who's going to be fitting for him."
\old One day, God said, "It is not good to let Adam alone.  I am going to give him a helper
who's going to be himself."
\old One day, he noticed [MM: saw] that it is not good to let Adam alone.  That he's going to
give him a helper.
\anc Gen.02:18
\cn MM:  Here the phrase "fitting for him" is what is used in the Supyire Genesis draft.
\tst Tst2:  Why does God say it not good for Adam to be alone?  God wanted someone to
help work with Adam.  The world can not be full of people without the woman.  Without a
wife, it's just him.  That's not good.
\tst Tst2:  How will a "helper be himself"?  God will give the man another to help him.  This
other will be one that is like him.  How is this helper like him?  He is like him.  (This
phrase was just reiterated.)  Who would someone like him be?  The woman is someone
like him.  (comme lui in French)
\tst Tst3:  Why is it not good for man to be alone?  It's not good to be alone.  It's not good to
work by yourself.  He needs a helper.
\tst Tst3:  What does it mean that "to be himself"?  It means the helper will be like his family
and do the work of his family.  For example, this man is a Sanogo (His family name is
Sanogo) and comes from this "Sanogo home".  God made a "Berte" (the man's wife's
family name) to join him and help him to do his work.
\tst Tst3:  In retelling, in line 15, he did not word the phrase "who will be himself" phrase the
same way, but basically said the helper will be "like him".  This may be a better way to
state this.  However, this also does not coincide with the Supyire draft.  Based on the
fact that the phrase the craftor has used does not seem to be any more re-tellable than
the Supyire draft phrasing, we will match that of the draft to state that God will give him
a helper who will be "fitting/suitable" for him.
\tst Tst3 (retest):  In retelling, he now matches the revised "fitting for him" phrase.
\tst Tst5:  When someone is fitting for you, how would you describe that person?  He said
that about Awa because she was good for him and came to help him in the garden.  She
came from his rib.  She was good for him because it is not good  to be alone.  My
husband would say that about me because I help him and work for him.  I am fitting for
him.  What ways might they be fitting?  She came from him, they are one.  She was his
to help him because it was not good for him to be alone, so God made her from his rib. 
She will live, and eat, and learn together and this is how they are fitting.

\ln 01.20b  
\bt There was a good alliance [MM: {relationship}] between the man and
woman and God. 
\anc Gen.03:08 - 09 , Hamilton Commentary on Genesis 3:8 in TW says "The verb used here
to describe the divine movement...suggests iterative and habitual aspects. Such walks
would take place in the early evening.  The Wycliffe Bible Commentary states of these
verses, "The loving Creator could not overlook their disobedience, nor could he leave
quivering sinners in their poignant need. They were his own. His holiness must come,
clothed with love, to seek, find, and judge them. ... Of course God knew where the man
and woman were. But he was appealing to them, seeking through tenderness and love to
win a favorable response." 
\anc Gen.01:26 -30  "And God said, Let us make man in our image, after our likeness"  The
Wycliffe Bible Commentary, Electronic Database states in regard to this verse, "It is
clear that man, as God made him, was distinctly different from the animals already
created. He stood on a much higher plateau, for God created him to be immortal, and
made him a special image of His own eternity. Man was a creature with whom his Maker
could visit and have fellowship and communion."
\tst Tst3:  How is there a good relationship between the man, woman, and God?  There work
was one.  They were all doing one work, like when everyone works together.  It means
they have good relations with each other.
\tst Tst2:  In the retelling, the specific line about how the relationship between man, woman
and God was good was omitted in the retelling, but was brought up in the line of testing
questions.  Due to a subtheme of relationship and based on the fact it has been retold
before and was brought up on its own in questioning, this line will not be cut.

\dt 31/Dec/2008

\c 02
\t The Fall Story
\co Supyire
\p
\co Redemptive Theme:  The story shows the need for restored relationship with God as
now the good relationship has been broken by the disobedience of man.  God's
power is seen as he removes sinful man from His provision in the garden and curses
man to a life of hardship and death.
\co Basic Biblical concepts :  Sin is disobedience to God's instruction.  There are
consequences to sin - the breaking of relationship between man and God.
\co Cohesion / Background:  The story continues with man and woman in the garden
from the previous story.  Cohesive use of tree that gives knowledge of good and bad
as woman eats the fruit because she wants to be intelligent like God.  Sin's
consequence  is cohesively defined in terms of the redemptive theme of
"relationship".
\p
\co Story crafter:  SS
\co Backtranslator:  BK      
\co Resourses used in crafting: Audio versions of Bambara Bible, Supyire Genesis draft,
La Bible Parole De Vie (French Bible)
\p
\co Audio last edited: Oct 17, 08
\co BT file edited Oct 21, 08
\p
\tst Testing Results:  This story was re-told very well.  As questions were asked throughout
the testing session large portions of the story were also retold in addition to their
responce.

\tst General Testing Comments:  Tst2:  One gentlemen, Ngo.  In the newest testing session
our tester retold this story with great detail.  Overall, the retelling of dialogue was
accurate and level of detail retained.
\p
\tst Tst2 (Retest):  Retested again for retellability and to probe further questions.  See
comments below.   
\p

\bt This is something true that happened, 
\old So, the animals and birds that God created were not as cunning as the snake.  The

\ln 02.01a 
\bt After God created {KT: create} the {world}, He let the man and
woman in the {garden}.  The animals and birds that God created were
not as cunning as the snake.  The snake was the most cunning.
\old The animals and birds that God created {KT: create} were not as cunning as the snake. 
The snake was the most cunning.
\anc GEN.03:01
\anc Anchor for "letting them in the garden" : Gen.02:15
\tst How was the snake the most cunning?  he was the most intellegent of the animals but
Adama was still over him, 
\cn MM:  Here, the word "cyiige" is the term used in the Supyire NT & Gen drafts as
"cunning".  It means to be clever, smart, aware.  "When a child is smart lots of things
stay in his memory."  It can also mean, to make intelligent, "I made the child
intelligent."  it can also mean "to tip someone off, example: the guards had installed
themselveds on the road he was taking so i tipped him off and he went back."  We have
seen this word used to describe a person who is trying to take advantage of a person or
family.

the woman what they could eat, but said, "The snake went to the woman in the garden
and asked her what she could eat."  However, because the remainder of the diaolgue
between the woman & snake was told well, and this was told in previous retellings, the
direct dialogue will be maintained here.  He is using the same terms we use in the story.
\tst Tst2 (retest):  In retest, again, he does not say "Did God ask.." , but states, "Can you
eat..."  This may stem from a mistunderstanding that the snake is actually not trying to

draft here).  Revised.

\ln 02.21
\bt Then God chased the man and the woman out of the garden.  
\anc gen.03:23
\cn MM:   Here, the word "chased" can also be expressed as "kicked out" or "to make
something leave", to "force away".  It does not have to literally mean "chasing" in a
physical sense, but can mean "to make something leave" through words. This is the
word used in the Supyire draft for this verse.
\tst Why did God chase them from the garden?  Because they did these bad things and ate
the fruit he told them not to eat
\ln 02.21a
\old {Why?}  Because they ate the fruits of the tree that God told them not to eat. 
\old Why?  Because they refused God‚Äôs promise.  They ate the fruits of the tree that God
showed them not to eat. 
\old Then He said now they may be like me.  He knows the different between bad and good.
\old Then He said now you, man, may be like me.  He knows the difference between bad and
good. 
\cn BK explained that "they refused God's promise" can also be said that they betrayed God
or did not hold to the promise he had given them, which was to not eat of the fruit of the
one tree.  BK also explained "the relationship between them and God became hard" to
be that the relationship is broken.  It is what you would say when something happens
between people and they can no longer be together, help each other, work together... 
We know that the relationship between God and man was forever changed at this
moment, we see in in 3:22 that it is clear that he now knows the difference between
good and evil, the Lord then expelled them from the garden 3:23.
\anc gen.03:07 , gen.03:11 , Gen.03:22- 23 
\tst Why did they refuse God's promise?  because he gave them  the words and told them
not to eat the fruit of the one tree when they could eat of the fruit of all the trees in the

\tst What kinds of things did God promise them?  to eat all the trees in the garden but the
one, God was with them, walking and talking with them
\tst Tst2:   In retelling, he did tell of the hardness of their betweens / relationship between
them and God (line 21b), but he did not state line 21a, as to explain why God kicked
them out of the garden, even though this was an area that he talked about with us
during the questioning time.  This first sentence in line 21a may be omitted.  It is made
clear in the remainder of the sentence that they disobeyed God (refused His promise) by
eating the fruits of the tree God showed them not to eat. The fact that "they refused
God's promise" does not seem to be necessary and was omitted in retelling.
\tst Tst2 (retest):  This line was not retold in retesting and is implied throughout the story.

\dt 31/Dec/2008

\c 04
\t Noah Story
\co Supyire
\p
\p
\co Redemptive Theme:  The story points to God saving those who have a good
relationship with Him.  The story shows that God uses His power for the provision of
those in good relationship with Him.
\co Basic Biblical concepts: God's all-powerful nature.  God's goodness is seen in His
hate for all things evil.    
\co Cohesion / Background:  The story connects the broken relationship with God and
sin entering the world, to now a world full of sin and evil.  Cohesively defines Noah
as a man in a good relationship with God.
\co Worldview / Selection Issues:  As many Supyire believe the only access to God is
through intermediaries or other spirit beings and do not believe a direct relationship
with God is possible, this story builds on what a relationship with God is, as Noah
hears from God and obeys.
\p
\co Story Crafter:  SS
\co Story Backtranslator:  BK
\co Resources Used in Crafting:  Audio versions of Bambara Bible, Supyire draft of
Genesis, and La Bible Parole De Vie (French Bible)
\co Audio Latest Revision 10/21/08
\co BT File Latest Revision 10/21/08

\tst General Testing Comments from 8/15/08:  Tst Group 4 - Friend at Shop in Town:  Our
woman friend at the shop retold the entire story front to back.  She actually expanded
parts of the story.  For example,  she explained that God sent Adam and Awa out of the
garden because they had done something wrong against him and ate of the fruit of the
tree (remembering the previous stories). She expanded and included that God was
angry because there was sin everywhere and darkness everywhere on earth.   I was
impressed with the details that she remembered, everything from God closing the boat,
to God not forgetting them, to God blowing wind, to the number of days it rained, to the
figures of speech like the earth drinking the water, to a small detail like Nu and his
family praising God, to the idea that there will always be a rainy season and dry, cold
and heat, night and day.  See further details within BT lines.
\p
\tst General Testing Comments 8/22/05:  Tst5:  Day Guard.  The retelling of this story was
not as strong as Tst4.  There were some items that were summarized and some that
were skipped all-together.  See comments within BT text for further details of the
retelling.
\p

\anc gen.06:05 , gen.06:06
\cn MM:  This expression "God's face was soured" is the literal translation meaning "to be
grieved, upset".  It is how the Supyire Draft translates "God was grieved in his heart".
\cn KH:  The Supyire word "pege" means corruption, wicknedness, violence, evil, or ill will. 
This is the term used in the Gen Supyire draft in both the Fall to describe the "nastiness"
placed between the snake and woman, Gen.03:15, & Noah, Gen.06:05, stories.  An
example of this would be "The evil which is in you against you God causes to come back
on yourself."  We have seen this when people talk about how people have come to harm
them or to do something through a fetish against a person or village.  We have seen
sacrifices left in public places specifically to bring an evil against another.  This word can
descrie this action especially if you are on the receiving end.
\tst Tst4:  How is nastiness everywhere?  It is like darkness.  It is everywhere.  Is it a good
thing?  The things they were doing were not good.
\tst Tst5:  What does it look like for nastiness to be everywhere?  People are not doing good
things, they were doing bad things.  Is there any nastiness here in Mali?  Yes.  An
example is sometimes people capture and kill other people for money.  That is evil. 
Sometimes husbands beat or kill their wives or wives kill their men.  How do people
know what are good things and what are bad things?  A person knows what a good thing
is to himself, what is good for himself can be good for another.
\tst Why is God's face sour?  He is angry.  The people are doing evil.

\anc gen.06:09
\cn MM:  The word for right, "t√¨√¨" has several meanings.  It can mean to go straight, in the
directional literal meaning.  ‚ÄúDo not turn right here, but go straight.‚Äù  It can also mean
‚Äúto be correct, right‚Äù.  As in, ‚ÄúWhat you are doing, is not right.‚Äù  We have heard this used
to describe people or their actions as being right or not right in the moral sense of the
word (as in English). When added to the end of another word, it can also mean simple,
not complex.  i.e. ‚Äúarajo-tiiwe‚Äù means ‚Äúa simple, non-complex radio.‚Äù  This is the word
used in the Supyire Gen. as NT draft to mean ‚Äúright‚Äù or ‚Äúrighteousness.‚Äù   Examples: It is
used in Gen. 6:9 to describe Noah‚Äôs relationship with God.  Also, in Gen 15:6 for
‚Äúrighteousness‚Äù, ‚ÄúAbram believed the LORD, and he credited it to him as righteousness.‚Äù 
It is found in the NT in Romans 10, for righteousness ‚ÄúSince they did not know the
righteousness that comes from God and sought to establish their own, they did not
submit to God's righteousness.  Christ is the end of the law so that there may be
righteousness for everyone who believes.‚Äù
\tst Why did God like Noah?  Because Noah did God's work.  He was "right" before God.

\tst Tst5:  Why did God choose Nu?  Nu was afraid of God.  Nu praised God and sought God.

\ln 04.26
\bt And God blew the wind and the water started going down
\anc gen.08:01
\cn MM  We have used the same expression as in the Supyire draft.  It basically means that
God caused the wind to come.  Many times in Supyire, an action that occurs is
automatically credited to God.  For example, you say, "God sweeps the road."   It
doesn't mean that He literally "sweeps" the road, but it means that God causes the road
to be free from obstacles.  The same type of expression is used here.
\tst Tst4:  Why did God blow wind?  He blew the wind so the water would go back down into
the earth, so that you would see the ground again.
\tst Again, this line was said word for word in Tst4 retelling, however it was forgotten in Tst5
retelling.  However, it was discussed through the line of questioning.

\ln 04.39

\tst Tst4:  What does this look like?  It means that dry seasons won't end and rainy seasons
will not finish.  It's good that these don't end.  If these things stop, the world would end.

\ln 04.40

\anc gen.08:22
\ln 04.41

\anc gen.09:11
\tst This line was omitted in both retellings.  This repetition then only serves to make the
story longer and can be deleted.
\cn MM:  This line has been deleted based on ommision in retelling.
\ln 04.42
\bt When the dark sky is seen, I will bring the rainbow.  This rainbow will
be a sign of my alliance.  
\old The rainbow will appear.  This rainbow will be a sign of my alliance.
\anc gen.09:13 - 15
\cn MM:  This phrase "when the dark sky is seen" has always been in this line.  It was
omitted by the BTer.  However, in discussions with our craftor, he stated that it would not
be natural to cut this phrase, because it's only when the sky is dark, that a rainbow can
be seen to have appeared.
\cn MM:  The Supyire word for "rainbow" literally translates as "Rain's machete"  We have
had several discussions and quizzed several people on the word for "rainbow."  Is there
a traditional story for the rainbow?  No one seems to know or remember one.  Why is it
called Rain's Machete?  It's called that because it literally "cuts" the rain.  It is a sign that
the rain for that day is finished.  Another word for rainbow is the "rain rests".  Why
would God use this as a sign of His alliance?  God said he would not kill the earth again
by flood, so he stops the rain, the rain will rest or be cut, and there will not be a flood. 
God gave us this sign so that we would see it, remember Him and remember that He will
not forget His promise to not destroy the earth through flood again.  This is the term
used in the Supyire Genesis draft, Gen.09:13.
\ln 04.43
\bt Whenever I see this rainbow, I will remember that alliance that I took
with you and your offspring
\anc gen.09:13 - 15
\tst Tst4:  Why is the rainbow there?  God put it there.  It tells us that the rain may fall, but
the earth will not be destroyed from it.
\tst Tst5:  Why does a rainbow come?  God bring it.  He told Noah he would lower it.  The
promise He made Noah - it will not be forgotten.
\tst While in Tst4 retelling the lines about the rainbow were included, and actually expanded
upon to say "now, when we see the rainbow, we know the rain has come, but it will not
destroy the earth"; in Tst5 the rainbow was omitted all-together in the final retelling.  In
the retelling that was not recorded, he did state these lines.  
\ln 04.44

\dt 31/Dec/2008

\c 06
\t Abraham Story
\co Supyire
\p
\co Redemptive Theme:   The story begins to show how a good relationship with God
can be obtained through belief in Him.  The story shows God's desire for relationship
with man, even after sin has entered the world.
\co Basic Biblical concepts :  God fulfills His promises (seen in intro of next story).  God's
power to provide.    
\co Cohesion / Background:  The story sets the stage for future reference to the
"Israelites" as "the people of the offspring of Abraham".  The story continues to
build the concept of relationship with God as He personaly guides and provides for
people.  It continues to call people to trust and obey Him.
\co Worldview / Selection Issues :  The story shows the benefits of good relationship
with God - His blessings and provisions.  Having descendants is a big desire within
the Supyire culture, therefore emphasis has been placed on God's promise and
power to provide the solution.
\p
\co Story Craftor:  SS
\co BackTranslator:  BK
\p
\co Resources used in Crafting: Audio of French Bible- Parol de Vie, Bambara Bible, and
Supyire Draft of Genesis
\p
\co Audio Revised: Oct 21, 08
\co BT Revised:  Oct 21, 08
\p
\tst Testing Results tst2:  Lady friend at Boutique:  This story has quite a bit more dialogue
than normal, that added some levels of difficulty.  But the story was retold well, one of
our testers retold story skipping the intro.  The intro was talked about within the
questions we asked was understood and explained.  The testing respondent retold the
Brehima story, without the intro other than saying that this is true... it was interesting
she retold the story without most of the dialogue but included what the dialogue meant. 
The fact that God did not forget the relationship he had with Adama & Awa and that God
chose a man to take care of this crowd on his behalf, in his name (which is literal
translation).  The parts about Brehima being told to leave, leaving, the blessings God
give him, and all that he takes with him.  One area that was skipped in the retelling was
Brehima's age, but they brought it up in disscussion on their own.  
\p
\tst Testing Results tst3: Day guard friend, this retelling was not as exact as the previous
retellings of this story, he skipped many of the details that are the meat of the promise
of this story.  Notes from his retelling are below.  While in this story and previous stories,
this testing group's retelling has been captured and has been the primary source for
questioning the story's retellability ...

\cn MM:  It seems that our back-translator did not know the English term for relationship,

friendship but close to but not a promsie, this is a action to you or for you that you do
want, where there would be blessings and an alliance between people.

(cut)."  She did change the Supyire wording of the relationship breaking. The wording

actually matches what the SIL translation team suggested we use for the relationship
between God and man breaking (the Supyire word used here literally translates "cut").

\ln 06.12

\anc gen.12:07
\cn KH:  Scripture says that Abraham offered a sacrifice, but here (in Supyire culture), most
all sacrifices here are offered to fetishes here to gain power over something or to curse/
harm someone.  So in order to avoid possible misinterpretations of what Abraham is
doing or sacrificing to, it is generically stated that Abraham was worshiping God.
\tst Why did Brehima praise God?  Because he is going to have descendants, because he did
what God said & left his home and his family to do what God said.

good about him and to him.  your pray to God

away from story flow.  Deleted.

\c 08
\t King David
\co Supyire
\p
\co Redemptive Theme:  The David-stories show an indepth study of a man who has a
personal relationship with God and the power and provision of God acting on his
behalf.
\co Basic Biblical concepts :  God fulfills His promises.  God has the power to choose
kings and leaders.   
\co Cohesion / Background:  Story sets the stage for the King who is coming from within
David's descendants.  
\co Worldview / Selection Issues :  As the concept of "power" is something that the
Supyire people seek, these stories were selected in part to show the direct
interaction between man and God and the power of God given to a man who is in a
good relationship with Him.  No intermediaries are needed.  In this story, the stage
is set as David is chosen and God gives him power.
\p
\co Story crafter's name or initials:  SS
\co Backtranslator's name or initials: BK
\co Resources used in crafting:  audio of Bambara scripture text, audio of French "Parole
de Vie" text
\p
\co MM:  Latest Audio Revision 10/21/08
\co MM:  Latest BT File Revision 10/21/08
\p
\tst General Testing Comments: They were able to retell the story as it has much action.  
\p
\tst General Testing 2 (Group of women + language helper in village):  Retold the story very
well.  The introductory transition was summarized very briefly in the retelling to state
that Breihma's offspring got big, and these words tell about how David became king. 
This could potentially be based on the fact that this group of women had not recently
heard the previous stories prior to this one.  See Tst4 for thoughts on this.
\p
\tst General Testing Comments:  Tst3:  Woman friend at boutique.  Unfortunately, she is one
who had not heard the previous stories.  Again, she skipped over the entire transition
into the story and started with "There was a man there.  He was God's messenger,
Samuel..."  This raises the question if a transition is really necessary, re-tellable, or if
this transition should be shortened.  See comments below.
\p
\tst General Testing Comments:  Tst4: Day Guard Friend.  This testor had recently heard the
first 4 stories prior to this one.  He was able to tell the introduction, but does offer a
summary of lines 2 and 3.  Based on this and the other retellings, the introduction can be
trimmed down and shortened, but remain in the story as it is a transition from previous
stories and is able to be retold.
\p

\ln 08.02
\bt God kept the {promise} with Abraham.  
\old The promise that God took with Abraham, God did that promise.  
\anc Gen.15:05 , Gen.15:18 - 21 , Gen.17:06 - 08 , Heb.11:08 -10 , Joshua, Judges 1
(conquest of land promised), Old Testament , TN , mat.01:1-17 (fulfillment of promise of
generations to come and future kings)
\cn BK:  The word here used for "did" means that God did not betray him, but instead did
what He promised.  "To keep a promise".
\tst In describing what the word "foong" means, "did", it was explained that it is like an oath. 
Example:  If I say that he is a Christian and he will not become a Muslim, then I will do it
- I will not become Muslim.  That is his promise kept.
\tst Tst2:  How did God keep his promise with Abraham?  Gave him a big offspring.  Many
descendants.
\tst Tst4:  This part was retold with the same words for "promise" as in the original.  How did
God keep His promise with Abraham?  Ab is going to take God's road.  God would give
Ab many descendants.  Ab did many good things for God.  God kept His promise to give
him many descendants.  Many people - they are many. His children had children - they
were many.

to have.

beautiful.  His skin is good.

\anc 1Sa.16:06
\cn BK: The Supyire term here "na carra eye may" translates to "for sure", but literally
means "without discussion", as in "there is no doubt".
\tst Why does Samuel think this one is the king?  He is tall, good looking, and has good skin.

\anc 1Sa.16:03 , TN suggests, "I will show/point out to you the one I have chosen/appointed
to be king. Then pour oil on his head to demonstrate that he is the one I have chosen.‚Äù
\tst Why does Samuel pour oil on David's head?  To show he's God's king.  Is there anything
like this here in Mali?  No, but people will understand this part of the story.
\tst What do people do when you get a new chief here?  Have a fete (party) - people come
and see the new chief, greet him, bless him.  Drink. Eat a lot.  African dance.  Sacrifice
to fetishes.
\tst Tst2:  Why did they pour oil on David?  God trusts David.  He will be king.  His heart is
good.  
\tst Tst2:  How do they do that in Mali?  They don't pour oil on people.  But they affirm them
with words like "You are capable."  "You can do this."  They acted out bowing in respect,
shaking hands in a respectful manner, and saying words of affirmation to the
up-and-coming "king" or chief.
\tst Tst2:  The only detail omitted in the retelling was the fact that pouring of oil on him was
done to show that he would be king one day.
\tst Tst3:  Again, the explicit unpacking of why they are pouring oil on his head has been
omitted in retelling.  This line simply told in the retlling as "He is going to be king one
day."
\tst Tst4:  This sentence was again omitted in retelling.  Therefore, it seems the unpacking of
the "pouring of oil on his head" is unnecessary information and distracts from the natural
story flow.  It will be deleted.  THIS LINE HAS BEEN DELETED.
\tst Tst4:  How do they show someone will be a leader/king in Mali?  They take lots of
pictures.  When it is good for everybody - here they clap their hands, shout, dance, sing
- only when it's good for them.

\tst Tst4:  How did God's Spirit come down on him?  It camed and entered his heart.  His
heart is good.  He will be a good king.  What can God's Spirit do?  You accept God and

\tst Tst4:  In the retelling, He stated that God's Will (Part of God) descended into David's

\ln 14/May/2008
\dt 31/Dec/2008

\c 10
\t David & Goliath
\co Supyire
\p
\co Redemptive Theme:  This David series story continues to show an indepth study of
a man who has a personal relationship with God.  This story show's God's power
over enemies.  The story builds on the redemptive theme that those in good
relationship with God, those who trust in God's power for deliverance, are given
power from God and saved from their enemies.
\co Basic Biblical concepts :  God is all-powerful.  
\co Cohesion / Background:  Continuing to build the recognition of "David"'s name for
the coming of the future King from his line of descendants
\co Worldview / Selection Issues :  Contniues to build on the direct "access" to God's
power, by belief in Him, through no other intermediaries.
\p
\co Story Craftor:  SS
\co Story BackTranslator:  BK
\p
\co Resourses used in crafting: Audio versions of French Bible- Parole de Vie and
Bambara Bible
\p
\co Audio last edited on: Oct 14, 08
\co BT file last edited:  Oct 21, 08
\p
\tst Testing Results:  Original Testing Session 1 and 2:  This is story was recieved very
positively by BK and those who heard this in its inital round of testing.   In tst2, of a
group of several women in the village, the retelling went well.  One area that there
continually seems to be a bit of difficulty in the retell is the name of the "Philistines
people".  This is of course a foreign word, when the name was needed throughout the
story a couple of times they did say the "Philisti-people" and at other times they called
them "Goliath's people" .  We will look at future testing.
\p
\tst Testing Results:  Tst3:  Woman friend at Boutique, tested retellability.
\p
\tst Testing Results:  Tst4:  Day Guard friend, probed for world view.
\p

\c 12
\t David defeats his enemies
\co Supyire
\p
\co Redemptive Theme:   This David series story continues to show an indepth study of
a man who has a personal relationship with God.  This story again show's God's
saving power over enemies for those who trust in Him.  The story builds on the
redemptive theme that those in good relationship with God are ones who believe in
Him, that He will fulfill His promises.
\co Basic Biblical concepts :  God fulfills promises - David becomes king.  God hears the
prayers of His people.  
\co Cohesion / Background:  The story introduces the concept of the coming King from
within David's descendants.  Continues to build the concept of what relationship
with God can be like - Man can communicate with God through prayer.
\co Worldview / Selection Issues :  This story shows God's power over enemies,
enemies who are not on God's road, but worshipping the fetishes.  The story again
shows God's promises to bless through the giving of a big offspring.
\p
\co Story Craftor:  SS
\co Backtranslator:  BK
\co Resourses used in Crafting: Audio of French Bible- Parole de Vie and Bambara Bible
\p
\tst Testing results:  In both Bt and testing this story went well, had good reproducibility, and
was well understood.  They really get into the battles.  The group of women & our
language helper did a very good job with the retelling throughout the entire battle sceens
until they reached the part in the story where the prophet comes to talk to David.
\p
\tst Tst2:  Day Guard.  
\tst Tst3:  Woman friend at Boutique:  Tested for retellability
\tst Tst4:  Second Woman friend at Boutique:  Again, tested for retellability.  Retold in great
detail with the exception of an omission within line 4, misplacement chronologically of
line 6.
\co
\co Audio Last Edited:  9-14-08
\co BT File Latest Revision:  10-14-08
\p

\c 20
\t Elijah & the prophets of Baal
\co Supyire
\p
\co Redemptive Theme:  The story points to the solution that by believing in God, there
can be a good relationship with Him.  God is more powerful than all things, nature
and fetishes.
\co Basic Biblical concepts :  God is the one and only all-powerful God.  Call for obedience
and a view of disobedience and the worship of fetishes as sin.
\co Cohesion / Background:  The people of Abraham's offspring turn away from God,
again reiterating the need for restored relationship.  The story continues to build on
the concept of prayer and the fact that God's power is accessible through prayer.
\co Worldview / Selection Issues :  As it is typical in Supyire culture, to simply add
another belief or practice on top of traditional beliefs, this story was selected in part
to show that a choice must be made.  The story calls for recognizing God as God
alone, and only worshipping Him.  The story differentiates the worship of fetishes
and the worship of the True God.
\p
\co Story crafter: SS
\co Story backtranslator: BK
\co Resources used in crafting: Audio of French Bible Parole de Vie and Bambara Bible
\p
\co BT file last edited:  Oct 21, 08
\co Audio last edited: Oct 18, 08
\p
\tst Testing Results:  Original testing in village.  Retold well, with details maintained.  Enjoyed
the story and retold it with enthusiasm.
\p
\tst Tst2:  Woman friend at Boutique.  
\p
\tst Tst3:  Day guard.  With the exception of a few details of the sacrifice regarding the hole
and water placed in the hole, the story was told well and in its entirety.  See comments
within BT for proposed changes to text.
\p
\ln 20.01 
\bt This is something true that happened.
\anc 2Ti.03:16 , Psa.119:142 (New Century Version) "...your teachings are true";
Psa.119:160 (NIV) "all your words are true"; Jhn.17:17 "your word is truth".
\ln 20.02
\bt After {King} David's time, the people of Abraham's offspring left God's
{road} and were praising {KT: praise} fetishes {KT:  fetish}.
\old After {King} David's leadership {KT: throne} ,the people of Abraham's offspring refused
God [turn their back] and were praising {KT: praise} fetishes {KT:  fetish}.
\old After King David's leadership the people of Abraham's offspring refused God [turn their
back] and were praising {KT: praise} Baal fetishes {KT:  fetish}.
\old After the period of Nu when God destroyed the world with the flood, expect Nu and his
children there on earth,
\anc 1ki.18:18
\cn MM:  During final read through, a subtheme of God's road has immerged.  We suggest
modifying this line slightly to read, "After King David‚Äôs time, the people of Abraham‚Äôs
offspring let God‚Äôs road and took the road of the fetishes.‚Äù
\cn MM:  Based on the confusion in using the term "messenger" for both God's messengers
and Baal's messengers in retellings, this has been rephrased.  Eli is God's messenger. 
Baal's prophets are referred to as the "fetish worshippers".
\cn MM:  Culturally, these fetish worshippers are the ones responsible for the actual sacrifice
and worship give the fetish.  People come to these people to request things of the fetish. 
In a way, a fetish "chief".
\tst Tst2:  How do you turn your back on someone?  It's a bad thing to do.  I say I will come
greet you, but I don't.  I turn my back to you, and don't see you.
\tst Tst2:  How would you turn your back on God?  They did (past tense) pray to God and
work for him, but now (present) they did not.  They turned away, turned their backs on
God's road.
\tst Tst3:  Why did Abraham's offspring turn their back on God?  Because they believed in
the fetish.  The fetish, they thought, was good for them.  They turned their back on God
to follow Baal.
\tst Tst3:  Why would they praise Baal fetishes?  Because they thought Baal was good for
them since they had turned their backs on God.  When something is good for you, you
say it and give it praises.

\cn KH:  Numbers seem to be a difficult area for us.  Most all of the time when numbers are

misunderstood and therefore removed from the story.

\cn MM:  Culturally, the act of simply worshipping multiple things or practicing the customs of

keeping the aspects of their old ways.  This thought of having to choose one and not
worshipping both, should draw the attention of the Supyire.

\dt 31/Dec/2008

\c 22
\t Isaiah Prophecy
\co Supyire
\p  
\co Redemptive Theme:  The story builds on the problem of sin in terms of people
leaving God's road.  The story connects that all people have done wrong.  The story
points to the solution in terms of the coming one who will restore relationship
between man and God.  The story points to God's power over sin and over death by
rising this coming one from death.
\co Basic Biblical concepts :  All have sinned.  There is one who will come, suffer, and die
for our sins.   
\co Cohesion / Background:  People "turning their backs" and "leaving God's road". 
God's desire for people to have relationship with Him, to be "on His road". 
Cohesively speaks of the coming king within Abraham's offspring who will reign
forever.  Introduces the concept that the coming one will "suffer and die" for man's
sin.  Introduces this "Savior" that the people are now waiting for.
\p
\co Story crafter: SS
\co Backtranslator: BK
\p
\co Resources Used in Crafting:  Audio French Parole le Vie Bible, Audio Bambara Bible,
Crafted Version of Story in French 
\p
\co BT file last revised 21Oct08
\co Audio last revised 18Oct08 
\p
\tst Tst:  Original testing done in village and with group of men in Nearby village, then with
Tst2 and with our women friends at the boutique.  However, story has been modified and
shortened based on lack of retellability of previous story.
\p
\tst Tst2:  Day Guard friend
\tst
\p
\ln 22.01a
\bt This is something true that happened.  
\anc 2Ti.03:16 , Psa.119:142 (New Century Version) "...your teachings are true";

\ln 22.01b
\bt After God's {messenger} Eli's time, Abraham's offspring people

\anc isa.03:08 , isa.01:02 , isa.01:04 , 2ki.10:31 , 2Ki.14:24, 2ki.13:06, 2ki.15:24 , 2ki.17:02
- 23 , TN introduction to Isaiah it suggests, "Many times the kings thought about what
they wanted more than about God‚Äôs law, however, and the people did too.... "
\tst Tst2:  Why do you think Abraham's offspring turned their backs to God again?  Because
God's road was not good for them anymore.  They did no longer want to do the things of
God - the things God wanted them to do.
\ln 22.02
\bt And God {sent} messengers to the people of Abraham's offspring to
speak to them.  {Why}?  Because God wanted them to take His
{road}.
\old So, God chose a lot of messengers who can say God's words.
\anc isa.01:01 , 1ki.22:14 , isa.06:09, jer.01:01 - 10 , Continuing in TN introduction to Isaiah,
"When this happened, God sent his prophets‚Äîpeople who spoke his message‚Äîto the
kings and the people. These prophets told God‚Äôs message in many different ways.   In
these ways they tried to help the people understand how much God wanted them to
repent and live the way that was best for them‚Äîfollowing his law. "
\cn MM:  Here it was explained to us by BK that, "to take His road" means that God wanted
the people to follow Him, follow His ways and do His will.
\tst Why would God send them messengers?  To tell them how to take his road.  
\tst Tst2:  Why does God want Abraham's offspring to take His road?  Because the Savior is
coming after and when he comes he will save them.  And so that they would not be
doing bad things against God.  He doesn't want us to do bad things against Him.
\tst Tst2:  In retelling he does not state .."Why?  Because ..."  However, this phrase has
proved to be a natural retellable phrase throughout the story set and will not be changed
here.  
\ln 22.03

\old Among these messengers Isaiah was one of them.
\anc isa.01:01 - 02 , isa.06:08 , isa.08:11

that were going to happen.  He told him how a child would be born to Abraham's

\ln 22.05

\tst Tst2:  How can God show Isaiah what will happen?  God took him, he was God's

\ln 22.11

\ln 22.12

\tst Tst2:  In retelling, he adds "and take another road."  This may be a good addition to

\ln 22.13

\anc isa.53:06 NLT - implied information.  "laid on him the sins of us all" (implied - we have

\cn The phrase here "do bad things" is the Supyire term for sin.   
\tst Tst2:  Why do we do bad things?  Because people don't listen and don't know God's
words.  The people who don't know God, they praise the fetishes because the fetishes
are strong - they can kill people, but not all of the people or all the time.  The fetishes

they don't know. But the fetishes can't hurt people who have God's Words.  We do what
God's words say, the whole world when they don't have God's Words, do bad things.
\ln 22.14
\bt But God put the load of our sins on His Worker.
\old But God put the load of our sins on the {savior}.
\anc isa.53:05 , 06  , NLT translation states, "5¬†But he was wounded and crushed for our sins.

\cn MM:  The term "load" is used in context with sin in the Supyire NT draft.  Example, in

same as the word used in the story
\tst Why will he take the load of our sins?  He knows us, will take God's good/best road for
us
\tst Tst2:  How will he take the load of our sins?  We do bad things, but he will take them
from us.  God will put them on top of him.  God said he is our Savior.  He will take our
bad things away from us - Our Savior will take our bad things and take them beside God
- So when God judges us, He does not see those bad things.
\tst Tst2:  How did God put the load of our sins on our savior?  He took our bad things on top
of him so that we could go next to God and be with Him, walking in His light.
\tst Tst2:  Why did God do that?  Because God said he would save us from our bad things
and save us by His work.  
\tst Tst2:  Why would God put the load of our sins on him?  Because God said he was giving
a Savior to save us, to take the sins from us and give us peace and life.
\tst Tst2:  This line was omitted in retelling.  Based on multiple testing questions, he seems
to understand the line.  However, this may not be a natural phrase to retell.  We can
retest this to see if this needs unpacking or deleting.

\tst Tst2:  Why is He like a sheep?  Because He will be beat and tied up and killed, but he
won't speak and he won't run.

\dt 31/Dec/2008
\dt 11/Sep/2008

\c 26
\t Birth of Jesus
\co Supyire
\p
\co Redemptive Theme:  The story points to the solution to sin through the birth of
Jesus, the one who will save.            
\co Basic Biblical concepts :  Jesus is God's Son, He was born of a virgin, through the
power of God's Spirit.  
\co Cohesion / Background:  Ties the "Savior people are waiting for" to the birth of
Jesus.  Cohesively establishes Jesus coming from David's descendants.
\co Worldview / Selection Issues :  Shows an angel of God coming and speaking to
Mariam and the shepherds - God communicates with people through His angels. 
Calls people to respond in obedience.
\p
\co Story crafter: SS
\co Story Back-Translator: BK
\p
\co Resources Used in Crafting:  Audio of French Bible "The Parole de Vie", Bambara
Bible, draft of Supyire New Testament
\p
\co BT file Last Revised: 21Oct08  
\co Audio Last Revised: 21Oct08
\p
\co
\tst Tst:  Original Testing:  Within village family.  Retold well after shortening the story.  
\tst Tst2:  Second testing group with men in Nir-village.
\tst Tst3:  Day Guard
\tst Tst4: Woman friend at Boutique, tested for retelling.  Overall, the story is retold well with
minor details omitted.  See individual line numbers where omissions have been made.
\co

they have done - so that they will be without those bad things in front of God.

Mariam.  She will have a baby boy and name him Jesus.  He will be the Savior.

\ln 26.06

\cn MM:  Here, someone who is your "ancestor" is referred to as your "grandfather".  
\tst Tst3:  How will God give him a throne and he be there forever?  Because he is God's
Son.  He is the savior and God is giving it to him.  God gave David the throne.  God can
do it.
\tst Tst5 (retest):  New phrasing of line above retold in final retest as is.  
\ln 26.07
\bt Then the girl said, "How can that happen?  Why?  Because I do not

\anc luk.01:34
\cn MM:  This is the culturally appropriate way to say she is a virgin.
\ln 26.08
\bt Then the angel said, "God's soul [MM: {spirit}] will come into you.  God
is all powerful and will give you {power}.  This power will make you
pregnant.  And the child that you'll give birth to will be a great person. 
They will call him the "Son of God". "
\old Then the angel said, "God's soul [MM: {spirit}] will come into you.  And the child that
you'll give birth to will be a great person.  They will call him the "Son of God". "
\anc luk.01:35 , luk.01:32 NLT "¬†He will be very great .
\cn MM:  With the help of the National SIL team, the concept of "God's Spirit" coming to
Mariam has been unpacked here.  
\cn MM:  The term here for "great person" is "she-bow".  Literally, "Big person".  BK states,
"It means "VIP"".  
\tst What do you think when you hear a 'VIP"?  It is someone like a king or president.  
\tst How will Mariam have a baby if she has not known a man?  God will give the baby.     
\tst tst2: Why is the child going to be called "God's Son"?  God will give Mariam the baby.
\tst Tst3:  How can God's Spirit give her a baby?  Because God's Spirit came on her and
gave her this pregnancy.  Not a man.  
\tst Tst3:  Why will he be a great person?  Because he is God's Son.  He will be important
(ATT, our president, is important).  Also, because he is born by God's Spirit and not a
man.
\tst Tst4: In retelling this particular line, she states, "God said to her, 'You will become
pregnant.  I will bless you.  The boy that you will have, you will name him Jesus.  He will
be king, forever.  He will be king forever.  He is the Son of God"  Here, this is the first
use of the "God's Spirit" within our story set.  While this is the same term used in the
Supyire NT, it seems people are not familiar with the term.  While it has been retold in
previous retellings, it was not here.  It may be best to also state "God's power will come
to you" to unpack this more.  Revised.  Retold.

\anc luk.01:38
\tst In testing they explained that the word "slave" implies that she is working for God. 
However, they also used an example, sheep are a shepherd's "slave".
\tst tst2: Why does Mariam say she is God's slave?  She does God's will.    
\tst Tst3:  How is Mariam God's slave?  Because she praised God and took (accepted) this
message - she was his slave.
\tst Tst4:  In retelling, she stated that Mariam said "May God make it happen"  This may be a
good simplification of this line; the part about her being God's slave was not retold. 
Revised.

\ln 26.11

\anc luk.02:04
\tst tst2:  Why do Mariam and Ishuff go to their father's village?  to write their names.  Why

the people.
\tst Tst3:  Why would the king want everybody to write their names?  Me, I would come here
to my father's village of Farakala.  He did this because he wanted to know everything
about the people of his country.
\tst Tst4:  This line was retold, including the name of the village "Bethlehem."  
\ln 26.12
\bt There, Mariam was on the spot to give birth.
\old There Mariam was on the spot to give birth.  Then they entered where the horses sleep.
\anc luk.02:06 
\cn MM:  "On the spot" is a literal translation.  This basically means she was going into labor.
\ln 26.13
\bt Then she gave birth to a son.  She clothed him and put him in the
[animal] watering trough.  {Why}?  Because they didn't find a place to
sleep in the visitor/stranger's room.  It was full of strangers.
\old Then she gave birth to a son.  He was her first baby.  She clothed him and put him in the
[animal] watering {trough}.  {Why}?  Because they didn't find a place to sleep in the
visitor/stranger's room.
\anc luk.02:07
\cn MM:  This "watering trough" is the closest thing to a manger the Supyire know and see. 
It is made by taking out the inside of a tree, somewhat looking like a canoe, and placing
water in it for the animals to drink.  This word is the same as used in the Supyire NT
draft.  It literally translates "animal drinking boat".
\cn MM:  There are no typical "inns" in Supyire villages.  However, they understand the
concept of having places where visitors or strangers can sleep.  They use the terms
"stranger's house" or "stranger's room" for such places for travellers to stay when they
do not have family or friends to stay with.
\tst tst2: Why did Mariam put the baby in a watering trough?  The strangers house was full. 
There were too many people in the town.  It was full.
\tst Tst3:  How do we know this was her first baby?  Because this is the first one she will
have/birth.  She had not birthed any before him - because God said he would give this
baby to her - His Spirit came on her.  This is her first.
\tst Tst3:  Why did she put him in the watering trough?  Well, she wrapped him and laid him
there while he was sleeping because there was no room for them at the stranger's
house.
\tst Tst3:  Why didn't they find a place in the stranger's room?  Because the stranger's room
was full of strangers who were there to write their names down.
\tst Tst4:  In retelling, she did not state "Why?  Because they didn't....".  This line could be
rephrased to make it explicit, "Why?  Because the stranger's room was full of strangers. 
There was no place for them."
\tst Tst4:  In retelling, she omitted "He was her first baby".  This can be deleted from the
story.  Deleted.   
\ln 26.14
\bt At that time, there were some shepherds spending the night in the
bush and taking care of the sheep.  God sent one of his angels to
them.
\old At that time, there are some shepherds spending the night in the bush and taking care of
the sheep.  And one of God's angels told them [MM: began speaking to them]
\old When she gave birth, at that time, there are some shepherds spending the night in the
bush and taking care of the sheep.  And one angel told them [began speaking to them].
\anc luk.02:08 - 09
\tst tst2:  Why did an angel go to the shepherds?  To tell them that a child - the VIP - God's
Child - has been born.  They praised God and sang.
\tst Tst3:  Why did the angels go to the shepherds?  Because the angels had words that were
true and they (shepherds) didn't know it.  The angels went to tell them of the savior that
was born.  He had good news for them.
\tst Tst3:  Why were they spending the night in the bush?  Because they were there to watch
the sheep.  They didn't want the sheep to die or be eaten.
\ln 26.15
\bt When these shepherds saw the angel, they were frightened,   
\anc luk.02:09 
\tst Tst3:  Why were they frightened?  Because they didn't know angels.  They came to
them.  But they were scared.  They may have thought they would take them.
\ln 26.15b
\bt but the angel told them "Don't be afraid. Why?  Because I come to tell
you a good news. 
\anc luk.02:10
\tst tst2:  Why should the shepherds not be afraid of the angels?  Because they came from
God. 
\tst Tst3:  Why would angels go to shepherds to tell them good news?  They went to tell
them their savior was born today - so the shepherds would know because they didn't
know that he was born.
\ln 26.15c
\bt There was a child born in Bethlehem today.  He comes to save {KT:
Savior} people.    
\old Today, a savior was born to you in Bethlehem.  He is Christ, the Lord.  He is God's
Chosen One.  He will save people.
\anc luk.02:11, TN suggests translating Christ or Messiah as "God's Chosen One", TN
suggests "Christ:  the Messiah, the "anointed one".  He was the one God chose to save
his people."  TN suggests for Luke 2:11 "Tonight in Bethlehem, one has been born to
save you.  He is the Messiah, the Lord."
\tst Who do you think the angels are speaking of when they save a savior was born?  This
"savior" is Jesus.  
\tst tst2:  Why is this child called a savior?  He will save people from their sins or bad
actions.
\tst Tst3:  How was a savior "born to them?"  He was born to them because God's angel went
to Mariam.  God's Spirit gave her the pregnancy and told her she would have a son to be
named Jesus.  He would be the savior.  He would save them.  He came to save them.
\tst Tst3:  Why is he God's Chosen One?  Because God gave him to Mariam.  God gave her
the pregnancy.  
\tst Tst3:  How will he save the people?  From the bad things they will do.  He will save them
in the future.  God will ask them of their bad things.  What is he saving the people from? 
From their bad things - when God asks them and judges them.
\tst Tst4:  In retelling this, she states, "There was a child born in Bethlehem today....He is
important.  The child's name is big.  He will be king forever."  This dialogue is now long
and with many difficult key terms.  It should be reduced and could simply state "There
was a child born in Bethlehem today.  God has sent him to save people." The use of
Christ and Lord will not be used cohesively throughout the story set and should be
deleted here.  Revised.
\ln 26.15d

\ln 26.16
\old At that moment, a crowd of angels came to join the first one.  Then they started praising
{KT: praise} God and singing.  
\anc luk.02:13 , TN also suggests, "praising God: The angels were already giving praise to
God for Jesusí birth when they appeared. This could be a song or a shout."
\cn MM:  Culturally, singing is often a way to give praise.  When the angels were praising
God by "saying" 'Glory to God ...', that would be something that culturally could be sung
as a praise or prayer.
\tst How can you "praise" God?"  It means to "give thanks to God", or to say that "God is
good."  
\tst Tst3:  Why did the angels join together to praise God?  Because God is their boss and
that is what you do.  You praise the one over you/your boss.
\tst Tst4:  This line was not retold.  It can be deleted from an already long story.  Deleted.
\ln 26.17

\tst Tst3:  Why did the angels go to look for what the angels said?  To see that their words

\tst Tst4:  This line was retold as, "The shepherds let their sheep and went to Bethlehem to

can be maintained, "Let's go to Bethlehem to see this child."  Revised.
\ln 26.17b

\ln 26.18
\bt When they arrived there,  they saw Mariam, Joseph and the baby.

\ln 26.18b

\tst Tst3:  Why were they astonished?  Because of what the shepherds were saying.  They

\ln 26.19
