\ln 26.20
\cn MM:  Lines were deleted  -- possible misunderstanding of how these "important" people
knew a king was born.
\old Some important people came from another {country} to see the baby.  Why?  Because
they knew that a king was born and they wanted to praise him.
\old Important strangers came from another country.  Why?  Because they knew a king was
born.
\old The wisemen came from another village to ask the king about the baby.  "We are
looking for the baby that was born, to respect him."
\anc mat.02:01 - 02
\cn MM:  This line was changed due to cultural baggage of the word used for "wise men".  
\tst tst2:  Why did these people come to see the baby?  They wanted to praise and respect
him.  They knew He is God's Child, God's Son.
\tst Tst3:  How did they know the baby was the king?  Because they heard the words of the
others praising him and God and they knew he was the king and savior.
\ln 26.21
\old After that, on the way the stars guided them to the place where the baby was born.
\anc mat.02:09 - 10
\cn MM:  Again, this line was deleted due to cultural baggage and assumptions in testing
made about people who "follow a star".
\ln 26.22
\old As soon as they arrived there, they saw the baby and kneeled down and greeted {KT
praise} him and gave him gifts with joy.
\anc mat.02:11
\cn BK:  The phrase here used for "greeted him" is a term used for a greeting with respect. 
They did not simply greet him, but were "respecting" and "praising" him.  This term
would be used when greeting a superior.
\cn MM:  This portion of the story about the wisemen has been left in the story because of
the importance of greetings and gift giving in this culture.  It shows that the person who
is being greeted is important, a good person, worthy of visiting. [Later deleted]
\tst tst2:  Why did they give him gifts?  Because they knew he was a VIP.  Because they are
happy and joyful.  
\tst tst2:  What does the story tell you about Jesus?  Jesus is truth.  He is God's child, God's
VIP, God's Son.  Jesus is "God's Chosen One."
\tst tst2:  What do you like about the story?  Jesus came.  He will be VIP and save people
from their sins.  Also liked how when Mariam was told she's having a baby, she said,
"How?" and God made it happen.
\tst Tst3:  Why would important people bow down to a baby?  Because they knew he would
save them, he was big - they understood.
\tst Tst3:  How do you give a gift with joy?  Because they gave the gift because it is good to
give things.  It does give joy because it was good for them to give it.

\c 28
\t John the Baptist and the Baptism of Jesus
\co Senufo Supyire
\p
\co Redemptive Theme:  This story points to the solution that the Savior who is coming
has the power over evil, power to save the good.  The story therefore points to the
need to have good relationship with God and be saved from the coming judgment.
\co Basic Biblical concepts :  The story introduces concepts such as baptism,
repentence, judgment, forgiveness.  Jesus is God's Son.
\co Cohesion / Background:  The story introduces the concept that some leaders of
God's praying house are not truly following God's road.  The story introduces the
concept of "repentence" in terms of "leaving your old road" and "taking God's road"
and calls people to be baptized in order to show this repentence.
\p
\co Story Crafter:  SS
\co Story Backtranslator:  BK

\dt 01/Jan/2009

\c 30
\t Woman at the Well
\co Supyire
\p
\co Redemptive Theme:  This story begins to cohesively express the concept of
redemption through the theme of relationship - as the people here "trust" Jesus. 
This same word for "trust" is seen in previous stories, as in Abraham, to bring a
good relationship with God.  The solution to sin, Jesus, is made clear as He himself
states He is the Savior they are waiting for.
\co Basic Biblical concepts :  Through Jesus, one can have eternal life.  Jesus has God's
all-knowing power.     
\co Cohesion / Background:    The story introduces the selection of Jesus' disciples and
begins His ministry time.  The story shows Jesus' desire for relationship with people,
even a woman he's not supposed to relate with.
\co Worldview / Selection Issues :  Water is a very important aspect of life here.  The
Supyire people live in a dry place, where water is sometimes not available.  This
story was selected to emphasis God's provision in terms of "water" - water that
Jesus offers of eternal life.   Also, as knowledge is power here - Jesus' power will be
seen in the story.
\p
\co Story crafter's name or initials: SS
\co Backtranslator's name or initials: BK 
\p
\co Resources used in crafting:  Audio of French Parole le Vie , audio of Bambara
scripture, audio of Supyire NT draft
\p
\co BT last revised:  10/18/08
\co Audio last revised:  10/18/08
\p
\tst General comments regarding original test sessions:  (Tested twice in our original village
- once with group of men and women during onsite consultation.  Tested again with
group of younger women).  They seem to relate well to this story - the concept of water
and thirsting for water is huge here.  Also, the concept of worshipping false idols on a
mountaintop is something that happens here.  They do seem to like the fact that Jesus
knows everything about this woman, confirming the fact that knowledge here is power. 
They retold the story well as a group, only omitting a part of the dialogue between Jesus
and the woman - about the mountaintop and "you don' t know who you are
worshipping...".  We will further test to determine if the story is too long and the dialogue
needs to be shortened or not.
\p
\tst General Comments - Tst3 - Story told in "storying/discipleship group" of women/men in
village:  After listening to the story 3 times, they retold the story in amazing detail.  The
only line omitted was line 06 about the woman questioning the fact that Jesus didn't have
anything to draw the water with.  They also stopped short of saying the very last
sentence, "He is the World's Savior."  However, they themselves brought this last
sentence up in later questions.
\p
\tst Tst4:  Day Guard friend in town.  
\tst Tst5:  Woman friend at phone booth.
\p

for some water.  Why?  Because there is no relationship between our villages."
\anc Jhn.04:09
\cn MM:  The order of phrasing in this line was switched based on final recording and his
natural tendency to place the phrases in this order.  He did this on his own for both
retellings.
\cn BK:  The Supyire word used here for "no relationship" implies that there is no link
between the villages and that there are misunderstandings there.
\tst Why did the woman say Jesus should not ask her for water?  Jesus' village and the
woman's village have no dealings with each other.  Things like this happen here in Mali.
\tst Tst3:  What was the woman thinking when she asked "Why are you asking me for some
water?"  She knew that her people and Jesus' people had no relationship.  He should not
be talking to her and asking her for water.
\tst Tst3:  Do you think Jesus knew that his people and her people had no relationship? 
Hesitation.  First said no.  Then realized, "yes."  It was then discussed how they liked this
part because it shows that Jesus likes the woman because he speaks to her and offers
her water that gives life forever.
\tst Tst4:  What was the woman thinking when she asked "Why are you asking me for
water"?  Because her people and Jesus' people were not the same.
\tst Tst4:  How did she know there was no relationship between their people?  Because she
had learned about it.  
\ln 30.05
\bt So Jesus said, "If you knew the person you are talking to, you would
ask me for some water to drink.  I would give you some water, water
that will give life {forever}."
\cn The word for living water here is literally translated, "water that gives life that has no
end".
\anc Jhn.04:10
\tst Tst3:  What is Jesus' water?  It is water that gives life forever.  It is like a spring, that
never stops.  
\tst Tst3:  How do people get Jesus' water?  You follow God's road.  You believe and trust
Jesus.  
\tst Tst4:  Why should she ask Jesus for water?  Because Jesus is the Savior, but she didn't
know that.  
\tst Tst4:  How does Jesus give water that gives life forever?  Because you will be entered on
God's Road.  
\tst Tst4:  In retelling, he omits the last sentence.  "I would give you some water, water that
will give life forever. 
\tst Tst5:  In her retelling, she includes this last sentence and it does not need to be
changed.  
\ln 30.06
\bt Then the woman said, "This well is too deep.  But you have no [MM:
bag] to pull the water from the well with.  Where will you find that
water?"
\anc Jhn.04:11
\tst Tst4:  How does the woman think Jesus will get this water?  She thinks he will pull water
from the deep well and give it to her.  Where does he get his water?  From God's Words
that he will tell the woman.
\tst Tst4:  In retelling, he phrases this last question as , "How will you give me this water?". 
However, in tst5, she kept the phrasing the same, "Where will you find the water that
you are going to give me?"  This phrase does not need changing.
\ln 30.07
\bt Then Jesus answered her, "If someone drinks water from that well, he
will get thirsty again.  But the water I'm giving, if someone drinks that
water, he will not get thirsty again.
\anc Jhn.04:13 -14
\tst Tst4:  How can Jesus' water make you not thirst again?  Now, here, you drink, but then
you walk to your house and have to drink again.  But Jesus' water is God's Words. 
Words that are true.
\ln 30.08
\bt The water will be [MM: inside him] like a spring, that gives life
forever."
\anc Jhn.04:14
\tst What do you think is Jesus' water?  It is peace, food, strength, power, blessings.  Why is
it like a spring?  Jesus' water will never finish in your stomach.  It is like water that
comes up into a well.  Springs are a good thing.
\tst Tst4:  How can it be inside him?  Because Jesus said so.  God's Words are big and they
will not stop.  
\tst Tst4:  How is it like a spring?  Because it will not stop.  It is like the rivers - the water
goes and does not stop. 
\tst Tst4:  Again, he omits the phrase "that gives life forever."  However, this is included in
Tst5 retelling and does not need to be changed.

\anc Jhn.04:15

\anc Jhn.04:19

\tst Tst4:  Why did the woman think Jesus is one of God's messengers?  Because he knew

\tst Tst4:  This line was omitted from retelling.  Lines 12 - 15 should be simplified and/or

\ln 30.13
\bt "I‚Äôm going to ask you why our grandfathers were praising {KT: praise}
on that mountain, and you, the people of Abraham's offspring, are

\anc Jhn.04:20
\cn BK: "Even now in the village, there are some mountains people have their personal gods

general, those types of gods are situated on mountains.
\tst What do people here do on the mountains?  People pray to their idols on mountains. 
Many Malians worship idols on mountains.
\tst Tst4:  Why did the woman ask why Abraham's descendants praised God somewhere
else?  Because she knew that Abraham's descendants people were praying to God - the
others were on top of the mountain doing fetishes and not praying to God but to
something else.  Abraham's descendants people prayed to God.
\tst Tst4:  In retelling, he uses the word "pray" and "praying to God" instead of "Praise."

\ln 30.14
\bt And Jesus said, "A day is coming, when it will not be important that

\old And Jesus said, "A day is coming, you are not going to praise God on that mountain or
even somewhere else.
\anc Jhn.04:21
\cn BK:  This means, "that place to worship God has no importance, only your heart."
\tst Why does Jesus say this?  Because one day, you will pray to God not on the mountain. 
They will know God and follow God's road.  If they understand Jesus' words, they will not
go and pray on the mountain.  Even today, before people know Jesus, they go and pray
to idols on the mountains, because they don't know Jesus.
\tst Tst4:  Why will they not praise God on the mountain or somewhere else?  Because they
will all know God one day and not the others.
\tst Based on retellings, proposed line revision:  "A day is coming, when it will not be
important where you praise God.  God wants us to praise Him with our heart (or
insides)."  Revised.
\ln 30.15
\bt "God wants us to praise Him with our hearts. "
\old You don't know the one who you are praising, but we know the one we are praising. 
Those who are praising God with truth and soul {KT: spirit} are the one that God loves
{KT: love}."
\anc Jhn:04:22 - 23
\cn MM:  Who is someone who praises God with truth and soul?  BK: It is someone who
really agrees with the reason that he‚Äôs practicing‚Ä¶ is convinced.  Even some Muslims go
to the mosque to avoid people saying, ‚ÄúAh, he has no religion.‚Äù  He is praying in front of

\tst How do people worship with truth and soul?  These people really trust and believe God. 
By believing and trusting Jesus, he enters you and gives you the ability to worship in
truth.  Is it possible to "praise God" without truth and soul?  Yes, it's possible here. 
Example - people going to church or to mosque not because they want to, but because
their parents do.
\tst Tst4:  Why does God love them?  When your spirit comes to praise God and you say and
do these things, God loves you.  
\tst Tst4:  The meaning of this line was not captured in the retelling.  See simplification

\ln 30.16
\bt And the woman said, "We know, the Savior we are waiting for {KT:
Christ} will come.  He will tell us all the facts.
\old And the woman said, "We know, the {Savior} will come.  He will tell us all the facts.
\old And the woman said, "Really, we know that God's {Chosen} will come.  When he comes,
he will tell us all the facts"
\anc Jhn.04:25 , Supyire NT draft uses, "God's Chosen One" here.  "We know that the
Messiah will come (They call him "God's Chosen One.")
\anc GeCL has "the promised Saviour," both here and in most other places. (In Matt 2.4 it has
"the promised King," but see Matt 2.2 for the reason for the shift.) Either "the promised
King," "the promised Saviour," or even "the promised Saviour King" expresses
accurately the meaning that the original readers would have received.
\tst What do you think when you hear "God's Chosen One"?  Jesus.  God's Commissioned
One.  God choosing and sending a "Good One" - Jesus is God's correct person.
\tst Tst4:  How did she know God's Chosen One will tell the facts?  Because she knew he
would come and tell the facts.  Like now, Jesus has come and told her all about her. 
Jesus is there telling the facts.
\tst Tst4:  In the retelling, he again did not say "God's Chosen One", but on his own , said
"Savior."  This is a key term that will be used throughout for "Christ, Messiah, God's
Chosen One.".  Also in the retelling, he states, "When he comes, we will pray to God." 
He keeps the cohesive nature of what is happening in lines 14-15 - praying to God. 
However, these lines will be reworked.  Revised.
\ln 30.17

\anc Jhn.04:26

\ln 30.19

the village a few days to teach them.  So He stayed there several days.  Then they said

asked Jesus to stay in the village a few days.  So, Jesus stayed there a few days and

\ln 30.20
\bt Then many people trusted {KT trust} Jesus because of his words.  And
the people said, "Truly, this is the world's {Savior}."
\old Then they said to the woman, "We didn't trust him because of your words, but we hear
from his own mouth."  And said that, "We know he is the world's {Savior}."
\anc Jhn.04:42
\tst Why do many people trust Jesus?  They don't just trust her words, but they trust Jesus
because they have been with him and heard His words.
\tst How and when do you trust people here in Mali?  Here, there are many people that are
not correct, that you cannot trust.  But, if I commission someone (assign them with
something to do for me), then I must know them really well and believe them.
\tst Why do they say Jesus is the world's savior?  Because Jesus' road is life's good road. 
The road you should take.  A savior is someone who saves, literally "buys" the world. 
Jesus saves the world by forgiving the world - you believe in Jesus and he forgives.
\tst Tst4:  How do they know he is the world's savior?  Because the woman believed in
Jesus, but they wanted to know too.  When Jesus stayed with them and taught them,
they knew from God's Words that he was the one God sent to save the world.
\tst Tst4:  In retelling, it was stated as, "They did not trust him because of the words the
woman has said.  Because the words he said to them, they trust him. They trusted him
and said, ‚Äúhe is the world‚Äôs savior.‚Äù"
\tst Tst5:  In retelling, she point blank said, "They did not trust the words of the woman. So
they and Jesus spoke together.... Then they said, "Yes.  You are this one."  They trusted
in Jesus now.  Because of Jesus' words, they knew the woman was speaking truth.  .... 
"  Based on these retellings, this line could be simplified.  There is no need to draw out
an implied distrust between the woman and the village people.  This line can be
simplified to, "Many trusted him because of his words (end of proposed line 19 above)
and said, "He is the world's Savior."  Revised.
\p
\tst What part of the story do you like?  Jesus' water is good water - like a spring, with no
end, that gives life forever.  Also, how Jesus knew everything about the woman.  Also,
that the people wanted to see Jesus and after they saw him and heard him speak, they
trusted him.

\ln Further Thoughts from Tst3, Storying Group:
\tst What did you like about the story?  I liked that Jesus gives water that gives life forever. 
That you don't have to be thirsty anymore.  I like that Jesus was travelling around to
other villages and came to this one.  I like when the people believe Jesus because of His
own words.  I like when Jesus says "I am God's Chosen One."  I like that there is a day
coming when people won't worship on mountaintops,.
\tst What part did you not like?  I didn't like how the woman did not have this water that
Jesus was offering.  I didn't like how the woman's water would leave her still thirsty.  I
didn't like that the woman didn't offer Jesus water - you offer strangers water, you give
them something to drink.
\tst What does the story tell you about God?  The He is good.  That you should take His road
and do His work.    
\dt 01/Jan/2009

\c 32
\t Parable of Wheat and Weeds
\co Supyire
\p
\co Redemptive Theme:  Evil is present in this world, but Jesus is victorious over evil. 
The theme of relationship is expressed within this story as being on Jesus' road.
\co Basic Biblical concepts : Day of judgment is coming in which consequence of sin
results in eternal suffering.  Those who follow Jesus will stay forever in God's
Kingdom.
\co Cohesion / Background:  This story connects those who are on "Jesus' road" to
those who will enter God's Kingdom.  Continues to build on Jesus' ministry time
period and what Jesus did while on earth.
\p
\co Story Crafter: SS
\co Story BackTranslator:  BK
\co
\p Resources used in crafting session: Audio of French Bible, "Parole de Vie",
Bambara Bible, Draft of Senufo Supyire New Testament
\p
\co BT file Last Revised: 14Oct08
\co Audio Last Revised:  22Sep08
\p
\tst General Comment:  Original testings include multiple testings within our village, as well
as testing with the men in Near village.  In testing, the actual parable itself is retold very
easily.  The introduction is retold with ease as well.  However, the explanation of the
parable, while it is understood, is more list-like and a more difficult to re-tell.
\tst Tst2:  Storying group in village, village family women
\tst Tst3: Day Guard
\p
\ln 32.01
\bt This is something true that happened.
\anc 2Ti.03:16 , Psa.119:142 (New Century Version) "...your teachings are true";
Psa.119:160 (NIV) "all your words are true"; Jhn.17:17 "your word is truth".
\ln 32.02
\old When Jesus was 30 years old, he started delivering God's speech.
\anc luk.03:23
\cn MM:  This line was deleted because it was added chronologically to the "Woman at the
Well" story which was added to the story set.
\ln 32.03a
\bt Jesus was teaching people God's speech, healing people, and chasing
away evil spirits [MM: { demons}]  from people.
\anc luk.04:15 , luk.04:16 , luk.04:40 - 42
\tst Tst3:  How was Jesus healing people and chasing away evil spirits?  Because he would
pray to God, as He is God's Son.  He is the Savior - He would pray they would be healthy
and they would be.  He would pray the evil spirits would leave - and they did.
\ln 32.03b
\bt He was followed by many people.
\anc luk.04:42
\tst Tst3:  Why did people follow him?  Because they wanted to be healthy and they wanted
to hear God's Word from him. 
\ln 32.04a
\bt {Why}?  Because they wanted to hear God's words from him.
\old They wanted him to heal them.  
\anc luk.04:40-42
\ln 32.04b
\bt They also wanted him to heal them.  
\old They also wanted to hear God's words from him.  
\anc luk.05:01
\cn MM:  In final recording, he switches the order of lines 04a and 04b.  
\tst Tst3:  Why would they want to hear God's Words?  Because they want to follow God's
road and God's Words tell them how.
\ln 32.05a
\bt Always, Jesus was telling parables to people.
\old Jesus was always telling people through parables.  He was always telling parables to
people. 
\anc mat.13:34 - 35
\cn In testing, the word for "parable" was compared it to that of a proverb, which can be
true.  It is the saying or speak of the "old men".  True words, but sometimes difficult to
understand the meaning.
\tst Tst2:  This line was omitted in retelling, but retold in Tst3.  This line can be simplified to
state, "Jesus was always telling parables to people."  Revised.
\ln 32.05b
\bt One day, Jesus told them this parable about God's Kingdom {KT:
throne}.  He said ....
\old Then Jesus told them a prophecy [MM: example].  He said that, "God's {throne} [MM:
kingdom] looks like this thing..."
\anc mat.13:24
\tst Why did Jesus say these words, "God's Throne looks like this thing..."  To tell people to
take God's road and to make them understand how to take God's road.
\tst In a second testing session, the word for "prophecy" was explained as a commonly used
word and means "example".  It was explained that while Jesus was always telling people
parables, the following was an example of one.... and then Jesus starts the parable
about the farmer.
\tst Tst3:  Why would Jesus tell them a prophecy/example?  Because they came to him to
hear from him, so he told them parables.
\tst Tst2:  This line was not retold.
\tst Tst3:  In retelling, this line was not retold.  Could be simplified to, "One day, Jesus told
them this parable about God's Kingdom.  Revised.
\ln 32.06
\bt There is a farmer who went to his farm and sowed a good grain.  
\old A farmer went to his farm to sow a good grain. After sowing the grain, he returned
home.  
\anc mat.13:24
\tst Tst3:  In this line, he introduces the character of the farmer by stating, "There was a
farmer there" before proceeding with the line.  This would be a good way to introduce
the farmer in the story.  The line, "After sowing the grain, he returned home" was not
included in his retelling or in Tst2 retelling, as it would be natural for all farmers to return
home by nightfall, this information can be deleted from story as it is inferred culturally.
\ln 32.07a
\bt By night, one of his enemies {KT: enemy} went to sow the weeds in
the farm. 
\anc mat.13:25 
\tst Tst3:  Why would the farmers enemies sow weeds there?  Because for an enemy, it is
good for the enemy to do this bad thing.  The enemy was bad and planted weeds in the
farmers good grains.
\ln 32.07b
\bt The weeds as well as the grain, germinated and were growing up
together.
\anc mat.13:26
\ln 32.08
\bt One day the workers went to visit the farm.  They found that these
weeds were growing up between the growth.  They returned home
and said to the owner, "Didn't you sow a good grain in the farm?"
\old One day the workers of the owner of the farm, went to visit the farm.  They found that
these weeds were growing up between the growth.  They returned home and said to the
owner, "Chief, didn't you sow a good grain in the farm?"
\anc mat.13:27
\cn MM:  The word here used for "visit" also implies "to check" or "to guard".  Even on a day
in which people are not "working" the fields, they send someone out to the fields to look
and check them and ward off any animals that may be disturbing them.  The word here
used for "growth" is the same as nurture or seed.  It is understood in testing to be the
good seed that was planted and is now growing up.
\tst Tst3:  Why would the workers ask if the chief had sown good grain?  Because the farmer
said he had planted good grains, but they went to the field and found the bad growing up
with the good grain.
\tst Tst3:  This was simplified to, "One day, the workers went to the farm and found the bad
weeds with the good.  ...."   In tst2 retelling also, the "workers of the owner of the farm"
was simplified to "the workers".  This phrase can be simplified.  In tst2, they do include
the fact that they went to "visit" (check on) the field.  This phrase will remain.  Both
testing groups stated the question to the chief in the line well.  Revised.
\ln 32.09
\bt "Where did these herbs/weeds come from?"
\anc mat.13:27
\cn MM:  The word for "weeds" is a generic term for grass.  It is all encompasing - anything
bad that grows up from the ground that farmers would not like.
\tst Tst3:  This was omitted in retelling.  It was also omitted from Tst2 retelling.  While this
line seems to connect the dialogue flow between lines 8 and 10, it does not seem
necessary and does not seem to distract from the natural flow of conversastion based on
retellings.  It can be deleted.  However, after discussing with crafter, he chose to leave
this in and retold it in final crafting.
\ln 32.10
\bt Then he said, "It's the job of an enemy."  Then the workers said, "Do
we pull the weeds?"
\old Then he answered them, "It's the job of an enemy."  Then the workers said, "Chief, do
you want us to pull out these weeds out of the farm?"
\anc mat.13:28
\tst How did the farmer know it was by the enemy?  Because the enemy doesn't do good
work.  He knew he had planted good grain in the field.  The bad got there because the
enemy is bad.
\tst Tst3:  In both tst3 and tst2 retellings, the workers respond more simply by saying, "Do
we pull the weeds?".  Neither of the retellings re-state "Chief" here.  This line can be
simplified as in the retellings "Do we pull the weeds?"  Revised.
\ln 32.11a
\bt The owner said, "[MM: No, Leave them.]  By pulling out the weeds you
are going to pull some growth also.
\old He said, "[MM: No, Leave them.]  Let them grow together.  Why?  Because by pulling out
the weeds you are going to pull some growth also.
\anc mat.13:29
\tst Tst3:  Why would he let them grow together?   Because he doesn't want to kill the good
grains - they will grow together and when the crops are old, the harvestors will tie up the
bad and burn them.
\tst Tst3:  In both tst2 and tst3 retellings, they omitted the second phrase, "Let them grow
together."  This can be deleted and remain as, "No.  Leave them.  ...."  Revised.
\ln 32.11b
\bt When harvesting I am going to ask the harvester to cut the weeds, tie
them, and put [MM: burn them]  in the fire.  After that, they will cut the
harvest and put into my grainery."
\old Leave them, when harvesting I am going to ask the harvester to cut the weeds, tie
them, and put [MM: burn them]  in the fire.  After that, they will cut the harvest and put
into my grainery."
\anc mat.13:30
\cn MM:  While the concept of letting the weeds grow up with the wheat, is one that makes
sense to us, as I struggle to tell the difference between wheat and weeds.  However, this
concept is slightly more foreign to the Supyire as they are farmers. Working the field
and pulling the weeds is child's work.  They pull weeds as they come up.  However, in
testing, it was understood that this final harvest represented the end of the world when
the "good" people will be separated from the "bad people".
\tst Why did he tell them to wait to pull up the weeds?  Because they would pull up some
good ones with the bad.  Wait until harvest comes .... (retold ending of farmer parable).
\tst Tst3:  Why would they burn the them?  Because they are not good.  
\tst Tst3:  In both tst2 and tst3, the repetition of the phrase, "Leave them" was not included
and can be deleted.  Revised.
\ln 32.12
\bt When Jesus said that, he went into the house.  So his students {KT:
disciple} followed him inside and asked him about the parable about
God's kingdom.
\old When Jesus said that, he went into the house.  So his students followed him inside and
asked him about the parable that he told about the weeds and the growth.
\anc mat.13:36
\tst Tst3:  Why would his students ask him about this?  Because they wanted to know all that
Jesus was saying in this parable.  They wanted to understand..
\tst Tst3:  In retelling, he stated, "When Jesus was finished with his words, he entered the
house.  His students then asked him about hsi words."   The last part of this phrase can
be deleted, "about the weeds and the growth".  The testing respondent does retell the
word "parable" in previous lines above and the first part of this line will remain the
same.  Revised to match introduction "about God's kingdom."
\ln 32.13
\bt Then Jesus said to them, "I am the planter of the good grain." 
\old Then Jesus said to them, "The chief of the growth is me [MM: the planter of the good
grain], Jesus.  "
\anc mat.13:37
\tst "Why is Jesus the planter of the good grain?"  Because He is God's Son.  It is He who
judges and chooses good from bad.  He takes the good to be with God and puts the bad
to burn in a fire.
\tst Tst3:  How is Jesus the planter of good grain?  Because he was over the growth - He was
in charge, like a boss.  He is over his disciples and students.
\ln 32.14
\old The farm is the {world}.  The good grain are the persons who are in God's Kingdom. 
The bad weeds are those who are following Satan.
\old "The farm is the world.  The growth is God's kingdom.  The weeds are the persons who
are turning people away from God and doing unrightful actions."
\anc mat.13:38
\cn MM**  LINE REMAINS CUT FOR RETELLABILITY PURPOSES
\tst What is the good grain and would do you think good grain would do?  They are those
who follow God's road, listen to His Words, listen to Jesus' Words and do them.  They are
family with God.
\tst Tst3:  How are the weeds those who follow Satan?  Because they were the bad ones. 
Weeds are bad.  Those who follow Satan are bad.
\ln 32.15
\bt The end of the {world} is harvesting.  
\old "The enemy is Satan.  The harvesting is the end of the world.  The harvesters are God's
{angels}."
\anc mat.13.39
\tst "Why is Satan the enemy?"  Because he stops people from going on God's road.  He
does bad things, is the chief of evil spirits.
\tst Why is the harvest the "end of the world"?  There was much intriguing conversation as
one man said, "The world's going to end?"  Then the others discussed this with him....
yes, it's going to end.  It's like harvest because it's when the good people will be
separated from the bad.  The bad will burn.
\tst Tst3:  While other testing respondents have had problems with the list like structure of
lines 13-15, this testor had no problems and retold this part well (outside of putting the
'harvestors are God's angels" before the "harvesting is the end of the world" phrase.
While this testing respondent retold this part well, tst2 had difficults in retelling and had
to pause many times with this list.  One proposed change here:  Delete line 14, delete
"the enemy is Satan and "the harvestors are God's angels".   This would read, "I, Jesus,
am like the planter of good grain.  The end of the world will be like this harvesting.  At
the end of the world..." continue with line 16b.  In general, the end of the story has been
told much better than this list like description in these lines.   Revised.
\ln 32.16a
\bt At the end of the world ...
\old "That the same, at the end of the world ...
\anc mat.13:40
\tst See proposed revision in line 15.  Revised.
\ln 32.16b
\bt I will send {KT: sent} out my {angels}.  They will sort out those who
are mine.
\old I am going to send my angels to sort out the good people from the bad ones ...
\anc mat.13:41 , TN states in reference to the good ones, "those whom God considers to be
good"  and of the bad, "These evil people are not truly those whom God rules".
\cn MM:  In revising this line, our craftor stated it in this manner.  He said it would be
unnatural for you to say the angel came and "sorted out" the bad ones.  The bad ones
are too numerous to "sort out".  It would be like "sorting out" rice from among pebbles. 
He also stated that if it were Jesus talking, Jesus would say "those who are mine" and
"my road" verses saying "God's road" because He and God are one.  This also makes an
important connection to the Assurance story to come and begins to plant seeds that
God's road and Jesus' road is one and the same.  Those on Jesus' road will enter God's
kingdom.
\tst Tst3:  Why is Jesus going to send his angels?  Because he is going to choose the ones
who are not going to be burned.  The angels will choose the ones he has chosen who are
going to be in God's kingdom.
\ln 32.16c
\bt Those that are not on my {road} will be thrown into a fire that cannot
be extinguished.  
\old and throw the bad ones into a fire that cannot be extinguished.
\anc mat.13:42
\tst Tst3:  How can there be a fire that cannot be extinguished?  Because God allows it.  It is
for the bad ones who do not do the good things.
\tst Tst3:  In retelling, he uses the word "enemies" here, instead of "bad ones".  
\tst Tst2:  In retelling, they state "those who are believers" vs. "those who do not take God's
road."  They state, "Those who are believers will enter peace.  Those who do not take
God's road, will be burned in a fire that cannot be extinguished."
\tst This raises the question of using the terms "good ones and bad ones".  It may be most
natural to use "those who are on God's road" and "those who do not take God's road". 
TN states in reference to the good ones, "those whom God considers to be good"  and of
the bad, "These evil people are not truly those whom God rules".  Line has been revised.
\ln 32.17
\bt There, they are going to cry and crunch their teeth.  Why?  Because
they will stay in suffering forever.
\old They will stay there and crunch their teeth.
\anc mat.13:42 , TN says, "Where there will be weeping and gnashing of teeth: The evil
people will cry for themselves in that terrible place and grind their teeth because of their
great pain. This may also imply anger (Newman). This implies that they will not die but
will continue to suffer."
\tst Why were they crunching their teeth?  Is this good?   "It's not good to crunch their
teeth.  People do it when they don't have anything to eat or drink."
\tst Testing Group of Men:  Said, they are crunching/grinding their teeth because they are
filled with sorrow and regret.  They miss God.  It's a Senufo proverb that is understood
to express regret/sorrow.
\tst Tst3:  How will they crunch their teeth and cry?  Because they will be in the fire crying
out "Waa waa waa".  
\ln 32.18
\bt Those that are on my road will go and stay in God's kingdom {forever}
and they will shine like the sun.
\old The good ones will stay in God's kingdom and shine like the sun."  
\anc mat.13:43
\tst As we are always being told, "Get out of the sun.  Sit in the shade.", we asked "Is this a
good thing - to be like the sun?"  "Yes.  In this case, yes.  To stay in God's kingdom, and
shine light like the sun."
\tst Testing Group of Men:  "Why will the good ones shine like the sun?"  Because they did
good things and now will be helped by God.  They are happy because they are with
God.  And - they're not in the fire and not crunching their teeth - they're full of joy
because they're with God.
\tst Tst3:  How will the good ones shine like the sun?  Because they will be in God's
kingdom.  They will be clean and praising God.
\tst Tst3:  While this is restated in retellings, it may be best to unpack "shine like the sun"
and state, "God will make them joyful and great, like the shining sun"  TN suggests, "God
will glorify them and cause them to be joyful and to be great. "  Left as is.  Unless further
testing determines it necessary to unpack.
\ln 32.19
\bt If you want to know these things, open your ears and really listen.  
\old After saying this, Jesus said, "The one who wants to know, has to open his ears, and
listen."
\anc mat.13:43
\tst Why does Jesus say this?  To have them listen to God's Words and then tomorrow, after
you listen, you can change your road.
\tst Tst3:  Why would one want to open his ears and listen?  Because if you listen and know
these things, you will hear God's words and know God.
\tst Tst3:  In retelling, he continues with the dilaogue, omitting, "After saying this, Jesus said
....".  This can be deleted.  He also uses more direct speech and says, "If YOU want to
know these things, open your ears and listen."  This seems more natural and can be
changed.  Revised.
\p
\tst What does this story tell you about Jesus?  When the world ends, Jesus gives life to
people.   He loves people.  Jesus is the one who gives judgment.  He is God's son.
\tst What does this story tell you to do?  I will take God's road with strength and leave the
bad things behind.  I will tell others.
\dt 01/Jan/2009

\c 34
\t Jesus Heals Demoniac
\co Supyire
\p
\co Redemptive Theme:  Jesus has power over evil.  Jesus has the power to save people
from evil.            
\co Basic Biblical concepts :  Even the evil spirits recognize Jesus as God's Son and
having power over them.   
\co Cohesion / Background:  The story introduces the concept of going and telling others
of the power of Jesus.  
\co Worldview/Selection:  As being "possessed" by an evil spirit is a real and present day
threat to the people here, this should be a story that speaks directly to this
animistic, spirit-driven society - telling them where true power can be found.
\p    
\co Story Crafter:  SS
\co Story Backtranslator:  BK
\p
\co Resources Used in Crafting:  Audio of French Bible, Bambara Bible, Senufo Supyire
New Testement draft
\p
\co Audio Last Revised:  21Oct08
\co BT File Last Revised:  21Oct08
\p
\tst Testing Results:  Original Testing done in our village as well as with a group of men in a
Nearby village.  This is a great story that has proved itself easy to retell.
\tst Tst3:  Day Guard
\tst Tst4:  Phone booth friend - tested retellability only.  She retold the story very well with
details included, except for those notated within the BT text.
\p
\ln 34.01
\bt This is something true that happened.
\old This is a strange thing that has happened that is also true.
\anc 2Ti.03:16 , Psa.119:142 (New Century Version) "...your teachings are true";
Psa.119:160 (NIV) "all your words are true"; Jhn.17:17 "your word is truth".
\ln 34.02
\bt Jesus and his {disciples} travelled to another village.  They arrived at
the place.  There was a man there.
\old When Jesus and his {disciples} were going to a village, they arrived at a place where
there was a man. 
\old When Jesus and his disciples were going to a village, they arrived at a place where there
was a man in the forest.  
\anc mrk.05:01 -02
\cn KH:  In crafting we tried to make the location that Jesus and his followers were going to
generic, because in one of our previous trainings we crafted this story and had a great
deal of difficulty with the concept of them going across the sea. Since large bodies of
water are not known here it is a confusing concept.
\tst Tst3:  Why was Jesus going to a village?  To say God's words to the people there.  Why? 
Because they should take God's road.
\tst Tst3:  In retelling, he retells this line more naturally by saying, "Jesus and his students
travelled to another village.  There in that place, there was a man possessed by
demons."  Tst4 also does a similar simplification.  It will be adjusted. Revised.
\ln 34.03
\bt He was possessed by {demons}.  He was sleeping in the grave yard
and wandering around the tufts.
\anc mrk.05:02 -03, 05
\tst Have you ever seen someone who is possessed by demons?  Yes, even here in our
family there are several who from time-to-time have demons enter them.
\tst Why would the man live in grave yard?  Because the demons had him and he was not
correct (He was not in his correct state of mind).
\tst Tst3:  How did they know he was possessed by demons?  Because he lived in the
cemetary.  He ran around.  He had his hands tied up, but he was too strong with the
demon in him  and cut through.
\ln 34.04
\bt Some time they tied his hands and his feet with chains, but he cut 
through all of them.
\anc mrk.05:03 -04
\tst Who tied him up?  The people from his village.  How did he cut/ break through them? 
The demons were stronger than him.
\tst What happens to people when they are possessed by demons?  They are irrated,
disturbed, they scream and cry out a lot.   Do they get violent?  sometimes.
\tst Why did people try to tie him up?  Because his head and heart were bad.  His head had
left him because of the demons.  
\tst Tst3:  Why did the people tie his hands and feet with chains?  So he would stay at home,
but he was too strong and kept breaking them, running off to live in the fields or the
cemetary.
\tst Tst3:  How did he cut through them?  The demons helped him to do it.  They were very
strong.  They would make him turn and twist his hands until he could break/cut the
chains.
\tst In retellings, the same word for "cut" is used as in the original story text.  This word is
natural and retellable.  
\ln 34.05
\old People did not succeed to control him. 
\anc mrk.05:04
\tst Tst3:  Why did the people not succeed to control him?  Because he is strong.  His power
was greater than all of them.  How?  The demons were in him - they were strong and
controlled him and made him walk the cemetary.
\tst Tst3:  This line was not retold.   
\tst Tst4:  This line was not retold and can be deleted from story.  It is clear from line 04 that
the people were not controlling him.  Deleted.
\ln 34.06
\bt At the time the man possessed by demons saw Jesus, they ran to
him, and kneeled in front of him.
\old At the time, the man haunted by demons saw Jesus, ran to him, kneeled in front of him,
and asked, 
\anc mrk.05:06
\cn BK:  Kneeling in front of someone is done to show respect.
\tst Why would the man kneel in front of Jesus?  Because he knew who Jesus was.  
\tst Tst3:  Why did the man run to Jesus?  Because he knew that God's Son had come.  How
did he know this?  Because they said the savior would come to save them, and save him
by chasing the demons out of the man.
\ln 34.07
\bt Then Jesus told the demons to leave the man.  
\old "God above's Son, what are you looking for?"
\anc mrk.05:08
\tst Tst3:  Why did he ask "what are you looking for?"  Because he knew Jesus just wouldn't
just be there walking around - but Jesus was going to the village and saw the man.
\tst Tst3:  In retelling, he simplifies "God's Above Son" to "God's Son."  This is a good
simplification.
\tst Tst4:  She does not state, "God's Above Son", but "Father God's Son."  She also
rephrases the question to "Why have you come here?"
\tst Tst3:  In retelling, both times, he added a phrase, "What are you doing here?"  This,
along with the testing questions, seems to indicate a misunderstanding of the scripture
meaning of "What do you want with me?" or "Do not torment me."  It may be best to
restate this so the order is also clear chronologically ... When Jesus was telling the
demons to leave the man, he cried out, "Leave me alone Jesus - Son of God.  Do not
torment me"    Revised.
\ln 34.08
\bt Then the man said loudly, "God's Son Jesus.  Do not harm me.  I beg
you {KT: pray} , leave me alone."
\old Then Jesus asked the demons to leave the man. 
\anc mrk.05:07
\cn MM:  Here "said loudly" is like a shout or to "cry out".  Literally translates "to speak with
force".  
\tst Tst3:  What did Jesus do when he told the demons to leave the man?  He told the
demons to leave the man with force because he wanted the demons to leave the man,
so he could be healthy and with Jesus.
\tst Tst3:  Why would Jesus tell the demons to leave the man?  Because Jesus knew they
had entered and he wants the man to be healthy, to stay at home with his family, and
for this extraordinary thing to happen.
\ln 34.09
\bt Then Jesus asked him, "What's your name?"
\anc mrk.05:09
\tst Tst3:  Why did Jesus ask him his name?  Because Jesus wanted to know the man.  When
you know the name you know more of them.  Yes, but who answered?  The demons,
because they were many in the man.  They are demons, but also like people - they are
broken, but they can walk and talk and they want to be in people.
\ln 34.10
\bt He answered, "My name is Many People.  {Why}?  Because we are
many."
\anc mrk.05:09
\tst Why does he respond, "My name is Many People"?  Because there are many demons in
him.
\tst Tst3:  Why does he say "Many People"?  Because there are so many of the demons in
the man.  So many that when Jesus tells them to go to the pigs, they kill all of the pigs.
\tst Tst3:  In this retelling he does not keep the "Because we are many" in direct quotes but
states, "Because there are many demons in him." However, in Tst4, she keeps direct
quotes here and the line will remain as is.
\ln 34.11
\bt Then the man said to Jesus, "Don't you chase us from this land."
\anc mrk.05:10
\tst Tst3:  Why did he ask Jesus not to chase them away?  Because their country was good
for them.  They wanted to stay and not go to another.  They asked to go into the pigs so
they would leave the man, but not the country.
\ln 34.12
\bt "We beg you to let us go into those pigs."
\anc mrk.05:12
\tst Why would the demons want to enter the pigs?  Because they have to go somewhere
\tst Why did they ask to go into the pigs?  Because they thought Jesus was going to kill them
- they asked to go into the pigs.  
\tst Tst3:  How did the demons enter the pigs?  Responded, 'How can I know this?'  I don't
know demons.  The same way they entered the man.  The pigs didn't know.  They could
not accept (they could not control the demons) what the demons did, so the demons
entered them.  But then the  pigs became mad and went into the water and died.
\ln 34.13
\bt And Jesus said "Yes" and accepted {KT: accept}. So the demons left
the man and entered the herd of pigs.
\old And Jesus accepted {KT: accept}.  So the demons left him and entered the herd of pigs.
\anc mrk.05:13
\tst Tst3:  Why did Jesus accept?  Because Jesus wanted them out of that man; so the man
could be healthy.  
\tst Tst3:  In retelling, he said, "Jesus said, 'Yes'.  Then the demons left him and entered the
herd of pigs."
\tst Tst4: In her retelling, she states, "Then Jesus raised the demons out of the man and put
them into the herd of pigs."
\tst Based on these retellings, the phrase "Jesus accepted" is not being retold.  It could be
rephrased as Tst3 states.  Jesus said, "yes." ("hhuh." in Supyire).  Revised.
\ln 34.14
\bt There were very many pigs.
\old The pigs that were possessed by the demons were about 2000.
\anc mrk.05:13
\cn KH:  In previous testing, this number was not understood and therefore removed.  
\ln 34.15
\bt The pigs run to the water [MM: ran and fell into the water] and died.
\anc mrk.05:13
\tst Who is the cause for the pigs dying?  The demons.  
\tst How did the pigs die?  They ran into the water and died.  How?  They entered the water. 
They could not breathe.    
\tst Tst3:  Why did the pigs run into the water and die?  Because the demons entered them,
so they went running, but when they entered the water, the water went into their noses
and killed them.
\ln 34.16
\bt Those who were taking care of the pigs, when they had seen that,
they went to the village and told people about what they had seen.
\anc mrk.05:14
\tst Why would the people go to the village to tell about what they had seen?  They were
scared
\tst Tst3:  Why did the pig watchers go to the village and tell?  Because they didn't believe
that Jesus had told the demons to leave the man.  But Jesus told them to leave the
man.  The demons entered the pigs and the pigs died.  But those in the village didn't
know this, they didn't believe that Jesus did it.  The pig watchers were astonished that
Jesus did this.
\ln 34.17
\bt So the people came out to see this strange thing {KT: extraordinary}.
\anc mrk.05:15
\tst Tst3:  Why did the people come?  Because they wanted to see this extraordinary thing,
that this thing is true, this true thing that Jesus had done.  They wanted to see the man
without demons.  They came and the man was sitting with Jesus, wearing clothes and
calm.
\tst Tst3:  Why is this thing strange?  Because Jesus had cast the demons out of the man into
the pigs.  The pigs died, but now the man is healthy.  Not anybody can do this.  Before
this man could not be controlled, but now he sits calm with Jesus.
\ln 34.19
\bt The man who was possessed by demons, they saw him sitting next to
Jesus, wearing clothes, and calm.
\old They came to see Jesus with the man who was possessed by the demon sitting near him
with clothes, and calm.   So they went and told this about.
\anc mrk.05:15 -16
\cn BK:  The word "calm" means that the man was quiet, in his right mind, and peaceful.
\tst Tst3:  How was the man now clothed and calm?  Testing respondent changed his posture
to sit correctly, and quietly, and then said, "I now sit calm, like the man was doing.  He
was like this because he was now without the demons, they had left him.
\tst Tst3:  Why did the people go and tell about this?  Because Jesus had cast the demons
out of the man.  This is astonishing.  The pig watchers were tellings people, so they
came to see this true thing that Jesus had done.  They saw it and were astonished.  Now
they are going and telling about it.
\tst Tst3:  This line could be simplified to "They saw the man who was possessed by demons
sitting next to Jesus, wearing clothes, and calm."  He also omitted the phrase, "They
went and told this about".  Could be deleted as it does not add to the theme of the
story.  Revised.
\ln 34.20
\bt Everybody was {astonished}, so they asked him to leave their
{country}.  Why?  Because they were afraid.
\anc mrk.05:15 , mrk.05:17 , luk.08:35 , luk.08:37
\tst Why would they ask Jesus to leave?  They were afraid of this strange thing
\tst Why did the people ask Jesus to leave?  Because of the amazing thing Jesus did.  Why
would they want him to leave?  Because they were afraid He would do it again.  Was this
not a good thing that Jesus did for them?  It was good that the man was healed, but it
was not good that the pigs died?  Is Jesus good?  Yes, he healed the man.  This was
good.
\tst Tst3:  Why are they astonished?  Because the demons were out of the man.  The whole
village could not control him, but Jesus who was one man, made the demons leave the
man and he is now healthy.
\tst Tst3:  Why were they afraid of Jesus?  Because they didn't believe what he had done. 
They did not want to take his road, they were on their own road.  Jesus was only one
man when the whole village couldn't control him.  Only Jesus made the demons leave. 
The man was healthy.  Here, this whole village would be scared if this happened here.  If
this happened tomorrow, everybody would be scared.  The demons listened to only
Jesus, only Jesus.
\tst Tst3:  In his retelling, he changes the sentence structure to state, "They were afraid and
then they asked Jesus to leave their country."  However, in tst4, the sentence structure
of the "Why?  Because.." was kept as is and does not need changing.
\ln 34.21
\bt Jesus, when returning back, the man who was possessed by the
demons asked him to follow Jesus.
\anc mrk.05:18
\cn BK:  Here, the phrase "returning back" means Jesus is returning to the place where he
came from/ leaving.
\tst Why did the man want to go with Jesus?  Because Jesus had healed him.  Because Jesus
was good for him.  
\tst Tst3:  Why did the demon possessed man want to follow Jesus?  Because Jesus had
made him healthy and chased the demons out of him.  He wanted to go be one of his
students, because he had healed him.  And because Jesus was good for him - everything
he had done for him was good.
\ln 34.22
\bt So Jesus said stay here and tell people the strange thing [kh:
extraordinary things] that he has done to him.
\anc mrk.05:19
\tst Why would Jesus tell the man to stay and tell?  Because this thing had happened to him. 
he could tell about Jesus' strength
\tst Why did Jesus tell him to stay?  So people will believe in Jesus and like Jesus.  
\tst Tst3:  Why did Jesus tell him to stay?  Because Jesus wanted him to stay and tell all his
people of his country what the astonishing things Jesus had done for him.
\tst Tst3:  In retelling, he omits "strange thing" and just states "the thing that has happened"
... however, this is most likely just a performance error as he does use the word
"strange thing" at other times.  Also, in tst4, she does restate this line using the phrase
"strange thing".  It will remain as is.
\ln 34.23
\bt And the man left and went around everywhere telling people what had
happened.
\old And the man went to tell the story everywhere, to all the people in the villages and
hamlets.
\anc mrk.05:20
\tst Tst3:  Why did the man tell the story everywhere?  Because it had happened.  Jesus
wanted everybody to believe in him.  The man believed it was Jesus/him.  He went to tell
people, so others could believe.
\tst Tst3:  Here, the word for "hamlets" is not retold, It could be simplified to ... "to tell the
story to people in many villages."  The word for "hamlet" does not seem highly
retellable.  It is not retold in Tst4 either and will be cut.
\tst Tst3:  While in his retelling, he does not use the word "story", but states, "he went and
told this ...".   Line has been revised with help of craftor.  See above.
\ln 34.24
\bt The people were {astonished}.  
\old And that action astonished everybody.
\anc mrk.05:20
\tst Tst3:  Why were people astonished?  Because the whole place tried to control him and
only Jesus could.  Jesus made the man healthy.  They were astonished because of all
that.
\tst Tst3:  How did Jesus do this strange thing to him?  Jesus did this because he was the
Savior that had come.  Everybody knew the Savior was coming, but it was Jesus.  Jesus
did this.  Only Jesus could save him.  Jesus saved him when he made the demons leave
him, now he is not tied up, out in the field or living in the cemetary, but he is healthy and
home with his family.  Jesus saved this man.
\tst Tst3:  Based on retelling, this could also be simplified to, "The people were astonished."  

\tst
\ln Further Testing Comments from Group of Men in Nearwhy:  
\tst What part of the story do you like?  When Jesus healed the man by kicking the demons
out.
\tst What part of the story do you not like?  Pigs dying.  Why did they have to die?  Also,
when Jesus tells the man to stay here.
\tst What does the story tell you about God?  We should trust God.  God is stronger than the
demons.  God can kick out demons.
\tst What does the story tell you about people?  We should run/walk beside Jesus.  We
should follow his road.  When you take the Jesus road, he can change your life.  God's
words are true.
