\c 36
\t Jesus heals woman and daughter
\co Supyire
\p
\co Redemptive Theme:  Jesus has the power to save people from sickness.  The story
builds on the redemptive theme that it is a belief or trust in Jesus that saves people.
\co Basic Biblical concepts :  Jesus has God's healing power.  Jesus has power over
death.  
\co Worldview/Selection:  Sickness is everywhere here.  As the Supyire people often
seek healing power through sacrifices to fetishes or other intermediaries, this story
was selected to show Jesus' power over sickness.
\p    
\co Story Craftor: SS
\co Story Backtranslator:  BK
\co
\co BT file last Revised:  15Oct08
\co Audio Last Revised:  24Sep08
\p  
\tst Testing Comments:  Original Testing done in our village.  
\tst Tst2:  Group of men in NearWhy.  This story was retold well and well understood.  
\tst Tst3:  Day Guard 
\tst Tst4:  Phone Booth friend - tested for retelling.  
\p
\ln 36.01
\bt This is something true that happened.
\anc 2Ti.03:16 , Psa.119:142 (New Century Version) "...your teachings are true";
Psa.119:160 (NIV) "all your words are true"; Jhn.17:17 "your word is truth".
\ln 36.02
\bt Jesus and his students {KT: disciples} were travelling to another
village.  Many people came and gathered around him.
\old When Jesus was going on the other side of the river, many people came and gathered
around him.
\cn MM:  This line has been modified to keep things cohesive with the demoniac story before
this.  We did not have them "crossing the river" in that story, but just stated it as they
were "travelling" to another village.  We wanted to keep it consistent here.
\anc mrk.05:21
\tst Tst3:  Why were people gathering around him?  Because they knew that their Savior had
come.  The book had said the Savior would come and he would be king.  It's Jesus and
he had come to them.
\ln 36.03
\bt One leader [KT {leaders}] of God's Words Schoolhouse came before
Jesus and he kneeled down in front of Jesus and said,
\old One {leader} of the church [MM: God's praying {house} ] came before Jesus and he
kneeled down in front of Jesus and said,
\co **** NEW *******
\anc mrk.05:22
\cn MM:  God's Words Schoolhouse is the keyterm for "synagogue".  It is what is used in the
Supyire NT draft.
\tst Tst3:  Why would this leader kneel down in front of him?  He came and kneeled in front
of Jesus because he wants his child to be healthy.  He is down like that because he is
begging Jesus.  Because he wants his child well, so she won't die.  He kneeled because
Jesus is the Savior and could save his child.
\ln 36.04
\bt "My little daughter is about to die.  I {ask} you, come and put your
hand on her, so that she can recover."
\old "My little daughter is about to die.  So come and put your hand on her head, so that she
can recover and get up."
\anc mrk.05:23 , French Text in Le Parole de Vie states, "Come and put your hands on her
head so that she will be healed and live."
\cn MM:  The phrase "get up" here is used and associated with wellness.  It is also used in
greetings from time to time, when asking "How is someone?"  They can reply, "They
have gotten up."  Which means they are well.
\tst Testing Group 2:  Why does the man come and kneel before Jesus?  He wanted his little
girl to be healed.  She was dying.  He trusted Jesus.
\tst Why does he want Jesus to put his hand on his daughter?  He knows that Jesus is strong
and can heal her.
\tst Is it normal for people to be healed in this way?  No, but Jesus can.  This is why the
leader wants Jesus to put his hands on his daughter's head.
\tst Tst3:  How could Jesus help his daughter?  He could pray to God and ask God not to let
the child die.  Jesus is God's Son, so if Jesus prays and asks for his daughter to be well
and not die, God will accept because Jesus is his son.  Because Jesus is the Savior.
\tst Tst4: In retelling, she omits the phrase "get up".  
\tst Tst3:  In retelling, he omits "on her head" and "get up"  ... These phrases can be
deleted.  Revised.
\ln 36.05
\bt Then Jesus took the road to go there.    
\old Then they took the road.
\anc mrk.05:24
\cn MM:  This is the cultural way of leaving.  Before anyone can leave a place, they must
literally ask their company "for the road."  Asking, 'May they leave?'
\tst Testing Group 2:  Who took the road?  Why?  Jesus, the leader of God's praying big
house, the people who were following Jesus.  They went to the leader of God's praying
big house.
\ln 36.06
\bt Then many people followed him.  Some were even walking on his
heels.
\anc mrk.05:24
\tst How can they "Walk on his heels"?   Many people were crowding around him, so much so
that they were in effect stepping on his feet.  They were "pressed" upon him.
\tst In Testing Group 2, they acted this out.  Actually walking so closely being him, they were
stepping on his heels.  
\tst tst3:  How does someone "walk on his heels"?  Well, the people were so many on the
road they were all close and stepping on each other, they were too many together.
\tst Tst3, Tst4:  In both retellings, they included the expression above "walking on his heels"
as in the original.  
\ln 36.07
\bt Among the crowd, there was a woman who was sick for 12 years.
\anc mrk.05:24
\tst Tst3:  Why do you think she was sick for so long?  She was sick for a really long time,
12 years.  She went to get well, but they took her money.  She still wasn't healthy.  The
healers couldn't do it, but she knew all she had to do was touch Jesus clothes.
\ln 36.08
\bt And she went to many healers until her fortune had disappeared.  But
there was not any progress.
\old She  [MM:  was suffering] and she went to many healers until the lady's fortune had
disappeared.  But there was not any progress.
\anc mrk.05:26
\cn MM:  There are many "traditional African healers" and traditional medicine still being
practiced here.  This part of the story shows that while this traditional method of healing
was not successful, Jesus' power is more powerful than this.
\tst Would this happen here?  Yes, it could.  It's possible for this to happen here in Mali.
\tst Tst4:  She omits "She was suffering".  
\tst Tst3: In retelling, he omits "She was suffering".  This can be deleted as it seems
apparents without stating explicitly. Deleted.
\ln 36.09
\bt She said inside, "As soon as I touch Jesus' clothes, I will be healed."
\old So she came behind [MM: through] the crowd and touched Jesus' clothes.
\anc mrk.05:27
\tst In Testing Group 2, they acted this scene out.  Woman comes up through the crowd and
touches the backside of Jesus' clothes.  Jesus does not see her, because there were
many people around him.  He didn't see her.  He asked, "Who touched me?"
\tst Tst3:  How does the woman approach Jesus?  She was down.  There were many people. 
She went slowly, slowly, and she just reached out to touch him.  There were many many
people, she could only go small small.
\tst Tst4:  This line, as well as line 10 was retold as is.  
\ln 36.10
\bt So she came through the crowd and touched Jesus' clothes.  
\old Inside she thought that as soon as she touched Jesus' clothes, she will recover.
\anc mrk.05:28
\tst Tst3:  Why does she want to touch his clothes?  So her sickness would be finished.  She
believed Jesus was the Savior.  She had to only touch his clothes.  She didn't have to
even touch his skin for him to save her.
\tst Tst3:  In retelling, he chronologically places this line before line 09.  This seems to make
the story flow more naturally. Revised.
\ln 36.11
\bt When she touched Jesus' clothes, she was healed.
\old When she touched Jesus' clothes, she {noticed} that she was healed.
\anc mrk.05:29
\tst Tst3:  How does she notice that she is healed?  Because she knew that she had touched
Jesus' clothes.  She knew Jesus could make her healthy.  Jesus knew he had been
touched because she was healthy too.  Because her sickness was finished.
\tst Tst3:  In retelling, he states, "she found that ..." instead of "noticed". 
\tst Tst4:  In her retelling, here, she restates, "She came and touched Jesus' clothes." 
Based on retellings, this line can be simplified to, "When she touched Jesus' clothes, she
was healed."  Revised.
\ln 36.12
\bt Then Jesus knew that a force {KT: power} had left him to heal
someone.  So Jesus asked, "Who touched my clothes?"
\old So Jesus noticed that a force {KT: power} left Jesus.  So Jesus asked, "Who touched my
clothes?"
\anc mrk.05:30 NET , CONNOT, "Jesus felt a force leave him and he knew his power had
caused someone to be healed" 
\tst Tst3:  Why does Jesus ask, 'Who touched my clothes""?  Because he felt it.  When
someone touches you, and your clothes, you know , you can feel it, Jesus felt it.  How
does he know someone touched him?  Then, he looked around to see and he saw the
woman shaking - he knew he had been touched.
\tst Tst3:  In retelling, he states, "Jesus 'felt/found' ..." instead of "noticed".  
\tst Tst4:  She restates this part as, "A force of Jesus left him."  
\tst Based on retelling,  can be changed as suggested in CONNOT, "Jesus felt a force leave
him and he knew his power had caused someone to be healed"  Revised.
\ln 36.13
\bt His students answered, "Teacher {KT: Master}, you can see that there
are too many people around you.  Then, you are still asking the
question, 'Who touched you?'"
\anc mrk.05:31
\tst Testing Group 2:  Why does Jesus' students ask Jesus this?  People were really crowded
around Jesus.  There were many people that trusted Jesus.  They crowded around him. 
Many were touching and bumping up against him.
\tst Testing Group 2:  If there were many people pressing against Jesus, why was only this
woman healed?  She trusted Jesus.  Jesus knew her insides.
\ln 36.14a
\bt Jesus was looking in all directions.  
\anc mrk.05:32
\ln 36.14b
\bt The woman who was healed was so frightened that she was even
shaking.
\old Jesus was looking in all directions, then the girl that touched him was afraid, until she
was shaking.
\anc mrk.05:33
\tst Testing Group 2:  Why is the woman afraid?  Jesus is looking around.  She thought he
wouldn't know someone touched him.  He knew.
\ln 36.15
\bt And she came and kneeled down in front of Jesus and told him
everything.
\old And that one came and kneeled down in front of Jesus to tell all the truth [MM:
everything].
\anc mrk.05:33
\tst Tst3:  Why did the woman come and tell the truth?  Because she had been sick for 12
years.  She told Jesus everything because she now knows he is the Savior. He had
saved her from her sickness.  She believed in Jesus and had wanted her sickness
finished.
\tst Tst3:  In retelling, he states, "She went and knelt down ..", more natural than "And that
one came.."  This will change.
\ln 36.16
\bt Then Jesus said, "Go in {peace}.  God healed you.  Why?  Because you
trusted {KT: trust} me.
\old Then Jesus said, "Go.  Your trust has healed you.  May God save you."
\anc mrk.05:34
\tst Testing Group 2:  Why has he healed her?  Because she trusted in him.  
\tst Tst2 explained: "Go in peace" is a blessing commonly used here for those who are sick...
asking God to give them peace.  It's also a good thing to say when leaving a group.  May
God give you peace as you leave.
\tst Tst3:  How has God healed her?  Because she believed that Jesus was the Savior.  Jesus
said - May God give you good health - Jesus was God's Son, She believed he could save
her from her sickness.  Why?  Why?  Because she believed Jesus could make her
healthy - she touched his clothes and is healthy because she believed.
\ln 36.17
\bt And that {moment}, some men came from the house of the leader of
God's Words Schoolhouse and said to the man, "Your daughter is
dead.  Let Jesus in peace."
\old And that {moment}, some men came from the house of the leader of the church and
said to the man, "Your daughter is dead.  Let Jesus in peace."
\old And that {moment}, some men left the family of the leader of the church and said to the
man, "Don't bother the teacher.  Your daughter is dead.  Let our Teacher in peace."
\old And that moment, some men left the family of the leader of the church and said to the
man, "Don't bother the teacher.  Your daughter is dead.  Let our father in peace."
\co ******* NEW *****
\anc mrk.05:35
\tst Why do they say 'Let our Teacher in peace'?  It means that they should not bother or
disturb Jesus anymore.  
\tst Testing Group 2:  Who were these people talking to?  The girl's father and one leader of
God's praying big house.  
\tst Testing Group 2:  Acted out the word "bother".  It means as it does in English. 
Constantly interupting and asking something of someone...  Why were they saying this? 
Because the man's daughter had already died.  Leave him.
\tst Testing Group 2:  Who is the Teacher here?  Jesus.
\tst Tst3:  Why did they say, "Don't bother the teacher?"  Because the child had died and
they didn't believe Jesus could make her alive again.
\tst Tst3:  In retelling, he states, "Leave Jesus in peace.  Your little girl is dead."  
\tst Tst4:  In her retelling, she states the first line as, "Don't cause the Teacher to suffer."  It
does not seem the phrase "Don't bother him" is natural in retelling.
\tst Based on retellings, this line can be restated as, " Your daughter is dead.  Leave Jesus in
peace."  Revised.  
\ln 36.18
\bt Then Jesus said, "Trust in me.  I can heal her."  
\old Then Jesus said, "Don't be afraid.  Trust only."
\anc mrk.05:36 , TW the "Index of Implicit Information..." states "believe that I can still help
her."
\tst Testing Group 2:  Why does Jesus say this?  Because Jesus will heal her.  Trust him.
\tst Tst3:  This line was omitted in retelling.
\tst Tst4:  This line was not retold here either.  TW, CONNOT suggests that sometimes "fear"
does not culturally fit here as a response to death.  This could be the case here.  And
also, sometimes "belief/trust" requires an object.  Therefore this could possibly be
restated as "Then Jesus said, 'Trust in me.  I can heal your daughter."    Revised.
\ln 36.19
\bt So Jesus took the road with three of his students.
\anc mrk.05:37
\ln 36.20
\bt When they reached the family, they found that people were crying
and shouting.
\anc mrk.05:38
\tst Why were the people doing this?  They were sad.  They thought the child had died.  
\tst Tst3:  Why were they crying and shouting?  Becaues they thought the child had died.  
\ln 36.21
\bt Then Jesus asked them, "Why are you crying and shouting?"
\anc mrk.05:39
\tst Tst3:  Why does Jesus ask "Why are you crying and shouting?" Because Jesus wanted
them to know the child hasn't died.  Jesus liked them and didn't want them to have to
cry.
\ln 36.22
\bt "The child will not be dead for much longer."
\old Jesus said, "The [MM: child] is not dead.  She is just sleeping."
\anc mrk.05:39
\anc TW, CONNOT, "Commentaries support the view that the girl really died and that Jesus
performed a miracle in returning her life to her. [Swete (p. 108) says: ‚ÄòThe fact of the
child‚Äôs death was obvious to the bystanders, and is apparently assumed by the
Evangelists‚Äô. Cf. Luke 8.53.]
\anc A second CONNOT has rendered the verse as, "The child has not died permanently, but
is sleeping."  
\anc Gundry Commentary on Mark states, "We should understand that Jesus' determination to
raise the girl from death and his confidence of success lead him to deny death with
respect to its present, apparent irreversibility and to hint at his raising the girl by using
the euphemism of sleep... for its happy similarity to the short duration of this particular
death and for the happy similarity between awaking someone from sleep and the miracle
of raising the girl that he is about to perform
\tst Tst3:  Why does Jesus say the child is not dead, she is sleeping?  Because the child
would not die.  Jesus said she was just sleeping so she was.  Jesus knew that he could
get her up.  He knew he could pray and God would answer.  But he didn't have to pray. 
He just touched her, put his hand on her, and told her to get up.
\tst Tst3:  Based on his answer, it seems possible to interpret this line as that the child has
not really died at all, but has only been sleeping this whole time.
\tst Tst3 : Retold these lines, line 21 and 22.
\tst Tst4:  She did not retell lines 21 and 22.   Based on the confusion in these lines from the
testing question and her omitting these lines altogether, we should make this clearer. 
Based on commentary anchors above, this line could say, "The child is not permanently
dead."  or "The child will not be dead for much longer."  Revised.
\ln 36.23
\bt And people were laughing at Jesus  And Jesus entered the small room
with his three students, the girl's father and her mother.
\anc mrk.05:40
\tst Why were the people laughing at Jesus?  They were mocking him.  They thought he
wasn't very intelligent, because they thought the child was dead.
\ln 36.24
\bt And Jesus said to the child, "You, get up."
\old And said to the child, "You, get up."  
\old When he reached her, he put his hand on the girl.   And said, "You, get up." 
\anc mrk.05:41
\tst Tst3:  Why does Jesus put his hand on her?  To make her get up.  It is like when you are
asleep and someone touches you, you wake up.  He did this so she would get up.
\tst Tst3:  In retelling, "When he reached her" was omitted and can be deleted from the
story.  Revised.  
\ln 36.25
\bt And Jesus took her hand to get up.
\anc mrk.05:41
\ln 36.26
\bt And the girl starts walking.
\old And the girl starts walking.  She was about 12 years old.
\anc mrk.05:42
\tst Tst3:  How could the girl get up and walk?  Because Jesus accepted for her to be up and
walking and eating.  Jesus was the girl's savior because he put his hands on her and told
her to get up.  She was the child of a boss from God's prayer house - who went to Jesus
and prayed to him.
\ln 36.27
\bt And Jesus said for the child's mother and father to give her some
food.
\old And Jesus said that to her parents to give her some food.
\anc mrk.05:43
\tst Tst3:  In retelling, he states "to her mother and father" and does not use the word for
"parents". 
\tst Tst4:  Again, in her retelling, she states "her mother and father."  For some reason, the
Supyire word for "parent" does not seem as reproducible as "mother and father".  We
will change this line.   Revised.
\ln 36.28
\bt And everybody was {astonished}.
\anc mrk.05:42
\tst Tst3:  Why were people astonished?  Because everybody said she was dead, but she
wasn 't dead.  Jesus healed her, touched her, accepted her, and she was undead.  She
came back from dead.
\p
\p
\tst Testing Group 2:  What part do you like about the story?  When the woman is healed
after touching Jesus' clothes, the woman is "right", Jesus tells the woman to go, Jesus
can do to us the same, we will not die, we can trust in Jesus and our bad-things can be
finished.  Jesus gives happiness/peace.
\tst Testing Group 2:  What's not good about this story?  The woman was sick for 12 years
and was not better, no medicine helped.  That's a long time.  When the people were
mocking Jesus - that's not good.
\tst What does the story tell us about Jesus?  He is the truth.  He is right.
\dt 01/Jan/2009

\c 38
\t Assurance Story - John 10
\co Senufo Supyire
\p
\co Redemptive Theme:  This story shows the relationship between Jesus and those
who follow Him, his sheep.  Those who have relationship with Jesus will be saved. 
Those in relationship with Jesus can have assurance that no one can take you away
from him as Jesus is all-powerful over all evil.
\co Basic Biblical concepts:  Jesus and God are one.  Jesus can give eternal life to those
who follow Him.   Jesus will die to save those in relationship with him.
\co Cohesion / Background:  The story builds the plot of those who are against Jesus
and sets the stage for the religious leaders to kill him.  Builds on relationship as
Jesus is God's Son, but they are also one.  Builds on the knowledge that Jesus will
die for the sins of man.
\p
\co Story crafter's name or initials: SS
\co Backtranslator's name or initials: BK
\p
\co Audio Last Revised:  29Sep08
\co BT File Last Revised:  14Oct08
\p
\tst Original Testing:  In village, with language helper and another friend.
\tst Tst2:  Day Guard.  I was surprised by the details that he kept in the retelling.  My first
thought was that this story needed shortening, but based on this retelling, it seems only
minor changes are required.  Even wording and phrases are kept the same as original. 
See BT text for comments.
\p
\ln 38.01
\bt This is something true that happened.
\anc 2Ti.03:16 , Psa.119:142 (New Century Version) "...your teachings are true";
Psa.119:160 (NIV) "all your words are true"; Jhn.17:17 "your word is truth".
\ln 38.02
\bt Many of God's praying {house} {leaders} did not {accept} Jesus.  
\anc  jhn.05:18
\tst Why did they not like Jesus?  The words Jesus is saying are not good for them.  They
know Jesus' road is good, but they don't like His road - they like the dark road.
\tst Tst2:  Why did they not accept Jesus?  Because Jesus is not good for them.  They did not
like Jesus because he was there to save people and they could not.
\ln 38.03
\bt So, they were trying to put a trap against Jesus because of his
words.  
\anc jhn.05:18 , 
\cn BK:  "To set a trap" literally means to set the thing that people use to catch animals, to
plot to catch him.
\tst Tst2:  How would they set a trap against Jesus?  Like a trap that you step into, it grabs
your foot and holds you.  They want to trap Jesus because of the true things he is doing.
\tst Tst2:  Why because of his words?  Because of the words he says and they hear, they
don't like it.  So they want to trap him.  His words are true, but they say they are not.
\tst This line was retold as is. 
\ln 38.04
\bt One day, Jesus said, "I am the Good Shepherd."  
\old One day, when they were talking with Jesus, Jesus said, "I am the [MM: Good]
Shepherd."  
\anc jhn.10:14
\cn MM:  The phrase "Good Shepherd" is the same as the one used in the Supyire
Translation.
\tst Why does Jesus say He is the Good Shepherd?  He is God's Son.  God's Child - His road
is good.  Why is he like a good shepherd?  He wants to show people the good road - the
best road.
\tst Tst2:  How is Jesus a good shepherd?  Because the shepherd speaks good words.  He
talks to his sheep and they know his words.
\tst Tst2:  In retelling, this line was shortened to, "Then he said, I am the Good Shepherd." 
This could be shortened.    
\ln 38.05
\bt "My sheep know me and I also know them."
\anc jhn.10:14
\tst How do sheep know Jesus?  What do sheep do when they know you?  The sheep know
Jesus is good.  They see you.  They speak.  They approach and come near you.  Jesus'
sheep are people.
\tst Tst2:  How can Jesus know them?  Jesus knows them because there is one shepherd,
Jesus.  He knows his sheep and they know him because he is one.
\tst Tst2:  What are Jesus' sheep?  They are those who are his students.  
\tst Tst2:  How are they like sheep?  Sheep can be taught and can follow and go along.  So
we are like them.  We follow along.
\ln 38.06
\bt "My Father loves {KT: love} me.  {Why}?  Because I am going to give
my soul [MM: life] {KT: spirit} for my sheep, to save them {KT
Savior}."
\old "My Father loves {KT: love} me.  {Why}?  Because I am going to give my soul [MM:
life] {KT: spirit} in the name of my sheep." [MM:  for my sheep]
\anc jhn.10:15
\cn MM:  The phrase here is the same as the one used in the Supyire Translation.  "I will
give my life for my sheep"
\tst What do you think Jesus is saying he is going to do?  He will walk God's road and be
very tired for his sheep.  How will Jesus give his soul?  They are going to catch Jesus, kill
Jesus - but he is not going to run - he knows his heart is good and he is correct.
\tst Tst2:  Why does his father love him?  Because he is his Son.  Parents love their
children.  Jesus did things that were good for his father.  He said God's words and saved
God's people.  All of this was good for him and his Father.
\tst Tst2:  The line was retold as is.  However, it was unpacked to say, "He will give his spirit
(or life) for his sheep.  He will save his sheep.  He will give his spirit for his sheep and
save them.  He cannot be killed.  He will give his spirit and take it back again."  For
cohesive purposes, it would be good to unpack "give my spirit/life for my sheep" and say
"I will give my life, to save my sheep."  Revised.
\ln 38.07
\bt "No one can kill me, I will give my soul [MM:life] and take it [MM: back
again]."
\anc jhn.10:18
\tst How can he do this?  This means "I will give my life - they will kill me - but I will come
back to life.  I will leave death - take back my life from death.
\tst Why does Jesus say no one can kill him?  He knows they can't kill him - He is God's
Son.  He is strong - but he will give his life to them.
\tst Tst2:  How can Jesus give his soul for his sheep?  When his sheep die, Jesus will give his
own life for them.  He will give himself for their life/soul.
\tst Tst2:  Why will he give his soul?  Because his sheep are good for him.  He does not want
his sheep to die
\tst Tst2:  How will he take it back?  Jesus will go for them.  He will die and give his soul for
them.  He will die but 3 days later he will come back to life and take his soul back.
\tst Tst2:  How can no one kill him?  No one can take the life of God's Son.  No one can take
it from him.   
\tst Tst2:  This line was retold.  
\ln 38.08
\old That {moment} coincided with the cold and the day of the feast of God's praying house
was approaching.
\anc jhn.10:22 - 23
\tst What festival is this?  When does it happen?  Every year?  Confusion over this - knows it
is during cold season, but it seems this sentence is unclear as to what the fete is and if it
is a yearly occurance.
\tst Tst2:  Why would the people of God's praying house have a feast?  Because it is good
for them, for the work and what they do.
\tst Tst2:  Although retold, there seems confusion as to the feast that is coming and the cold
season, may be best to delete this line.    Deleted.
\ln 38.09
\bt Then, Jesus went to God's praying house and was wandering about
outside God's praying house.  
\old So Jesus went to God's praying house and was wandering about the God's praying
house's yard.
\anc jhn.10:23
\tst Tst2:  Why would Jesus wander the yard?  Because it was good for him to be there and
for him to pray to God.  When he was there walking, when the cold had come, the
people came near to him and asked when they would leave the darkness.
\ln 38.10
\bt Then some people came near him and asked him, "When are you
going to take us out of darkness?"
\anc jhn.10:24
\cn MM:  Again, this is the same phrase used in the Supyire Translation
\tst Tst2:  Why did the people ask Jesus, "When are you going to take us out of darkness?" 
Because they knew that Jesus could give them the light.  How can Jesus take them out of
darkness?  Jesus took them from the darkness, like when the night is over and the day
opens or when you close and then open your eyes to the light.  The people will come
with Jesus into the light.
\ln 38.11
\bt If you are the Savior we are waiting for {KT: Christ}, if you are that
one, tell us frankly.
\old "If you are the one chosen by God, tell us frankly."
\anc jhn.10:24
\tst Tst2:  Why do they want to know if Jesus is the one chosen by God?  Because they want
to know if Jesus can take them out of the darkness.  God's Chosen one can.  That is
what God's Chosen one will do.
\ln 38.12
\bt Then Jesus said, "The speeches that I am saying and the things that I
am doing have already told you frankly."
\anc jhn.10:25
\tst Tst2:  Why does Jesus say this?  Because Jesus has said God's Word to them and done
extraordinary things.  They all already know what Jesus has said and done.
\ln 38.13
\bt "But you didn't believe {KT: trust} them.  Why?  Because [MM:  you
are not my sheep.]"
\anc jhn.10:26
\tst Why does Jesus say this to the people?  He says that the things I do, the work I do, the
words I say, shows you I am God's Chosen One.
\tst Why does he say they are not his sheep?  His sheep know him, walk with him,
understand his words.  They are not like his sheep - they don't walk together with him.
\tst Tst2:  Why do they not believe Jesus?  The people from God's praying house do not
believe that Jesus can be God's Chosen One, they don't believe he is God.
\tst Tst2:  How are they not his sheep?  Because Jesus sheep are his students and they
believe in him, and follow, but these do not.
\ln 38.14
\bt "My sheep know me and I also know them.  They listen to my words. 
They also follow me."
\anc jhn.10:27
\tst What is the "they" referring to?  Jesus' sheep.
\tst Tst2:  Why would Jesus's sheep follow him?  Because Jesus has said God's Words and
done extraordinary things - they follow after him because he is the one shepherd they
knew and go after him.
\ln 38.15
\bt "I will give life {forever} to my sheep.  
\anc jhn.10:28
\ln 38.15b
\bt It's my Father who gave them to me.  No one can take them from me
by force {KT: power}.  Why?  Because God who gave them to me is
stronger than anyone in the entire {world}."
\anc jhn.10:29
\cn MM:  The phrase "take them from me" was explained in testing to mean "to take/pull
from".  Ex:  Jesus‚Äô people in one car,  another car of people in darkness.  No one from
the darkness car can steal/take anyone from Jesus‚Äô car.  Jesus‚Äô people cannot be pulled
into the other car.
\tst What is "they" referring to?  Jesus' sheep.
\tst How does Jesus‚Äô Father give him sheep?  Who is Jesus‚Äô Father?  God.  Jesus is the
sheep‚Äôs shepherd ‚Äì He works with the sheep God gave.
\tst Why does Jesus say no one can take them from Him?  God is stronger than everything. 
There is 1 God ‚Äì we should take His road.  Once you take God‚Äôs road ‚Äì people in
darkness can‚Äôt take you ‚Äì God is strong and will help you.
\tst Tst2:  How did God give Jesus his sheep?  Because God knew Jesus would give them his
words, Jesus is the only one.  
\tst Tst2:  How is he stronger than anyone in the world?  God gave the sheep to Jesus
because he gives them God's Words.  God's Words and God's strength is above/over the
world .  God gave his sheep to Jesus - He has made Jesus stronger for them.
\tst Tst2:  In retelling, he restates a second time, "I will give life forever to my sheep.  God
gave them to me."  This is most likely performance error as he then continues and
finishes the line as in the original.
\ln 38.16
\bt "I am the equal of God."  [MM:  God and I are one.]
\anc jhn.10:30
\cn MM:  Again, this phrase is the same used in the Supyire Translation.  It literally
translates, "God and I are one."  
\tst Why does Jesus say this?  He and God are one.  How?  God and He are the same.  Jesus
is righteous.  He is God's Son.  The same kind of way you say me and my father are
one.
\tst Tst2:  How can Jesus be one with God?  Because they have the same will, when you
have the same will, you are one.
\ln 38.17
\bt At the {moment} that Jesus said that, they took stones to kill him.
\anc jhn.10:31
\tst Tst2:  Why do they want to kill Jesus?  It was not for the strange things he did, but
because he said that he and God are one - this word is not good for them because they
don't think he can be one with God.
\ln 38.18
\bt Then Jesus asked them, "The good things that I did amongst you,
because of which one do you want to kill me by throwing stones?"
\old Then Jesus asked them, "The many strange {KT: extraordinary} things that I did
amongst you, because of which one do you want to kill me by throwing stones?"
\anc jhn.10:32
\tst Tst2:  In retelling, he uses the word "good things" here for "extraordinary things".  And
in line 19, he switches "good works" to "extraordinary things."  It is best for these to be
cohesive and to maintain scriptural accuracy "good things" is most closely linked to
scriptural meaning.  Revised.
\ln 38.19
\bt And they said, "It's not for the good things that you have done that
we want to kill you.  But, you, a human, compare yourself with God."
\old And they said, "It's not because of your [MM:  good works] that we want to kill you by
throwing, but we want to kill you because you destroy God's name.  Why?  Because you
are a human being, how are you going to compare yourself with God?"
\anc jhn.10:33
\cn MM:  It is the same word/phrase used here in the Supyire Translation for "good works".  
\tst Why do the people want to kill Jesus?  Not because of his good things/good work, but
because he broke the name of God.  They said Jesus is the same as people - but he tries
to measure himself with God.
\tst Tst2:  How did Jesus destroy God's name?  By saying that he and God are one - they
think that has broken God's name because they think you cannot be one with God.
\tst Tst2:  How is Jesus, a human, like God?  Because Jesus is God's Son.  They are one. 
But I am not one with my father - because of the bad things I have done.  When you do
bad things, you cannot be one - but Jesus and God are one.
\tst Tst2:  In retelling, he omits, "that we want to kill you by throwing, but we want to kill you
because you destroy God's name".  These phrases can be deleted as they do not add to
the story, but only make the phrase more complicated.  We can restate this more closely
to the retelling as, "It's not for the good things that you have done, but because you, a
human, compare yourself with God."  Revised.
\ln 38.20
\bt Then Jesus said, "Even if you don't believe {KT: trust} my words, you
can see that the good things I do and God's good things are one.  God
and I are one."
\old Then Jesus said, "Things that I am doing and the words that I am saying, even if you
don't {believe} my words, you should believe in those things.  If those are God's and
God's ones are the same you should know that I am the equal of God."
\anc jhn.10:38
\cn BK: It is clear that "if the things Jesus is doing" are God's, God's work is the same, then
they should know that He and God are one.
\tst What does Jesus say here?  Don't trust in my words - but the things I do that you see. 
Trust in these.  If the work I do, what I say, is God's work - you see this - then believe
in my words - God and I are one.
\tst Example - Jesus says rain will come, then God gives the rain - Jesus' work is God's work
- they are one.
\tst Tst2:  Why should they believe what Jesus does when they don't believe his words? 
Because they didn't believe his words, that they are one, but Jesus is like God because
of the things he has done.  The things he has done, they can believe in.
\tst Tst2:  How can "God's ones" know that Jesus is equal to God?  Because of the things he
has done - they believe that Jesus and God are one.  Why?  Because the things he has
done are as one with God.
\tst Tst2:  In retelling this is simplified,  And can be rephrased as, "Even if you do not believe
my words, you can see that the good things that I do and God's good things are one . 
God and I are one."  Revised.
\ln 38.21
\bt At the moment Jesus said that, they tried to catch him but they didn't
succeed.  
\anc jhn.10:39
\tst Tst2:  Why did they try to catch him?  Because they do not believe his words or believe
that he and God are one.  So they wanted to catch him so they could kill him.
\tst Tst2:  Why didn't they succeed?  Because God didn't accept/allow it.  God sent Jesus to
save them, so he ran away.  
\p
\ln Further Testing Questions from Original Testing:
\tst What part of the story do you like?  When Jesus says ‚ÄúI am God‚Äôs Son ‚Äì He and God are
one.‚Äù  Where it says ‚ÄúGod is stronger than the whole world.‚Äù
\tst What part do you not like?  Where they picked up rocks to kill Jesus. 
\tst What does the story say about God?  God alone is the true God. 
\tst What does the story say about people?  People who are Jesus‚Äô sheep, he likes, but
people who are not his sheep, he doesn‚Äôt like.

\dt 01/Jan/2009

\c 40
\t Sight Story
\co Supyire
\p
\co Redemptive Theme:   This story builds the redemptive theme that those who trust
in Jesus will be saved.        
\co Basic Biblical concepts :  Jesus will be beaten and killed, but will rise from death.   
\co Cohesion / Background:  Cohesively ties the words of Isaiah and what will happen to
this coming King, to what is about to happen to Jesus.  This is a preordained event. 
Cohesively connects Jesus as David's descendant.  The story calls people to respond
by seeking the power of Jesus, believing in Him, and then praising God for saving
them.
\p
\co Story crafter:: SS
\co Backtranslator: BK
\p
\co Resources Used in Crafting:  Audio versions of French Bible Parole de Vie, Bambara
Bible, Supyire NT draft
\p
\co Audio Last Revised:  20Oct08
\co BT File Last Revised:  21Oct08
\ln
\tst General Testing Comments:  In the initial testing of this story, the story was understood
and was easy to retell.  Unfortunately, some of the connections between this story and
other stories in our story set were not made (i.e. between the Isaiah prophecies and
what Jesus tells his students and the promise that God gives David to provide from his
offspring a king forever).  However, we realize that the testing of these stories have
been somewhat sporadic and not always chronological.  Hopefully, the connection will be
clearer in future storying groups.
\p
\tst Tst2:  Storying Group in Village (group of women in our village family):  Tested for
retellability.  See comments inserted into BT.
\p
\tst Tst3:  Day Guard.  Tested chronologically within story set and the connection between
Isaiah prophecy and Jesus coming from David's offspring were made.  See comments
inserted below.
\p
\ln 40.01
\bt This is something that happened that is also true.
\anc 2Ti.03:16 , Psa.119:142 (New Century Version) "...your teachings are true";
Psa.119:160 (NIV) "all your words are true"; Jhn.17:17 "your word is truth".
\ln 40.02
\bt One day, Jesus gathered his {disciples}.  
\old One day, Jesus gathered all his twelve {disciples}
\anc luk.18:31
\tst Tst3:  Why was Jesus with his disciples?  He was with those 12 men because they were
his students.  They wanted to learn God's Words from him - they were going to
Jerusalem.
\ln 40.03
\bt Then Jesus said, "In a little while..."
\old and said, "We are going to Jerusalem."
\anc luk.18:31
\tst Tst3:  Why were they going to Jerusalem?  Because it was Jesus' village.  It was his
place they were going to.  
\tst Tst2:  Lines 2 and 3 were retold as, "Jesus and his students left to travel to another
village.  And Jesus said, ..."  Depending on future testings, to avoid confusion it may be
best to avoid saying "We are going  to Jerusalem" and simply state "Soon ... all the
things .... (continuing with line 04).  See future testing notes.
\tst Tst3:  In retelling, he states, "Jesus and his 12 disciles were going to Jerusalem."  Based
on repeated confusion in this, this line can be omitted.  And left simply as, Jesus said,
"Soon ..."  Revised.
\ln 40.04
\bt "All the things God's messengers {KT: messenger} said about me  will
happen.  "
\old "All the things God's messengers {KT: messenger} said about me, will happen as it is
said."
\anc luk.18:31
\tst Tst3:  How can these things happen?  Because Jesus was not good for some people. 
God's messenger said that he would be taken, punished, beaten, and killed but he would
rise back to life in 3 days.
\tst Tst2:  In retelling, it was stated that "what my friends have said about me..."  This is
most likely performance error.  In previous retellings, and in previous story retellings
with this particular group, the terminology of "God's messengers" has been used and
retold.
\tst Tst3:  He does use the phrase "God's messengers" in retelling and this will remain as
is.  
\ln 40.05
\bt "They will contradict me [MM: punish me], make me suffer, spit on me,
and kill me.  But three days after my death, I will {rise} from death."
\anc luk.18:32 - 33
\cn MM:  "To spit on" literally translates as "throw saliva on him"
\tst Why is this going to happen?  Because the messengers said it would.  
\tst Tst3:  Why will they punish him and make him suffer?  Because what Jesus says and
does is not good for them, they don't like it.  They are his enemies.  They want him to
die and he will, but then raise back to life in 3 days and then he can go home.
\tst Tst3:  How does Jesus know what will happen?  Because these are the words of God's
messenger and Jesus is God's Son.  He knew this would happen.  He will let them.  He
will not do anything to them.  He is to suffer and die and come back.
\tst Tst3:  How will he rise from death?  God will do it.  Jesus is God's Son.  Jesus will die but
God will bring him back to life.  God will accept him to come to life.  Jesus is the Savior -
he is our Savior, so God will save him from this death.
\tst Tst2:  This line was retold exactly.   
\ln 40.06
\bt The words that Jesus was saying, his disciples did not understand.  
\old When Jesus had said this, his disciples didn't know that [MM: did not understand].  Why? 
Because it was hidden from them.
\anc luk.18:34
\tst There seems to be confusion in this sentence.  Why do the disciples not understand?  It
is hidden from them.  Why is it hidden from them?  Confusion here.  Will further test
these sentences.
\tst Tst3:  Why didn't Jesus' disciples understand?  Jesus' words they refused because they
were not good for them.  The words were too hard for them to understand - the words of
God's messenger and of Jesus.
\tst Tst3:  How was it hidden from them?  Because it was not for them to understand.  Why? 
What the words were saying were bad for them, they could not accept what was going to
happen to Jesus.
\tst Tst2:  This was retold; however, it was retold out of order by stating, "This was hidden
from them.  The students did not understand."
\tst Tst3:  He omitted this line from retelling.  For simplicity and to remove confusion as to
why the words are "hidden from them", this line can be restated, "Jesus' disciples did not
understand his words."  Revised.
\ln 40.07
\bt And Jesus and his disciples were going to another village.  There was
a blind man.  He was sitting near the road begging {KT: pray} people.
\old And Jesus and his disciples were going to another village.  On their way, when they
reached the road, they have found a blind man sitting near the road begging {KT: pray}
people.
\anc luk.18:35
\tst Tst3:  Why were they going to another village?  Because it was Jesus' village - that is
where they came from.  
\tst Tst3:  Why would the blind man be beside the road?  He could not see - so he was sitting
next to the road begging for things.  He could not work, so he sat by the road asking for
money.
\tst Tst3:  How did they "find" the blind man?  Because the man was yelling "Jesus of David's
offspring, have pity on me."  He was yelling so Jesus had him brought to him.  Where did
they find him?  He was sitting by the road.
\tst Tst3:  In both retellings, this line is simplified as "There was a blind man sitting beside
the road begging people."  This introduction can be simplified as such.  The verb "they
found" is not retold.  Revised.
\ln 40.08
\bt When he hears people noise, he asked, "Why people are making
noise?"  
\anc luk.18:36
\tst Tst3:  Why did the blind man ask about the noise?  Because he could not see and he
wanted to know what was the noise of the people.
\tst Tst3:  Why are the people making noise?  Because they were all coming to Jesus, their
feet were walking and making the noise of them coming.
\tst Tst2:  In the retelling, they say the blind man asks, "Who's that?"
\tst Tst3:  In the retelling, he keeps the line as the original.  It can remain the same.    
\ln 40.09
\bt They said, "It's Jesus who is passing."
\anc luk.18:37
\tst Tst2:  In the retelling, they said, "It's Jesus voice.  Jesus is passing."
\tst Tst3:  Retold as is.  Will remain as is.  
\ln 40.10
\bt So the blind man shouted, "Jesus of David's offspring people, have
pity on me."
\old So the blind man rose up and shouted, "Jesus of David's offspring's people, give me back
my eyes [MM: Have pity on me.]."
\anc luk.18:38
\cn MM:  The phrase here, originally back translated as "give me back my eyes" is the exact
phrase used in the Supyire translation for "Have pity on me".  It sounds a lot like "give
me my eyes" in Supyire.  However, upon further testing and explanation, it does indeed
mean "Have pity on me."
\tst Why does the blind man shout this?  He knows Jesus is strong and can heal him.  Why
does he call Jesus, 'Jesus of David's offsprings people'?  Because David and Jesus are
from the same group of people.
\tst Tst3:  Why did the blind man rise up and shout?  Because he was calling out to Jesus of
David's offspring to come to him and to open his eyes.  Why did he rise?  Because he
wants Jesus to hear and understand what hs is asking him.  You can sit and yell but your
words will not go far.  You have to stand to be heard - when you stand, your words go
further and people hear you.  He could sit, but he wanted Jesus to hear him and have
pity on him.
\tst Tst3:  Why does he call Jesus, David's offspring people?  Because the Savior was going
to come from David's offspring people, so Jesus was from David's Offspring people.
\tst Tst3:  Why does he ask for pity?  Because he knew that he had nothing and that Jesus
had the medicine that could give him his eyes.  What is Jesus' medicine?  Jesus can say
it and open his eyes.  Jesus says it and he can see.
\tst Tst2:  In the retelling, they leave out the "rose up".  This can be cut from the story.  One
person said the blind man said, "Open my eyes."  The other one corrected her and said,
"Have pity on me."  They did include the "Jesus of David's offspring's people" in the
retelling.
\tst Tst3:  Retold again without the "rose up".  Will be deleted based on line of questioning
and misrepresentation of scripture.  Otherwise, line is retold as original.  Revised.
\ln 40.11
\bt At the {moment} he said that, the people told him "Be silent."  
\old At the moment he said that, some people became sad.  They asked him to be silent.
\anc luk.18:39
\tst Why did they want the blind man to be quiet?  They didn't want him to stop Jesus. 
Maybe they didn't want the blind man to see again.  Maybe they just didn't like Jesus.  ??
\tst Tst3:  Why did the people become sad?  They are not "sad", but what the blind man has
done is not good for them.  They are this man's enemy because they do not want his
eyes opened.
\tst Tst3:  Why did they tell the man to be silent?  Because they are bad and they don't want
Jesus to help the man by opening his eyes.  They are afraid if Jesus opens his eyes
Jesus will leave and they don't want that.
\tst Tst3:  What did they see and hear for them to become sad?  They heard the blind man
yelling to Jesus, for Jesus to have pity on him, but that was bad for them.  They didn't
want his eyes opened so they told him to be quiet.
\tst Tst2:  In the retelling, they stated, "It was not good for them and they said to be
silent."  
\tst Tst3: Line was retold as is.  However, based on questioning and the emphasis on their
thinking that the people were this man's enemies and did not want him healed, this part
will be cut, and left simply as "the people asked him to be silent."
\ln 40.12
\bt He shouted again [MM: with {power}], "Jesus of David's offspring's
people, give me back my eyes [MM:  Havy pity on me]."
\anc luk.18:39
\tst Tst3:  Why did he shout again?  Because he did not accept what they were saying, to be
quiet, he just shouted louder because he wanted Jesus to have pity on him and opn his
eyes.
\ln 40.13
\bt So Jesus stopped and asked them to bring him.  
\anc luk.18:40
\tst Tst3:  Why did Jesus stop and have the blind man brought to him?  Because he heard his
shouting, so he stopped and had the man brought to him.  Why?  Because he had pity on
him.
\tst Tst2:  In the retelling, they said, "And Jesus stopped and said, "You come to us."  And he
went to him."  This is perhaps performance error, but will be checked further.
\tst Tst3:  In retelling, he keeps the phrases as in the original.  
\ln 40.14a
\bt When they brought him near Jesus, Jesus asked him...
\anc luk.18:40
\ln 40.14b
\bt 'What do you want me to do for you?"
\anc luk.18:41 
\tst Tst3:  Why did Jesus ask the man, "What do you want me to do for you?"  Because Jesus
wanted him to say it - to say that he knew and believed.
\tst Tst2:  In the retelling, Jesus asked him , "You shouted to me, what will I do for you?"  
\tst Tst3:  This was retold as in the original.  This line will remain the same.  
\ln 40.15
\bt The blind man said, "I want to see."
\anc luk.18:41
\tst Tst3:  What does the blind man think Jesus can do for him?  He thinks Jesus can open his
eyes.  He thinks Jesus can because Jesus is the Savior and Jesus can save the man from
his blindness.
\tst Tst3:  Why does he want to see?  So he can see everything around him.  So he can work
and eat and not have to sit by the road and beg for help.
\ln 40.16
\bt Jesus said, "See."  His eyes opened and he saw.
\old Jesus said, "See."  His eyes opened.
\anc luk.18:42 - 43
\tst How does Jesus heal the man?  He opened his eyes to see.  How?  God gave him power
to heal. 
\tst Tst3:  How were his eyes opened?  Jesus asked him what he wanted and the man said
he wanted to see.  So Jesus said, "See" and he could.  Jesus saved him.  Now he can
see and work and eat.  How do you think Jesus was able to do this? Jesus is God's Son -
he is the Savior.  So jesus just had to say it because he is God's Son.  All he did was say
it, he put the blessing on the blind man and he could see.  Jesus could say "See", and
the man could, because he is Jesus.
\tst Tst3:  While in tst2 this line was retold as is.  In this testing retelling, he said, "Jesus said
'See.' And he saw."  May be best to make this explicit and phrase as "His eyes opened
and he could see."  Revised.
\ln 40.17
\bt And Jesus said, "God healed you.  Why?  Because you trusted {KT:
trust} me."
\anc luk.18:42
\tst Why did Jesus heal this man?  Because Jesus knew that the man has faith in him.
\tst Tst3:  Why did God heal him?  So that the man would not have to sit by the road and
ask.  So that he could work and eat on his own.
\tst Tst3:  Why did Jesus say this?  Because the man trusted Jesus and asked him for pity
and can now see.  Because the man believed enough to ask Jesus.
\tst Ts3:  Why did the man trust Jesus?  Because he knew that Jesus is the Savior.  The man
trusted Jesus because he heard the Savior was coming and was Jesus.  So Jesus saved
him.
\tst Tst2:  The second half of this line was omitted.  Check further testings.  
\tst Tst3:  This line was retold as is, including the "Because you trusted me." And will not
require changes.  
\ln 40.18
\bt So the blind man followed Jesus and praised {KT: praise} God.  And all
the people praised God.  
\anc luk.18:43
\tst Tst3:  How could the blind man follow Jesus?  He can see now.  He followed Jesus
because he wanted to.  It was good for him, because Jesus had opened his eyes.
\tst Tst3:  Why did the blind man follow?  Because he believed in Jesus.  Jesus had opened
his eyes.  So, now he wants to follow him because Jesus is the medicine for you when
you believe in him.
\tst Tst3:  Why did he praise God?  Because of the thing that he did.  His eyes were opened. 
He could see now.  They praised God because they feared him.  He is their boss.
\tst Tst3:  Why did all the people praise God?  Because God is the one who did it.  Jesus is
God's Son.  God helped Jesus to do it.  So they praised him.
\tst Tst2:  This line was retold exactly as is.  
\p
\p Further Testing Questions from Original Testing Group:
\tst What do you like about the story?  Jesus healed the man. 
\tst What do you not like about the story?  When the man called out to Jesus and the crowds
were trying to quiet him. 
\tst What does the story tell you about God's character?  God is strong.  He can heal.
\tst What does the story tell you about Jesus?  Jesus is God's Son, He is truth.  
\dt 01/Jan/2009

\c 42
\t Triumphal Entry 
\co Supyire
\co
\co Redemptive Theme:  Jesus states that he has come to provide a good relationship
between people  and God.  It is through belief in him that this good relationship can
come about.  This story draws out the power of Jesus as he is viewed as a king and
has the power to provide peace.
\co Cohesion / Background:  Introduces the place of Jerusalem, cohesively presents
Jesus as King, continues to build on the plot by the religious leaders to kill Jesus. 
Continues to build the consequence of not believing in Jesus, the enemy will have
victory over them.
\p

\co Story Backtranslator:  BK

de Vie, and Bambara Bible

the people and disciples put clothes on the donkey and before Jesus when he road on it. 
It was good that they worshiped him.  But they do not like/ it is hard for them when
Jesus cried over the city and that some want to kill him.

\ln 42.05

\ln 42.06
\bt If the owner asks, tell them the {Master} needs it.
\old If the owner ask them, what are you doing?  Tell them, "the {Master} needs it."
\anc luk.19:31
\cn MM:  The Supyire word for "Lord" is only used in Christian context and does not have
much meaning outside of Christian circles.  Therefore, instead of using the word for
"Lord" here, we have gone with a more generic term that means "Master or Teacher"."
\tst Tst2:  Why would the owner ask them what they are doing?  Because it was his donkey
and he wanted to know what they were going to do with it.  Why did he let them? 
Because they told him it was for the Lord, it was for Jesus.  When they told him they had
been sent for it, he let thim go.
\tst Tst2:  Why would Jesus need a young donkey?  Because it is good for him to ride it into
Jerusalem.  Jesus is going to ride on it and they can put their things on it.
\tst Tst3:  In her retelling, she said, "The Teacher needs it."  And does not use the word for
"Lord" here.  
\tst Tst2:  In his retelling, he uses the word "Lord".  Here, in this context, the word for "Lord"
simply means "Master".  Here in Supyire, this word means Master, similar to chief.  In
this context, the word "Lord" can remain in the story as it is not the same as "Christ, or
'Lord Jesus' or Lord God Almighty."

\ln 42.12

\ln 42.16

\tst In talking about the "stones shouting out" in testing their was a bit of discussion, why and

people had to shout about Jesus, because even here in the thickest of traditional religion
they had not heard of stones shouting before.
\tst Tst2:  How can stones shout?  When people aren't shouting, the stones can make the

\tst Tst2:  Why would the stones shout?  Because Jesus said if the people don't shout out, the

\tst Tst2:  Why would Jesus cry for the city?  Jesus was crying for Jerusalem because they
were broken and his heart was raised for them, like when you want something and it is
broken - you cry for it.
\ln 42.19

\tst Tst2:  How could they have peace?  They cannot because they refused it, they refused

\tst Tst2:  How did God come to help them?  God sent Jesus to give them his words - when

you and God.  But you did not believe in me."  This also emphasizes the relationship

\dt 01/Jan/2009

\c 44
\t Last Supper
\co Supyire
\p
\co Redemptive Theme:  The story shows that through Jesus' death, a new relationship
can be found between man and God.  It is through belief in Jesus that one can be
saved and have a good relationship with God.
\co Basic Biblical concepts : Introduces Lord's Supper in remembrance of Jesus, Jesus
died for our sins.      
\co Cohesion / Background:  Transitions from previous story as Jesus and his disciples
arrive at Jerusalem.  Cohesively builds on the plot to kill Jesus, introduces Satan as
God's enemy.  Continues to show that the upcoming death of Jesus is God's plan to
restore man's relationship with Him, preplanned by God, accepted willingly by Jesus.
\p
\co Story crafter's name or initials: SS
\co Backtranslator's name or initials:  BK
\p
\co Resources Used in Crafting Session:  Audio of French Bible - Parole de Vie, Bambara
Bible, Supyire NT draft
\p
\tst General Testing Comments:  It seems clear in testing the portions of the story regarding
the betrayal of Jesus and why Judas is betraying him.  It is clear the example of servant
leadership that Jesus sets.  However, it seems somewhat unclear the connection
between the bread and Jesus' body, the drink and Jesus' blood and God's new covenant. 
These are difficult concepts and do not seem well understood in the first testing session. 
The connection between Jesus' upcoming death on the cross and this last supper do not
seem to be made.  Any advice you may have, and how to anchor it, would be
appreciated.  Also, the story is long, making retelling difficult.
\p
\co Revised 7/7/08
\p
\co This story has been revised.  The plot has been developed further, adding details to
the plot of Judas' to kill Jesus.  The teaching section of the story, the washing of the
disciples feet, has been removed to shorten the story and increase it's re-tellability. 
The story flows and concentrates more on the plot to kill Jesus, His willingness and
knowledge of his upcoming death, and the significance of his death for everyone. 
Overall, the story flows better and ties better into the next story.
\p
\co Audio Last Revised:  20Oct08
\co BT File Last Revised:  21Oct08
\p

\tst Tst3:  Friend at phone booth.  Tested for retellability only.  
\tst Tst2 (Retest):  Tested again after final changes had been made.  Tested also for
reproducibility with changes.  See comments below.
\p

\ln 44.01

\ln 44.02
\bt {Why}?  Because a feast of Abraham's offspring people was coming.
\anc luk.22:01
\cn BK:  The word here for "feast" implies ceremony, celebration.  The word for "coming"
means that it was happening in the near future.
\tst Why was the village crowded with people?  Abraham's descendants were having a fete
(celebration).  
\ln 44.02b
\bt Jesus was saying God's words everyday outside God's praying
{house}.
\old Jesus was saying God's words everyday in the big church yard.

give God's Words to the people everyday.
\ln 44.03
\bt But the {leaders} of God's praying house were looking for a reason to
kill Jesus secretly , but they did not succeed.
\old But the leaders of God's praying {house} and the chief of God's praying big house
guardians were looking for a reason to kill Jesus secretly , but they did not succeed.
\anc luk.22:02 
\cn BK:  "Looking for a reason" means they were seeking for a motive to "kill him".  
\tst What do you think the religious leaders doing?  They wanted to take Jesus - we can't
know why, but many of these people want Jesus to die without others knowing.  It is
treason - kill because they don't like Jesus.
\tst Tst2:  Why did the people from God's praying house want to kill Jesus?  Because of the
words Jesus was teaching.  The people listened to Jesus' words a lot and this was not
good for them.
\tst Tst2:  How were they doing it secretly?  Because they wanted to kill Jesus and if they did
it for everybody to know, it would not be good for them because they don't want the
people to know so the people won't kill them.
\tst Tst2:  Why did they not succeed?  Because Jesus was good for all the people.  If they
were to kill Jesus, the people would kill them.
\ln 44.03b
\bt Why?  Because they were afraid of the people.  
\old Why?  Because everybody was listening to Jesus really.  Jesus was good for the people
{KT: love}.  
\old Why?  Because everybody was listening to Jesus really. 
\anc luk.19:48
\cn BK:  Here "really" is used to emphasize that the people were listening to Jesus with
intensity.  
\tst Why did the people listen to Jesus' words?  Because he is God's son, he is strong and
what he said was right.
\tst Tst3:  She retold this line as is.
\tst Tst2:  In retelling, he states "Why?  Because Jesus was good for the people" (in this case
"good for the people" means "loved by the people".  This would be a good natural phrase
here to explain further why they could not kill Jesus at this moment. Revised.
\ln 43.03c
\bt Everybody was listening to Jesus really.  Jesus was good for the
people.  
\old And they were also afraid of the people.

\tst Why were they afraid?  Because the whole world would beat them for Jesus.  
\tst Tst2:  Why were they afraid of the people?  Because they knew that Jesus is good for
the people.  If they kill Jesus, the people will want to come and kill them.
\tst Tst2 (Retest):  This line was not retold.  It may be an unnatural flow now.  This could be

\ln 44.04
\bt One day, God's {enemy} {Satan} entered Judas, Judas was one of
Jesus' disciples.  
\old One day, {Satan} entered Judas, Judas was one of Jesus' 12 disciples.  
\old One day, {Satan} entered Judas Iscariot, one of Jesus' 12 disciples.
\anc luk.22:03
\cn MM:  Final read through, showed the need to continue to unpack the concept of "Satan". 
Will say, "One day, Satan, God's enemy ..."
\tst Who is Judas?  One of Jesus' 12 disciples.  
\tst Tst2:  How did Satan enter Judas?  Because his head is not good.  He wanted to kill
Jesus like the people from God's praying house.  They wanted to kill Jesus.  Satan
entered Judas because of the badness he had in him.
\tst Tst2:  In retelling, he omits, "Iscariot, one of Jesus 12' disciples."
\tst Tst3:  In retelling, she states, "Judas, one of Jesus' 12 disciples."  There is no need to
state "Iscariot" here.  It is difficult to pronounce.  Revised.
\tst Tst2 (retest):  What do you think of when you hear "Satan"?  Satan wants to kill people
here.  When I hear Satan I think he wants to hurt, break, and kill people.  He wants you
to do bad things and not be right, not to do good things.  That is what I think when I hear
"Satan" here.
\tst Tst2 (retest):  Why did Satan enter Judas?  Satan entered Judas because Satan wants
Jesus delivered over to the enemies hands so he will be killed.  Satan knew the enemies
of Jesus wanted to kill him.  He also wanted to kill Jesus, so he entered Jesus.  Why?  So
Judas could put Jesus into their hands.
\ln 44.05
\bt So he went to agree {KT: accept} with the {leaders} of God's praying
big [MM: delete "big"] house to hand Jesus over to them.
\old So he went to agree {KT: accept} with the leaders of God's praying big house and the
chief of God's praying big house guardians to hand Jesus over.
\anc luk.22:04 , luk.22:06
\cn BK:  "to hand over" - An example would be to "hand over" a thief to the cops.
\tst Why did Judas want to kill Jesus?  Satan came on Judas.
\tst Tst2:  How did Judas know that the leaders of God's prayer house wanted to kill Jesus? 
Judas knew because he had heard them say how Jesus was not good for them.  He knew
this, but Jesus was not good for him too, so he could give Jesus to them and they would
give him money - that was good for Judas.
\tst Tst2:  Why would he hand over Jesus?  Because Jesus is not good for him.  Jesus was
his boss and the words and the things Jesus did were not good for him, so he could give
Jesus to them.
\tst Tst2:  In retelling, he omits "the chief of God's praying big house guardians" - these will
be summarized and left as "the leaders of God's praying house" for cohesive nature of
keyterms within story set.  Revised.
\ln 44.06
\bt They were very glad.  So they proposed him a sum of money.
\anc luk.22:05
\tst Who is "they"? The religious leaders. "Him"?  Judas.
\tst Tst2:  Why were they glad?  Because it was good for them to kill Jesus now.  
\tst Tst2:  Why would they give Judas money?  Because when you work for someone, you
pay them.  Judas was doing this for them, so they will give him his money.
\ln 44.06b
\bt From that day Judas was thinking about how to take Jesus to them.
\anc luk.22:06
\cn BK:  "Thinking" here is like "planning" how to take Jesus.  
\tst Tst2:  Why would Judas think how he can give them Jesus?  He thought all the time how
he could give Jesus to them and the thought about the money they had given him.  He
thought how he would take Jesus, like you take something from a person.
\tst Tst2 (retest):  Why was Judas thinking about how to take Jesus to them?  He was
thinking about how to take Jesus to them because he was Jesus' student.  Jesus was his
teacher.  He would be with Jesus.  When Satan entered him, and the enemies gave him
money to take Jesus to them, that is all that he thought about, how to take Jesus to
them.
\ln 44.07
\bt After that, Jesus and his disciples sat around the food.
\old After that, Jesus and his disciples sat around the food and started eating.  
\anc luk.22:14
\tst What happened next?  After that, Jesus and people began to eat - they are all around
(drew a circle on ground).
\tst Tst2:  Why would Jesus and his disciples sit around and eat?  Because they were one. 
They had been together, learning as one so they sat to eat as one.
\tst Tst:  Based on the misunderstanding that they had already started eating here, the can
be rephrased, to "After that, Jesus and his disciples sat around the food."  Revised.
\ln 44.08
\bt Then Jesus said, "I want to do this ceremony with you before I
suffer."  
\old Jesus said, ‚ÄúI decided inside myself,  to eat the food of this ceremony with you before I
suffer
\anc luk.22:15
\tst What do you think Jesus says here and why?  "I think when we finish eating, I will not be
happy."  He knows after he eats treason will happen.  Because he knows the treason is
getting ready to happen, they will take him.
\tst Tst2:  How did Jesus "decide inside" himself?  It was inside of him.  Like when you eat, it
goes inside of you.  Jesus decided - like how we said we were going to work.   You ask
me, and I said yes.  I accepted that you wanted to work, so after that Jesus decided
what they would do.
\tst Tst2:  How is this food for a ceremony?  Because when you have ceremonies or feasts,
you have food.  It's good for the people.
\tst Tst2:  Why will Jesus suffer?  Because the enemies will come for him and take him and
make him suffer and kill him.  
\tst Tst3:  In her retelling, she states, "I want to do this ceremony with you" This may be a
good simplification for the first part of the line.  Revised.

\anc jhn.13:15 , 17
\tst Referring to the entire "foot washing" section, why does Jesus do this?  It is like a
proverb of who works and who is in charge.  You know you are in charge, but you can
and you do the work of the workers.  Jesus says - me and you, no many different. 
Jesus gives this work - Jesus begins a work that is not finished - everybody is the same. 
Jesus washed their feet - why?  because they will not forget.
\ln 44.16

\ln 44.17

me."  
\old And said, "Eat this bread.  It's my flesh.  And remind yourself to me."
\anc luk.22:19
\cn BK:  Jesus did this because Jesus was about to suffer.  They would be reminded of him
from now on when they eat the bread.
\tst Why does Jesus do and say this?  Why does he say the bread is his flesh?  He wants his
students to all the time repeat and know and not forget.  Because if his flesh is bread,
then all the time they will eat it and not forget.
\tst Tst2:  How can this bread be Jesus' flesh?  Because Jesus was giving his life and flesh for
them.  So that when they eat his bread, they will remember Jesus.  They will eat the
bread and think of Jesus' flesh.  They will sweat and think of him.  How can this remind
people of Jesus?  Because if Jesus gives them bread - they ate and became full.  Jesus
gave them that bread - they cannot forget Jesus and all he will do for them.
\tst Tst2:  In retelling, he states, "Think of me."  Instead of "remind yourself to me." 
\tst Tst3:  In retelling, she states, "When you eat this, think about me."  This line can be
changed to "This bread is like my flesh, which I will give for you.  When you eat this,
think about me."   Revised.  Craftor stated it would not be understood to say "I give for
you".  He also felt it more appropriate to use the "remember me" phrase.  This was
retold in final retesting as is.
\ln 44.18
\bt Then he took water of fruit, and gave it to them.  And said for them to
drink it.  
\old And after that he took the cup, there was water of grapes in it, and gave it to his
disciples and said, "Drink this water of grape."  Grape is a tree which fruit [MM: fruit from
a tree] can be water.
\anc luk.22:20
\tst How can this phrase be explained?  A grape is fruit from a tree, small fruit you get the
water out of to drink.  It is good to say it like this because many people say Christians
drink beer and get drunk.  "Resin" (grape) is a word they won't know, but "fruit from a
tree" they will know.
\tst Tst2:  Why did Jesus give them the water of grapes to drink?  Because when you eat
things you have to drink something after.  Why grape water?  The grape water because
Jesus is going to die and give his blood for their bad things.  All of this is a part of the
sign of God's alliance with them.
\tst Tst2:  In retelilng, he states, "Then he gave them grape water and told them to drink it. 
The drink grape water is from a tree you drink the fruit of."
\tst Tst3:  In retelling, she states, "And gave them grape water to drink.  And said drink
this.  This is fruit water.  
\tst Tsts:  Based on retellings, this line is too complicated and unpacked for retelling.  It may
be best to simplify this to, "Then, he gave them fruit water to drink.  And said, "Drink
this fruit water. ..."  The word for "fruit" is something easily understood here.  There
seems to be no need to unpack the French word for "grape" here.  Revised.
\ln 44.19
\bt And said, "This water is like my blood.  I will die for your {sins}." 
\old And said, "If you drink that, remind yourself to God's new {alliance} that he links
because of my shed blood."
\anc luk.22:20, TN suggests "And he said, ‚ÄúThis cup of wine represents the new promise that
God gives to people which my life blood makes possible."  See also anchor for line 44.20.
\tst Tst2:  How can drinking that remind them of God's alliance?  Because Jesus told them so
that they could be one and they would not forget what Jesus was doing for them.
\tst Tst2:  In retelling, he simplifies this to, "God gave us this alliance, the grape water will
be my blood."   
\tst Tst3:  In retelling, she skips ahead to line 20 here.  She omits this line.   
\tst Tsts:  Based on lack of retellability, this line and line 20 could be restated as, "This is like
my blood.  I will die for your bad actions.  My blood will shed so that you can have life
forever.  When I die, God's new alliance with you begins.  That is, if you believe in me,
you will be saved.  There will be a good relationship between you and God."  This
unpacks it clearly, using cohesive terms and phrasing used throughout the story set. 
See additional anchoring here and in line 20 from TW. Revised.
\ln 44.20
\bt "When I die, God will place a new alliance [MM:  {relationship}]
between you and Him.  That is, if you {trust} in me, you will be saved
{KT: Savior}.  Then, there will be a good {relationship} between you
and God."
\old "The sign of God's new alliance is, "I, Jesus, will die in the name of your bad actions
{KT: sin}.  My blood will shed so that you can have life forever."
\anc luk.22:20 ,  TN suggests, "I am about to shed/lose it for your (plur) sakes."  TN also
states, " This new agreement or promise is that God will save all those who trust in Jesus
as the sacrifice for their sins (Romans 3:25)."
\tst MM:  Why they were drinking the water of grapes? BK:  Like Jesus' blood, the juice of
grape is red.  This would remind them of God's new alliance with them - the alliance is
Jesus' shed blood.
\tst What do you think is God's new covenant?  God's ceremony - God brings back Jesus
after death.  Alliance is like when you give a promise between people or villages. 
(covenant is same as promise).  Jesus will come back.  Why does Jesus say the drink is
to remind us of his blood?  So that you don't forget.  The drink is red, like his blood.
\tst Tst2:  Why is Jesus going to shed his blood?  Because Jesus is going to be killed for them
- so when they drink this , they will not forget that.
\tst Tst2:  Why will Jesus die in the name of their bad actions?  Because Jesus will accept all
the bad things of people.  He will save them from their bad things - he will die for them.
\tst Tst2:  How can Jesus' blood give life forever?  Because Jesus will be giving his blood for
theirs.  Jesus will be killed so they will not.  Jesus' blood is not like ours.  Jesus will come
back to life, so we won't die.
\tst Tst2:  How is this an alliance with God?  Because Jesus will die and will come back.  This
is a sign that is from God.  
\tst Tst2:  In retelling, he states, "I will die and rise from death.  My blood will shed to give
life forever to you."  
\tst Tst3:  She states this line as "I will die and rise.  I will die in the name of your bad
actions.  My blood will shed so that you can have life forever."
\tst Tst:  Based on testings and retellings, see proposed revision in line 19 above.    Revised.
\ln 44.21
\bt After that, Jesus said, "There is someone here with us who is going to
hand me over in the enemies' {KT: enemy} hands.
\anc luk.22:21 , TN suggests "Then Jesus said, ‚ÄúBut listen, the one who is about to deliver me
to my enemies ..."
\tst Tst2:  How did Jesus know someone will hand him over to the enemy?  He knew this
because when he was with them and teaching, he knew that they were not one - he and

Jesus.
\tst Tst2:  Why is this "someone" there with Jesus?  Judas was there with them because he
was looking for a way to give Jesus to the enemies - he was there with the disciples
because he was one of the 12, but he was there watching.
\ln 44.22
\bt God decided that [MM:  I will be killed], but the one who is going to do
this bad action {KT: sin} to me, it is finished for him.
\anc luk.22:22 , TN suggests "I, the man from God, will die. God has already decided that."

\tst Why does Jesus say that "God decided that I will be killed"?  Jesus says, "God proposes I

God is strong.
\tst What will happen to this enemy who hands Jesus over?  He is going to be broken.  
\tst Tst2:  Why did God decide to kill Jesus?  Because Jesus is his Son.  When he dies, he will
go and be with God again.  God sent Jesus as the Savior.
\tst Tst2:  How is it finished for the one who does the bad action?  Because he is broken and
he is not coming back to Jesus.  He is gone from them.  His insides are broken.  He will
suffer and be gone.  God will let him be this way.
\tst Tst2:  In retelling, he omits "God decided that I will be killed."  Also in retelling, instead
of stating "the one who is going to do this bad action to me", he states, "the one who will
give me to the enemies hands...".
\tst Tst3:  She does include "God decided that I will be killed."  She also keeps the original
phrasing of "the one who is going to do this bad action to me ..."  This line will remain as
is in the story.
\ln 44.23

\anc luk.22:23
\tst Tst2:  Why did the disciples ask themselves who could accept to do this bad action? 
Because they didn't believe it was possible for one of them to do this to Jesus.
\tst Tst2:  How could a disciple of Jesus want to do this bad thing against him?  Because

he cannot.  He is finished/broken.
\tst Tst2 and Tst3: In retelling, this was retold as original.

\anc mat.26:30

\cn MM:  This story is long and has been shortened.   This last sentence does not flow well

\dt 01/Jan/2009

\c 46
\t Judas' Betrayal 
\co Supyire
\p
\co Redemptive Theme:  While the enemy Satan is against Jesus, he has no power over
him.  Jesus is the more powerful victor.
\co Basic Biblical concepts :  Power of prayer, Jesus is handed over to be killed , Jesus
willingly accepted his upcoming death
\co Cohesion / Background:  Story continues with the day of the "fete", continues to
build on Jesus' foreknowledge of his upcoming death, builds on the relationship
between Father and Son, Jesus.  The religious leader's plot to kill Jesus continues as
they have come to take him.  The understanding of the enemy "Satan" is expanded
by referring to him as the "owner of darkness".
\co Worldview/Selection:  Again, as power is sought after through many different means
within Supyire culture, the power of prayer to "win the enemy" is seen within the
story.
\p
\co Story Craftor:  SS
\co Story Backtranslator:  BK
\p
\co Resources used in crafting:  Audio versions of Supyire NT draft, French Bible - Parole
de Vie, and Bambara Bible
\p
\co Audio Last Edited: 20Oct08
\co BT File Last Edited:  21Oct08
\p
\co MM:  After original testing and document submittal, this story has been revised. 
Much of the first portion of this story has been included in Story 44, "The Last
Supper" to maintain chronological events.  The revised story was then tested with
Tst3, and Tst4.  See comments within BT file.
\p
\tst Tst:  Original Testing Done in Village, 
\tst Tst2:  Nearby village with group of men.  Mostly tested for comprehension and
retellability.  Story has been shortened since then.
\tst Tst3:  Day Guard.
\tst Tst4:  Friend at phone booth.  Tested retellability only.  
\p

\tst Tst3:  Why was Jesus teaching his students?  He was teaching them God's words so they

\tst Tst3:  Why did Jesus tell them he was leaving?  He said that he is going and coming

\ln 46.19

\anc luk.22:40 , mrk.14:32

\tst Tst4:  In retelling, she gets off-path and talks about them praying together, but then
