\ln 46.20
\bt So that {Satan} cannot gain you."
\anc luk.22:40
\cn MM:  Here, the word "gain" means to "win" or "defeat".  
\tst Why did Jesus tell them to pray?  To keep Satan from coming onto them.
\tst Tst3:  How could Satan gain them?  Because Satan is coming to take Jesus - Satan
wants to have power over them and take them like he takes Jesus away.  What did he
do?  He does the things that are not good for God, things against God, like that the
enemies will come and take Jesus and beat him.
\ln 46.21
\bt He left and went a little further to pray.  
\old He left them and went a little further to pray.  
\anc luk.22:41
\tst Tst3:  Why did Jesus leave them and go a little further?  Because he was going to pray
to God.  He was praying that his own will would not be done, but God's will.  He went to
pray.
\ln 46.22
\bt He said, "My Father God, I beg {KT: pray} you to take this danger far
from me.  But I don't want my {will} to happen, but yours."
\old He said, "Almighty, I beg {KT: pray} you to take this danger far from me.  But I don't
want my {will} to happen, but yours."
\anc luk.22:42
\tst Why did Jesus pray?  He wanted to do the things that he did not likes and not what he
likes.
\tst Tst3:  Why did he pray for the danger to go far from him?  Because his suffering is
coming.  They will take him and beat him.  He prays for that danger to go far from him
because God can save him.  God is his Father.  He is big - he created the entire world -
God can save him.
\tst Tst3:  Why does Jesus not want his own will to happen?  Because God is His Father.  He
is the boss/chief.  He is praying for his will to happen.  God said he would suffer, so he
will suffer.
\tst Tst3:  In retelling, he omits the first sentence of the prayer and states, "I don't want my
will to happen, but God's."
\tst Tst4:  In retelling, she does include all of this prayer, but rewords the end to "I want
your will to happen, not mine."  There are many ways to express this, and all are very
similar to original story.  It will be left as is.
\ln 46.23
\bt After that, one of God's {angels} came and gave him strength {KT:
power}.  
\old After that one of God's {angels} was with him to encourage him.
\anc luk.22:43 
\tst Tst3:  Why did God's angel come?  To give courage to Jesus.  Jesus had been praying to
God.  He had been praying with his heart raised.  So God sent the angel to give him
courage.
\tst Tst3:  How did the angel give courage to Jesus?  He was there because Jesus was tired
and praying.  He would suffer, but the angel encouraged him by giving him power, God's
strength, he gave him.
\tst Tst4:  In retelling, she states God angels came to give him "strength" and does not say
"encouragement".  This would be a good change.  The word for strength is a very natural
word here and is often used as a blessing, "May God give you strength."  Revised.
\ln 46.24
\bt Then he prayed with strength.  
\old So with anger [KH: tension] he prayed.
\anc luk.22:44 , TN suggests "Then Jesus prayed even more strongly ..."
\tst How did Jesus feel?  "He was not happy.  His stomach hurt him.  Is he afraid?"
\tst Tst3:  How did Jesus pray with anger?  His heart/insides were raised.  Because the angel
gave him strength and power, he knew Satan was coming to take him and make him
suffer.  Why did he pray with anger?  Because he was praying for God to save him from
Satan.  Jesus was praying with anger - anger, you know, when you do not respond when
someone is talking to you or when you say you are going to beat someone and mean it. 
He did this so God would calm his heart.
\tst This line was retold.  However, based on testing questions and the possible interpretation
of this as "anger" instead of "tension", it will be revised to, "Jesus prayed with strength". 
Revised.
\ln 46.25

\ln 46.27

\ln 46.30

\ln 46.31

\ln 46.32

\tst Tst3:  Why did Jesus say "Stop."?  Because fighting was not good.  Jesus didn't want

\tst Tst3:  How did Jesus link his ear again?  Because Jesus prayed to God.  God did it.  Now

took the ear, and linked his ear again, and said, "Stop."

be changed.

\dt 01/Jan/2009

\c 48
\t Death of Jesus
\co Supyire
\p
\co Redemptive Theme:  Jesus has power to give people life above with God, to save
those who seek salvation from Him.
\co Basic Biblical concepts:  Jesus is handed over to be killed.  He is beaten and
crucified.  Dead and buried.  The story points to the consequences of sin are death
(as criminal points out), but points also to the forgiving power of God.
\co Cohesion / Background:  Relationship between Father and Son continues to be built. 
The time of "darkness" has arrived and is cohesively linked to the "owner of
darkness" in the story before thorugh the earth becoming "dark" here.  Isaiah
prophecy is fulfilled - Jesus is beaten and killed.  Cohesively draws out Jesus' status
as "King" and "Savior they were waiting for (Christ)".
\p   
\co Story Craftor:  SS
\co Story Backtranslator:  BK
\p
\co Resources used in crafting:  Audio versions of Supyire NT draft, French Bible - Parole
de Vie, and Bambara Bible
\p
\co Audio Last Revised:  20Oct08
\co BT File Last Revised:  21Oct08
\p
\tst Original testing = Our village with language helper and others.  
\tst Tst2: Testing group of men in Nir
\tst Tst3:  Day Guard.  He commented that this was a very good story.  One that he liked
and was easy to remember.  
\tst Tst4:  Phone booth friend.
\p
\ln 48.01
\bt This is something true that happened.
\anc 2Ti.03:16 , Psa.119:142 (New Century Version) "...your teachings are true";
Psa.119:160 (NIV) "all your words are true"; Jhn.17:17 "your word is truth".
\ln 48.02
\bt Early in the morning, the {leaders} of God's praying {house} and the
elders of the village agree {KT:  accept} to kill Jesus.
\anc Mat.27:01
\tst tst2:  Who wanted to kill Jesus?  Why?  The religious leaders - because they were
jealous.  An example of jealousy:  I want your motorcycle helmet, but I can't have it, so
I will break it so you can't use it.
\tst Tst3:  How do we know it was early in the morning?  Early in the morning, because that
was the day they were going to kill Jesus - early because the day had just started.  They
were going to kill Jesus because of his words.
\tst Tst3:  Why did they agree to kill Jesus?  Because Jesus was saying God's words and
God's words were not good for them.  Because they were not on God's road and were
the enemies.
\tst Tst3:  How did they agree?  Because the people from God's praying house went to the
elders because of the words Jesus kept saying.  They were all not on God's road so they
agreed to kill him because of what the people from God's praying house were saying.
\ln 48.03
\bt They attached him and brought him to the ruler, Pilate.  They arrived
in front of Pilate,   
\old They attached him and brought him to the chief [MM: ruler].  Pilate was the chief [MM:
ruler] of the country.
\anc Mat.27:02
\cn MM:  The phrase here "attach" means that they tied him with rope.  
\tst Who is Pilate?  He is the boss in charge.
\tst Tst3:  Why did they bring him to Pilate?  Because they wanted to kill Jesus and they
needed Pilate to say yes.  They wanted Pilate to say Yes, if he says yes, they will kill
Jesus.
\ln 48.04
\bt And said, "We have found this man leading these people on the bad
way, that he is the {king}."
\old And said, "We have found this man leading these people on the bad way, that he is
God's Chosen One, [MM: and that he is the {king}]."
\anc Luk.23:02
\cn BK:  "to put people on a bad way" means to lead them to revolt. 
\tst Why did the people decide to kill Jesus?  Because they said the words Jesus was
speaking was no good.  They didn't like it.  Who decided to kill Jesus?  Pilate.  Further
testing needed here - is this the answer simply because he was the leader in charge and
all decision go through him or is it clear that it is the religious leaders that have taken
him to Pilate and they are the ones wanting Jesus killed.
\tst Tst3:  How could Jesus have led people in a bad way?  They said that the words that
Jesus was teaching, God's Words, were leading them in a bad way - but the people of
God's praying house didn't know God's Words because Jesus was saying God's Words
and they didn't know they were true and said it was the bad way.
\tst Tst3:  How did Jesus say that he is God's Chosen One and King?  Because Jesus was
teaching the people and said that he was king, but these words were not good for the
people of God's praying house.
\ln 48.05
\bt And Pilate asked him, "Jesus, did you say that you are the King?"
\anc Luk.23:03
\tst Tst3:  Why would Pilate ask him this?  Because Pilate thought that their words were
lying.  He wanted to know if they were true.
\tst Tst3:  In retelling, he simplifies Pilates question to , "Jesus, are you the king?"  
\tst Tst4:  In her retelling, she states it as in the original.  This does not need changing.  
\ln 48.06
\bt Jesus answered, "If you say that.  My kingdom {KT: throne} is not in
this {world}."
\anc Luk.23:03 , Jhn.18:36
\cn BK:  The phrase, "If you say that" means "If that's what you say, then that is the truth." 
i.e. "If you say I'm a king, I'm a king."
\tst How does Jesus respond?  Pilate asked, "You are a king?"  Jesus answered, "What you
say is."
\tst tst2:  Why does Jesus say "If you say that."?  Jesus says he is a king.  If the country's
king says he is, he is.   
\tst tst2:  Why does Jesus say, "My kingdom is not in this world"?  Jesus kingdom - when we
die, we go to....  Where is Jesus' Kingdom?  It's beside/in front of God.  (Basically
meaning Jesus' kingdom is with God.)
\tst Tst3:  How is Jesus' kingdom not in this world?  Because of the things - good and bad -
that we do here.  When we do these things and we die, is when we go to Jesus'
kingdom.  Where?  With God.  When we do good things and walk on God's road, when
we die we will go and be with God - at God's house - his kingdom.  It's not here.
\ln 48.07a
\bt Then Pilate said to the leaders of God's praying house and the elders
of the country...
\old Then Pilate gathered the chiefs of God's praying house and the chief of the country
together 
\anc luk.23:13
\tst Tst3:  Why did Pilate gather them?  Because he wanted to ask them about killing Jesus
but they said Jesus should be killed.
\tst Tst3:  This line was omitted in retelling.   
\tst Tst4:  This line was omitted at first, but after pausing, retold and continued in the story. 
The sequence of events seems unclear here.  Rather than going into more detail and
unpacking this, we will rephrase the line to simply state, "Then Pilate said to the leaders
of God's praying house and the elders of the country..."
\ln 48.07b
\bt "You say this man is making people revolt.  But I do not find him
guilty. "
\old and said, "You brought this man to me by saying that he is making people revolt, but I
asked him in front of all of you.  You say that he's guilty, but I didn't find that he
deserves to be killed."
\anc luk.23:14
\tst Tst3:  Why did they tell Pilate Jesus was making a revolt?  Because they wanted to kill
Jesus, they do not like these words he was telling the people.  So they said he was
leading a revolt against them, but he wasn't.
\tst Tst3:  Why do they say he is guilty?  Because they want him killed for the words that he
is saying.  He is saying God's words, they were not saying the truth about him because
they want him killed.
\tst Tst3:  Why does Pilate say he does not deserve to be killed?  Because Jesus had not
done anything wrong.  He had not done any bad things to be killed for.  They were not
saying the truth.
\tst Tst3:  In retelling, the line was simplified to, "Pilate said, 'Hey, you say he is guilty of
leading people in revolt, but I don't find that he is guilty and deserves to be killed."
\tst Tst4:  In retelling, she states the line as in original.  This phrase can be simplified to,
"You say this man is guilty of leading people in revolt, but I do not find him guilty." 
Revised.
\ln 48.08
\bt "In this case, I will hand him over to be beaten and release him. 
\old "In this case, I will hand him over to be beaten and release him.  {Why?} Because I
didn't find him guilty."
\anc luk.23:16 , luk.23:14
\tst tst2:  Why does Pilate want to let Jesus go?  He knows Jesus is a King and tells the
truth.  
\tst Tst3:  Why does Pilate say to beat him?  Because Pilate does not want to kill him so he
says to just beat him.  Then he can go because he doesn't want to kill him.   Why does
he want to let him go?  Because he was saying God's words.  He had been comissioned
to them.  If Jesus is killed, who will say God's words to the disciples?
\tst Tst3:  This last sentence of the line was not retold.  It is repetitive.
\tst Tst4:  Again, the last sentence was omitted.  It will be deleted.  Deleted.
\ln 48.09
\old Pilate understood that the chiefs of God's praying house handed-over Jesus by
selfishness.
\cn BK:  This means that Pilate knew that these men handed Jesus over because of their
own selfish reasons.  He's not guilty.
\anc Mrk.15:10
\tst In testing when asked what this term for "selfishness" means, they said it's the people
who don't like Jesus.  They wanted him dead, they were rejecting Jesus's words and
were trying to break his good name. (To break his name means to hurt his reputation
and damage the good that he has done and is doing.)
\tst Tst3:  How did Pilate understand that they handed Jesus over by selfishness?  Because
he knew that Jesus said God's Words and that the people from God's praying house
didn't say God's Words - they were selfish because they wanted to be that one, the one
who spoke God's Words, like Jesus, But they were the enemy because of their
selfishness.
\tst Tst3:  This line was omitted in retelling.
\tst Tst4:  This line was omitted in retelling.  This line appears to block natural story flow.  It
will be removed from the story.  Deleted.
\ln 48.10
\bt Many people gathered.  They shouted loudly, "Kill him.  Kill him."
\old They shouted by saying, "Kill him.  Kill him."
\old They shouted by saying, "Let us kill him.  Kill him."  
\anc luk.23:21
\tst Who is shouting here?  Pilates people who wanted Jesus dead.  This is true but still needs
more testing or editing to show that their was also a crowd who was shouting.
\tst Tst3:  Why did they shout?  Because Pilate just wanted to beat him and let him go, but
they wanted Jesus killed, so they shouted it so Pilate would accept.
\tst Tst3:  In retelling, he states, "The people shouted ...."  This should be cleared up.  Based
on questioning it is not clear who is shouting.  Should be unpacked to say, "A crowd of
people gathered.  They shouted ..."  Revised.
\ln 48.11
\bt Then Pilate said, "I ask, what did he do that deserves killing him?"  
\old Then Pilate asked them, "What did he do that deserves killing him?"
\old Then Pilate went back and asked them, "What did he do that deserves killing him?"
\anc luk.23:22
\tst Tst3:  Why did Pilate ask them what he did that deserves killing?  Because Pilate didn't
know anything that Jesus had done to be killed for.  He knew he had not done any bad
thing, but they wanted to kill Jesus, so he was asking them what he had done to be
killed.
\tst This will be simplified to "Pilate asked, 'What did he do that deserves killing him?'" 
Revised.
\ln 48.12
\bt And people were still shouting loudly, "Nail him on the wood.  Nail him
on the wood."
\anc luk.23:23
\tst How do you picture this happening?  They wanted to nail him to the tree.  This was acted
out by one of the test group participants.  ... Will this kill a person who is nailed to a
tree?  No, but after it will.  Did they want Jesus dead?  Yes.
\tst Tst3:  Why would they want Jesus nailed on wood?  Because when you are nailed to a
tree, it will kill you, you will die.  They wanted Jesus to die.
\ln 48.13
\bt So Pilate did what the people wanted [MM: did the {will} of the
people].
\old It was out of Pilate's control.  So Pilate did what the people wanted.  
\anc luk.23:23 -24
\cn BK:  Pilate did the people's will.
\tst tst2:  What does the phrase mean "It was out of Pilate's control."?  All the people wanted
Jesus dead.  Pilate didn't want to.  But it was Pilate only - he maybe thought if he let
Jesus go, they would kill him.  It was Pilate only - everyone else wanted him dead.  So
Pilate had to.
\tst Tst3:  How was it out of Pilate's control?  Because Pilate alone could not save Jesus.  He
had to do the people's will by killing him.
\tst Tst3:  Why did Pilate do what the people wanted?  Because the people were too many
for him - they all wanted him killed.
\tst Tst3:  The phrase "It was out of Pilate's control" was not retold.  
\tst Tst4:  The phrase "It was out of Pilate's control" was not retold.  It will be deleted. 
Deleted.
\ln 48.14
\bt So the soliders went with Jesus.
\old So the soldiers went with Jesus into the place they were sitting.  
\anc mrk.15:16
\tst Tst3:  Why did the soldiers go with Jesus?  Because they took him and beat him with a
whip, they put clothes on him and put a hat of thorns on his head, they mocked Jesus.
\tst Tst3:  In retelling, he did not state, "into the place they were sitting".  This can be
deleted.  Deleted.
\ln 48.15
\bt And they were mocking him.  {Why}?  Because people were calling
him a king.  They beat him and spit on him.
\old And the other soldiers appeared and clothed Jesus in red clothes.  So, they made a hat
of thorns and put it on Jesus' head.  They were beating him, spitting on him, and they
kneeled down near Jesus and mocked him as if they were respecting him.
\anc mrk.15:17 - 19
\anc TW, CONNOT anchor - "they were making fun of the fact that he was called king."
\tst Why were they mocking him in this way?  To punish him.  They did this because they
didn't like him.  Further testing is needed to see if the connection between Jesus as a
king and the way in which the soldiers are mocking him is understood.
\tst tst2:  Why did the soldiers do these things to Jesus?  They were mocking him.  Why did
they mock him like this?  It was explained - wearing clothes like this was for a VIP or
king.
\tst Tst3:  Why did the soldiers put red clothes on Jesus?  Because they knew he was going
to die, so they put the red clothes on him.  Beacuse they were beating him and he was
going to die.
\tst Tst3:  Why would they put a hat of thorns on his head?  To make holes in his head to
make him bleed.  
\tst Tst3:  Why would you spit on a person?  Because that person is not good for you,
because you don't like them.  When they are bad to you,  The soldiers spit on Jesus
because they knew the words he said and they were not good for them.
\tst Tst3:  Why did they kneel and mock him?  Because they were mocking him.  They knew
they were going to kill him.  They were mocking him because he was not good for them
- he and the words he said.  He was only good for his disciples - loved by his disciples
but not by them.
\tst Tst3:  In retelling, he does not state that they were mocking him "as if they were
respecting him."  He only states, "they mocked him."
\tst Tst4:  In retelling, she omits the hat of thorns.  
\tst Based on testing answers and retellings, the connection between the attire that the
soldiers were placing on Jesus and that of a king, is not clearly and easily made.   In an
already long story, this line can be simplified to, "The soldiers mocked Jesus, that he was
called a king.  They beat him and spit on him."    (See TW, CONNOT anchor - "they were
making fun of the fact that he was called king.")  Revised.
\ln 48.16a
\bt Then they went with Jesus to nail him.  
\old After that, they went with Jesus to nail him.  He was followed by two people who did bad
things.
\anc mrk.15:20   
\tst Tst3:  Why were they going to nail him?  Because they wanted him to die.  They took
him to the killing place to nail him on the tree.
\ln 48.16b
\bt They were taking two people who did bad things, along with Jesus, to
be killed.  
\anc luk.23:32 
\cn MM:  Original BT was not an accurate word-for-word backtranslation to English.  This
line, 16) has been updated.
\tst tst2:  Why were these two men "following" Jesus?  They were two men who did bad
things.  The authorities caught them and took them.  They were forced.
\tst Tst3:  Why were the two people who did bad things with him?  Because they had done
bad things, the things that they could be killed for - they were also going to be killed with
Jesus.
\ln 48.17
\bt When they arrived, they nailed Jesus and nailed the two person on
Jesus' sides, one on the right and the other on the left.
\anc luk.23:32 -33
\tst tst2:  What do you see?   What were these men nailed to?  Three trees.  Jesus on one
tree.  And each criminal on a tree, one on his right, one on his left.
\tst Tst3:  Why did they nail the other two persons?  Because they had done really bad
things - really bad, so they were going to kill them with Jesus.
\tst Tst3:  Why did they put one on the right and the other on the left?  They put the bad
ones on both Jesus' right and left but they were bad and Jesus was their Savior, he was
in the middle.
\ln 48.18
\bt Then Jesus said, "My Father God, {forgive} them.  They don't know
what they are doing."
\anc luk.23:34
\tst Tst3:  Why did Jesus pray that God would forgive them?  Because of all the bad things
they had done and were doing.  By nailing Jesus and the other 2 bad people to the
trees.  Who was Jesus praying for?  The soldiers, the 2 bad guys, all the people there so
that they could enter God's kingdom also.  Jesus was their Savior.
\tst Tst3:  How do they not know what they are doing?  Because they all thought they were
doing a good thing by killing Jesus, but they didn't know.  They thought they would be in
God's kingdom, but God will suffer them instead, but Jesus prayed God would forgive
them.
\tst Tst3:  This line was omitted in retelling.
\tst Tst4:  This line was misplaced chronologically in retelling.  It was as if she remembered
she left the line out and included it in the story below. (around Line 21).  Based on line of
questions, this phrase and wording is understood.  It will remain in the story set.  In final
recording, we will try to place emphasis on this.
\ln 48.19
\bt After that, they continued mocking Jesus by saying, "If you are the
Savior we are waiting for {KT: Christ}, get down from that wood."
\old After that, they continued mocking him by saying, "If you are the one chosen by God,
get down from that wood."
\tst tst2:  How do they mock Jesus?  With their words.  Why like this?  They are saying words
like they are respecting him - pretending to respect him.   Mixing up - Jesus says he's a
king, they mock him by pretending he is.
\tst Tst3:  Why did they continue mocking Jesus?  They mocked him saying, "If you're God's
Chosen get down from that tree."  Why?  Because they knew Jesus was going to die, so
they mocked him.
\tst Tst3:  Why do they tell Jesus to get down?  Because they didn't accept that he was God's
Chosen, that he could get himself down.  But they were telling him this because if he
would he could go.
\tst Tst3:  Do you think Jesus could get down?  He couldn't because he died, when he died
then they took him down.  He couldn't because he died and gave his spirit to God.
\anc luk.23:35
\ln 48.20
\bt So one of the men nailed with Jesus said, "If you are the Savior we are
waiting for, escape yourself and also escape us {KT: savior}."
\old So one of the men nailed with Jesus said, "If you are the one chosen by God, escape
yourself and also escape us."
\anc luk.23:39
\cn BK:  Here the phrase "escape" is used as a verb and means "to save"..   
\tst Why are the people and criminals saying these things to Jesus?  The criminals say, "If
you are a child of God, why do they punish you?"  They think Jesus can save them, if He
is God's Son.
\tst Do you think Jesus could get down and save himself if he wanted to?  Jesus could free
himself but wouldn't.  Why did he not? ...... ??
\tst tst2:  "If Jesus is God's Chosen One, why didn't He come down?"  He didn't come down. 
He gives his life for people. 
\tst Tst4:  In retelling, she states, "then, one of the bad persons (aka criminal) said .."  In
other retellings, this has been said as in the original.  This is simply another way to
phrase this, but does not necessitate change.
\ln 48.21
\bt And the other answered, "Hey you.  Are you not afraid of God?  We
deserve this suffering, but Jesus didn't do anything bad {KT: sin}."
\old And the other answered, "Hey you.  Are you not afraid of God?  We are the ones who
deserve this suffering.  Why? Because we looked for it.  But Jesus didn't do something
bad {KT: sin}."
\anc luk.23:40 -41 
\cn BK:  The concept of "deserving something" can be stated as "we looked for it".  It means
"they deserved their punishment."
\tst How does this criminal respond?  He says "Jesus didn't do anything bad.  We did."
\tst Tst3:  Why do they deserve their suffering?  Because of all the bad things they had
done.  
\tst Tst3:  How did they know Jesus did not do something bad?  Because he had heard about
Jesus.  He heard that Jesus spoke God's words and was on God's road.  He had his
disciples.  The 2nd knew this, he had not accepted Jesus words before this, but he knew
now.  He knew Jesus was God's Son.
\tst Tst3:  In retelling, he states, "We deserve this suffering.  We did our bad things, but
Jesus has not done any bad thing."  
\tst Tst4:  In retelling, she states, "Are you not afraid of God?  We are the ones who deserve
this suffering.  Jesus didn't do something bad."  Omitting the "Why?  Because we looked
for it." phrase.  This can be reworded, "We deserve this suffering, but Jesus didn't do
anything bad."  Revised.
\ln 48.22
\bt And said, "Jesus, [MM: I beg {KT: pray} you], when you are in your
kingdom {KT: throne}, don't forget me."
\anc luk.23:42
\tst tst2:  In this testing session, the dialogue between the criminals was retold and
understood.
\tst Tst3:  Why did he ask Jesus not to forget him?  Because he knew Jesus was going to go
and be with God.  He knew he had done bad things, but still asked Jesus so he could go
and be with God too.
\ln 48.23
\bt So Jesus answered, "I say to you, today you are going with me
{above} to God."  
\old So Jesus answered, "[MM: I say to you,]  you are going to be with me today in God's
kingdom."
\anc luk.23:43
\tst tst2:  Why does Jesus say this?  Because the criminal trusted him.  
\tst Tst3:  How can he be with Jesus that day in God's kingdom?  Because he had asked
Jesus, like when you pray to God, knowing you have done bad things, God will forgive. 
Jesus accepted this 2nd man's words.  He would be there with Jesus.
\ln 48.24
\bt When the sun was in the middle of its course, the whole country
became dark. 
\anc luk.23:44 - 45
\cn MM:  This is understood to be midday or noon, when the sun is on top of your head or in
the middle of its course.
\cn BK:  To "become dark" is being "like the night".
\tst Tst3: Why did the whole country become dark?  Because they had killed Jesus.  This was
not good for God.  God did this because of the bad things the entire country had done. 
They all said to kill Jesus.  They, the entire country, had done these bad things and now
they are in darkness.
\ln 48.25a
\bt Then Jesus cried out loudly, "My Father God, I give you my {spirit}. 
When he said that, he died.  
\old Then Jesus cried out, "My Father God, I give you my soul {KT: spirit} into your hands." 
When he said that, he died.
\anc luk.23:46
\cn BK:  Jesus "cried out", but not in a crying/weeping way, but with a loud shout.
\tst How can Jesus give his soul into his hands?  "In a litttle bit he will die."
\tst tst2:  Why does Jesus say this?  Because He trusted God.  He was going to be with Him.  
\tst Tst3:  Why does Jesus say this?  Because God was Jesus' Father.  He heard Jesus and
knew that he was coming.  Because your soul is your life.  Jesus laid his soul to God.
\tst Tst3:  In retelling, he states, "I give my soul to you."  The phrase "into your hands" was
not retold.  
\tst Tst4:  She retells the phrase as in the original.  However, based on other storying groups
and tst3, it seems more natural to state "I give you my soul."  This will be shortened. 
Revised.
\ln 48.25b
\bt And there was a man who took Jesus and put him into a blanket, and
took him to the grave.  
\anc mat.27:57 -60 
\cn MM:  In Supyire culture, after a person dies, the body is wrapped in a "blanket" - or
wrapped somewhat like a mummy in cotton strips.
\tst Tst3:  Why did the man put Jesus in a blanket and put him in a grave?  Because when
you die, they wrap you up in the grave clothes.  They put you in the grave because you
are dead.  The blanket - because that is what you do.  The body grows, so you have to
tie it up.
\ln 48.26
\bt This grave was made through a stone.  When he put the body in the
grave, he closed it with another big stone and went back.
\anc mat.27:60
\tst Tst3:  Why did he close the grave with a big stone?  So that the grave would be closed. 
And no other people could enter.  
\p
\co Further Testing Questions from Tst2:  
\tst tst2:  What part of the story do you like?  The part where Jesus says, "God forgive them
they don't know what they're doing."  Another said where Pilate says, "Are you a king?"
and Jesus says He is.  Another said, the part where Jesus forgives them.
\tst tst2:  What part of the story do you not like?  When they were jealous of Jesus.  When
they were yelling and mocking and nailing Jesus to the tree.
\tst tst2:  What does the story tell us about God?  We should respect God.  We will walk with
God.
\tst tst2:  What does the story tell us about Jesus?  Jesus is a VIP.  Jesus is big and should
be respected.  Jesus died for our sins.  Jesus says "I give my life/soul to you - God."

\dt 01/Jan/2009

\c 50
\t Resurrection
\co Supyire
\p
\co Redemptive Theme:  Jesus is more powerful than evil, as he rises from death
conquering death and sin.  There is forgiveness of sins for those who believe in
Jesus, leaving old roads behind and taking Jesus' road.
\co Basic Biblical concepts: Jesus rises from death and goes above to God.  Promise of
his future return.  Forgiveness of sin and repentence.
\co Cohesion / Background:  Cohesively links what Jesus said would happen in stories
38 - 46 with what happened - Jesus would suffer and die, but 3 days later rise
again.  Jesus would give his life, but take it back again.  Cohesively expresses
repentence in terms of leaving your old road and taking Jesus' road.  Introduces the
concept that by believing in Jesus, people can be given the power of God through His
Spirit.  Continues to call people to go and tell others about the power of Jesus.
\p
\co Story Craftor:  SS
\co Story Backtranslator:  BK 
\p
\co Resources used in crafting:  Audio version of French Parole de Vie, Senufo Supyire
NT draft, and Bambara Bible.
\p
\co Audio Last Revised:  20Oct08
\co BT File Last Revised:  21Oct08
\p
\tst Original Testing:  In our village with language helper and a few women.  
\tst Tst2:  In Nearby village with group of men.  
\tst Tst3:  Day Guard friend.
\tst Tst4:  Friend at phone booth.  Tested for retellability.  
\p
\tst Tst3 (retest):  Tested again for questions to be answered within ConNotes discussions.
\p
\ln 50.01
\bt This is something true that happened.
\anc 2Ti.03:16 , Psa.119:142 (New Century Version) "...your teachings are true";
Psa.119:160 (NIV) "all your words are true"; Jhn.17:17 "your word is truth".
\ln 50.02
\bt After Jesus' death, the first day of the week, some women were going
to the grave with good smelling oil to put on Jesus' body.
\old After Jesus' death, the first day of the week, some women were going to the grave with
good smelling oil.
\anc luk.24:01
\tst [Discussion comparing burial customs] ...we don't put oil on the body.  If it's an old
woman who dies, the women all play music for her.  We wrap the body in cloth and
dance the body to the grave.
\tst Tst2: Why were the women going to the grave?  They were going with good smelling oil
to put on the body because the smell is good.  They were going together.  We do that
here sometimes.
\tst Tst3:  Why would the women be going to the grave?  They were going to see Jesus'
body, but he wasn't there.  They wanted to see his body because he said he would come
back from death.  They didn't believe that and still wanted to see him.  He was their
savior.
\tst TSt3:  Why would they have good smelling oil?  When oil smells good you rub it on your
skin.  They were going to rub this good smelling oil on Jesus' body so he would smell
good.
\tst Tst3 (retest):  Why were the women going to the grave?  The women were going to the
grave to see Jesus' body.  They went to rub the good smelling oil on his body, so the
body would smell good.
\tst Tst3 (retest):  What do you think the women were thinking when they went to the
grave?  They thought that Jesus was there, that's why they went with the oil to put on his
body.
\tst Tst3 (retest):  Tell me more about why they went there?  They went to rub good smelling
oil on his body, so it would smell good and his body would not have a bad smell.
\tst Tst3 (retest):  Do you think they remembered what Jesus told them about 3 days after
his death?  They remembered this only after they went to see his body and he was not
there.  They were going to rub oil on his body.
\ln 50.03a
\bt When they arrived there, they found out the stone was rolled and the
grave was open.  
\anc luk.24:02
\tst Tst3:  Why was the stone rolled away?  When Jesus came back to life, he opened the
grave and pushed the stone away (testing respondent made large pushing motion),
because Jesus left that grave.
\ln 50.03b
\bt So they entered and looked, but Jesus' body was not there.  
\old So they entered.  When inside, they didn't find Jesus' body.
\anc luk.24:03
\cn MM: Comparing Supyire burial customs --  the bodies are simply buried in a hole that a
group of men dig into the ground.  
\tst How did the women entered the tomb? The women entered the tomb through the
opening that had been closed with a stone.
\tst When the women saw that Jesus' body wasn't there, what do you think they were
thinking?  Ah, they may have thought some people came and stole Jesus' body.  Does
that happen...?  Yes, a lot.  People come and dig up and open the tombs.
\tst Tst3:  Why did they enter in?  Because it was open.  They were looking for Jesus but he
was not there.
\tst Tst3:  Why did they not find Jesus' body?  Because he was raised from death.  They said
after 3 days he would rise back.  So after 3 days, he was back from death.  He left.  He
went to the disciples house.
\tst Tst3:  In retelling, he states, "So they entered.  And were looking to find Jesus' body.  
\tst Tst4:  In her retelling, she states, "So they entered, but Jesus was not there."  It seems
there are several ways to state this.  It seems the phrase "when inside" is unnecessary. 
It may be best expressed, "So they entered and looked, but Jesus' body was not there." 
Revised.
\ln 50.04
\bt While they were there, 2 people came and stood near them.  They
were white until they were shining.
\old And 2 people came and stood near them.  They were white until they were shining.
\anc luk.24:04
\tst Who appeared to these women?  They were two "people", but they were not "people"
like you and I.  Who do you think it was?  We think they were angels.  What does the
word "shiny" mean to you?  It is like the bright color, like something metal when in the
sun.
\tst Why were these people white until they were shining?  it was their clothing, white
clothing that shines like a metal pot in the sunlight
\tst Tst2:  Why were these people white until shining?  Who were these people?  They were
shining like a metal pot shines in the sun.  It's the clothes - not white like white people,
but white like white pants.  And shining like this metal pot.
\tst Tst3:  Why did two people come and stand near them?  Because they came to tell them
the truth, that Jesus had risen from the dead.  They were really shiny and told them that
Jesus was not there.  Why were they searching for the living among the dead?
\tst Tst3:  How were they white until they were shining?  They were so white until they were
shining.  They were white and shiny because they were all good.  They were God's
messengers - they are God's angels.
\tst Tst:  In both retellings, this was retold as is.  Confirming the "white until shining" is
reproducible.  
\ln 50.05a
\bt Then they asked them, "What are you looking for?  Why are you

\tst Tst3:  Why did they ask the women who they are looking for?  They asked because they

\ln 50.05b

\ln 50.06

\ln 50.07

\ln 50.08

\old "And they asked us why are we looking for the live among the dead?  He is not here.  He

\anc luk.24:05 - 10 , luk.24:23
\tst How did Jesus come back to life again?  (After a surprised pause) "Well God brought him

\tst Tst3:  Why did the women tell the disciples all that happened?  Because they wanted

\ln 50.09

\anc luk.24:12
\tst Tst3:  Why did Peter run to the grave?  Because he wanted to see this true thing that he
women had said.  He wanted to see that Jesus had come back from death.
\tst Tst3:  Why did he run and look?  To see if Jesus' body was laying there, but it was not.  
\tst Tst3:  Why did he return back to them?  So he could tell them that it was true, that they

\ln 50.10
\bt Then Jesus showed himself to them and greeted them.  
\old Then Jesus showed himself to them and said, "May God give you {peace}."  
\anc luk.24:36
\tst How does someone "showed himself" to them?  It is like if you enter a large crowd of
people who you don't know and you shout to introduce yourself, "I am _______.".  You
"show" yourself to them.
\tst Tst2:  Why does Jesus say "May God give you peace." ?  To give them peace.  Because
they were scared and he wanted to give them peace.  There hearts were good.
\tst Tst3:  How did Jesus show himself to them?  Because he was back from death and he
wanted them to know it.  He was back from death and he showed himself to them.  Him,
his hands, and feet, so that they could know that it was him, so that they could know
him.
\tst Tst3:  Why did Jesus say "May God give you peace"?  Because they knew him, they had
followed him and listened to his words - so he told them to have peace - to take their
peace.
\tst Tst:  In both retellings, the phrase, "May God give you peace" was stated as in the
original.  
\tst Tst:  This line has been revised.  This is not a culturally normal way of greeting someone
"May God give you peace.", but more of a "leaving" remark made by people.  Therefore,
it will be simplified to "and greeted them".
\ln 50.10b
\bt They were afraid.
\anc luk.24:37
\tst Why do you think they were afraid?  If someone came back from the dead and appeared
in front of you, we'd all be afraid very much.
\ln 50.11

\old And Jesus said, "Don‚Äôt you believe {KT: trust} that I should raise from death again?"
\old And Jesus said, "Why are you selfish come into your heart? "
\anc luk.24:38
\tst Why was it hard for Jesus' followers to believe that he was alive again?  Because they
saw him die and dead.  they were really astonished and scared, because he was dead.
\tst Tst3:  Why did Jesus say, "Don't you believe I should raise from death again?"  Because
he told them he would die and come back.  He had died and he wanted them to believe
him and his words - they were sitting with him!
\tst Tst3:  In retelling he omits this question of Jesus.  
\tst Tst4:  In retelling, she states, "And Jesus said, "Don't be afraid.  It's me."  She omits this

\ln 50.12
\bt " It is really me." Then Jesus showed them his hands and his feet.  "I

\anc luk.24:39
\cn KH: Originally, our backtranslator stated "ghost" as "spoiled body".  However, upon
further testing and probing others, this is the Supyire expression for the concept of
"ghost".  It is the expression used in the Supyire NT translation in this anchor vs for
"ghost".
\cn From testing respondent:  A "ghost" is said to be what happens to you when you die and
your "body is gone". The spirit is not dead.  It does not have arms or legs, it does not
have flesh and bone and cannot eat.  It is not a demon or an angel.
\tst Tst3:  Why does Jesus say, "It is not a spoiled body"?  Because he was dead.  When you
are dead you become like this - your body is gone , no flesh or bones because you are
dead.  They are scary.  Young people cannot see them because they are young, but old
men can see them.  Here at night.  They walk in the darkness.  Old men see them
because they can, when old men die they can become like this.
\tst Tst3:  How could they think Jesus is a spoiled body?  They did not know it was Jesus. 
They thought it could of been a body that had come.
\tst Tst4:  In retelling, she states "Don't be afraid.  It's me."  She then states line 13 before
concluding with "I am not a spoiled body.  Why?  Because a spoiled body has no flesh
and bones."
\tst Tst3:  In retelling he states, "Don't be afraid.  I am not a spoiled body.  Spoiled bodies
do not have flesh and bone." 
\tst Tst:  Based on retellings, Jesus' dialogue is a bit lengthy to be retold well.  It should be
simplified. Proposed simplification for lines 11 - 12, "And Jesus said, 'Don't be afraid.  It's
really me.'  He showed them his hands and my feet.  "I am not a spoiled body.  A
spoiled body has no flesh and no bone."  Revised.
\ln 50.13
\old After that, he showed them his hands and feet and said, "Give me something to eat."
\anc luk.24:40 , luk.24:41
\tst Tst2:  Why did Jesus show them his hands and his feet?  because they saw him die,
nailed to the cross, by his hands and his feet.
\tst Tst3:  Why does Jesus ask for something to eat?  Because he was hungry.  So he asked
for food and they gave him fish to eat.  Then he ate it.  Because when you suffer you
become hungry or if it had been a long time since he had eaten, you become hungry.
\tst Based on testing, it seems there is a possibility to misunderstand why Jesus is asking for
fish.  Could he simply be hungry?  Also, for shortening the story, the part about the fish
can be deleted.  Deleted.
\ln 50.14
\old They gave him burned fish that he ate.
\anc luk.24:42 -43
\cn BK:  Here  "burned" fish is a fish that is prepared over an open flame - almost grilled. 
This is a common way to prepare fish.
\tst In testing we asked about the way this fish is prepared.  They understood and explained
that it was grilled over an open flame.  It's good.
\tst Tst2:  Why did Jesus ask them for something to eat?  to show them that he was real,
they were scared.
\ln 50.15
\bt "I told you, God's words said that the Savior you are waiting for {KT:
Christ}, he would suffer and die ...
\old And he said again, "It is said in God's book that his Son should suffer and die."
\old And he said again, "It is said in God's book that his Son should be handed over to the
criminals hands to suffer and die."
\anc luk.24:44 , luk.24:46
\tst Tst2:  Why does Jesus say this?  So they will believe in God and learn His book.  God's
words are true.    
\tst Tst3:  Why does it say in God's book that His Son will suffer and die?  It said God's Son
would suffer and die.  Jesus did.  He suffered and died.  But, he also came back from
death, because if he died, people could go to God's kingdom.
\tst Tst3:  How will God's Son suffer and die?  They caught him, they put clothes on him, a
thorn hat on his head.  They beat him with whips and spat on him.  He suffered.  Then
they nailed him to a tree to die.
\tst Tst3:  In retelling, it was stated, "And he said, "God's son had to come and suffer and
die."
\tst Tst4:  In retelling, she states, "God's Words say that His Son would suffer and die, but
rise three days after.    
\tst Tst:  Proposed line revision for lines 15 and 16, "I told you that God's words said that the
Savior you were waiting for {KT: Christ} would suffer and die and three days later rise
from death.  I am that one."  Revised.   In retesting, Tst3 (retest), this new revised line
was retold.
\ln 50.16
\bt and three days later rise from death.  I am that one."
\old "After his death he should come back to life 3 days later."  
\anc luk.24:46
\tst Why did this have to happen to Jesus?  so that the people could believe and learn and
use God's words
\tst Tst3:  How could he come back to life 3 days later?  God did it.  God is His Father, so
God did it.  He brought Jesus back to life after 3 days because it was good for him to do
it after 3 days.
\tst Tst3:  In retelling, this was omitted. 
\tst Tst4:  In retelling, she states this, "but rise three days after."  Revised.
\ln 50.17
\bt Many days later, Jesus came to them again.  He said to them, "You
have seen me suffer, die, and rise from death.  Now, go all over the
{world} and tell people to leave their {road} and take my road.  Then,
God will {forgive} their {sin}."
\old When Jesus said that he asked people to go and tell that all over the {world}.  That they
should change their behavior.  When they do that, God will {forgive} their {sins}.
\anc luk.24:47 - 48,  act.01:08, TN "You (plur) have seen me suffer, and die, and become
alive again. So go and tell others what you have seen."
\anc Anchor for "Many days later" - Marshall Commentary, Luke 22:44 "The teaching given by
Jesus follows on directly from the recognition scene and also leads on directly to the
departure scene. The whole series is thus placed on Easter Sunday evening, although in
Acts 1 Luke puts the departure forty days after the resurrection. ... he has consciously
telescoped his story at some point. A break at the end of the present scene is probable.
... it is probable that he is here summarising what Jesus said to his disciples over the
period of the resurrection appearances.
\tst How can someone change their life?   "Change your life - take a new road, Jesus' road.
\tst How do people take Jesus' road?  Do God's work.  
\tst Tst2:  How can someone "change your behavior"?  to literally turn around from bad to
good.  to turn your back on the bad things that you do or have done
\tst Tst3:  Why did Jesus tell them to go all over the world?  Because he wants the entire
world to know him.  They all do bad things.  He wants his disciples to go all over the
world to tell about his words, so that they can believe in him and do God's work.
\tst Tst3:  Why should they change their behavior?  They do bad things - but when they hear
and understand God's words, they will want  to do God's work.
\tst Tst3:  Why will God forgive their sins?  Because they had done bad things and when God
forgives them, they can go and be with God above.  When they listen to God's words, he
will forgive them.
\tst Tst3:  In retelling, he states, "He said, 'You will go the world and tell this to the people. 
You will be my witnesses." 
\tst Tst4:  In retelling, she also omits the "That they should change their behavior" and
states instead that "They should believe so that God will forgive them."
\tst Tsts:  Again, the concept of repentence is not retold.  This line may be retold as "You
have seen me suffer, die , and rise from death.  Now go and tell people all over the
world.  So that people will leave the road they are on and take my road. Then God will
forgive their sins.  Revised.  Upon retesting, Tst3 (retest), this line was now retold and
the concept of repentence told in terms of leaving their road and taking God's.
\ln 50.18
\old When that happens, you are going to be my witnesses all over the world.
\anc act.01:08 , luk.24:48 , 
\tst How would someone be a witness?   If I grab a criminal and take him to the mayor,
before I go to the mayor I will take someone with me who saw this also.  Another
example - If I take your book and Mowa sees me take your book.  You can say, "You
took my book.  Mowa is my witness because she saw you take it."
\tst Why did Jesus call these people his "witnesses"?  Because they know and have seen his
work and all that he has done.
\tst Tst3:  How can they be "witnesses" all over the world?  Because they listen and believe
these true things that have happened.  They saw it and went to tell others so they can
believe this true thing also.
\tst Tst3:  In retelling, this was simplified to "You will be my witnesses."  See proposed line
change in line 17 above.  Revised.
\ln 50.19
\bt God's {Spirit} will come upon you and give you {power}.  With this
power, you will be able to tell people about me.
\old So when that happens, I am going to give you a helper who is going to be the Holy Spirit
[KH: God's {Spirit}]."
\anc act.01:08 , luk.24:49, TN, "He meant that the Holy Spirit would soon come to be with
them to powerfully enable them to tell others about him."
\tst Tst3:  Why will Jesus give them a helper?  To help them do all of their work, because
God wants to help them with their work of going all over the world and tellings God's
words.  He wants to help them.
\tst Tst3:  How can he give them God's Spirit?  Because he is the good soul of God - there
are many people, the soul can help them to do God's good works.
\tst Tst3:  Line omitted in retelling.  
\tst Tst4:  Line omitted in retelling. 
\tst Tsts:  The reason this line may not be being retold is that in this story, the wording of
"Holy Spirit" has not been changed to match the keyterm for the story set, but is instead
using an old Supyire word that literally translates "Holy Spirit".  The wording in this line
could also be simplified.  "God's Spirit will come to you and give you power to tell people
about me." See revised line.   Line retold in Tst3(retest).
\ln 50.20
\bt When he said that, he took off.  He was covered by the clouds and
they couldn't see him.  
\anc act.01:09
\tst Tst2:  Why did Jesus "take off"?  What is this?  Jesus left the ground and went into the
skies, very literally went into the sky.  (This was even acted out with a sweeping motion
of the arms from the ground to the sky.)
\tst Tst3:  How did Jesus take off?  I didn't see it (he laughs).  But God called him and told
him to come so he took off and went above (made a motion with hands and a
"fooyaaa"sound as they went up).
\tst Tst3:  Why could they not see him anymore?  Because he went above.  Really far.  This
was an amazing thing.  They couldn't see him because he was far up.
\ln 50.21
\bt They looked at the sky and 2 people came and stood next to them and
asked them...
\old They looked at the sky {KT: above} and 2 people came down and asked them, 
\anc act.01:10
\tst Tst3:  Why did these two people come down?  Because they were there to tell them that
Jesus would one day come back the same way he left.  They came to tell them that.
\ln 50.21b
\bt "What are you looking at like that?  Jesus has gone {above} to God. 
But one day, he will come back to {earth}.  The same way you see
him leaving, this is the way you will see him come back."
\old "What are you looking at like that?  The way you are looking at Jesus going above is the
same way you will see him coming down."
\anc act.01:11
\tst Who are these people who came down?  We think they are angels, but the word does not
say for sure.
\tst Why do the angels say "you will see him coming down"?  Jesus is coming back one day,
coming back down from the sky the same way they just saw him leave."
\tst Where do you think Jesus goes?  The sky.  What's there?  He is with God.  He is God's
son.  
\tst Tst3:  How can Jesus come back the same way he went up?  God wants us to  listen to
God's Words and be one - Then God will take him back down.
\tst Tst3:  Why will Jesus come back down?  So he can be with his students/disciples.  So he
can teach them and be with them.
\tst Tst3:  In retelling, he states, "Jesus, you are looking for, has left.  The way you are
looking above, what you are seeing, he will come back in that same way."
\tst Tst4: In retelling, she states this line the same as original.   
\tst Tst:  Based on the vagueness of testing answers from Tst3 especially, this will be revised
to be more explicit. "Jesus has left and gone above to be with God.  But one day, Jesus
will come back to earth the same way you see him leaving." Revised.

\co Further Testing Comments from Tst2:  
\tst What did you like about this story?  I like the part when Jesus rose up into the sky and
we know he will come back again.  I like the fact that Jesus died but came back, his
students saw him and were frightened.  That we can turn our backs on the bad things in
our life.
\tst What did you not like about the story?  That Jesus died.  That bodies rot, but Jesus did
not!  
\dt 02/Jan/2009

\c 52
\t Pentecost and Early Church
\cat Supyire
\p
\co Redemptive Theme:  It is through belief in Jesus, that one can be forgiven and saved
by God.  God's victorious power can be received by those who have a good
relationship with Him by believing in Jesus.
\co Basic Biblical concepts:  Jesus died and 3 days later rose again, coming of God's
Spirit on Jesus' followers, forgiveness, repentence, baptism, communion of believers.
\co Cohesion / Background:  Continue to build concept of receiving power directly from
God through His Spirit.  Cohesively restates that the Jesus whom they crucified was
the Savior they were waiting for.  Calls people to repentence by believing in Jesus,
leaving their old road and taking Jesus' road for the forgiveness of sin.  Introduces
the term for believers and the fellowship of believers.
\p
\co Story crafter's name or initials:  SS
\p Backtranslator's name or initials:  BK
\p
\co Resources used in crafting:  Audio version of French Parole de Vie, Bambara
Scripture, Supyire NT draft
\p
\co Audio Last Revised: 06Oct08
\co BT File Last Revised 15Oct08
\p
\tst Note:  Originally, this one story was two separate stories (Pentecost and Early Church). 
Original testing groups described below have at this point, heard the original 2 stories. 
However, comments from testing lines that are the same, have been included in the file
below.  This story will be tested again for retellability purposes.
\tst Original Testing:  Village with language helper and women friends.
\tst Tst2:  Nearby village with group of men.
\tst Tst3:  Day Guard - this revised combined story was tested again with this testor for
retelling and comments are below.
\tst Tst4:  Woman friend at phone booth
\p
\ln 52.01
\bt After Jesus went {above}, several weeks later, a big feast for
Abraham's offspring people had come.
\old After Jesus went {above}, several weeks later, there was a big feast for Abraham's
offspring people. 
\anc  Act.02:01
\tst Tst3:  Why did Jesus go above?  He went above to be with God.  He went up.  
\ln 52.02
\bt Many {believers} of Jesus were together in one house.  
\old All of the {believers} of Jesus were together in one house.
\anc Act.02:01
\tst Tst3:  Why were the believers together in one house?  They were all together in one
house so they could pray to God together and that God would help them.
\ln 52.03
\bt While they were there, suddenly a noise came from {above}.  This
noise was strong like a wind.  People who were in the house, everyone
heard this noise in all parts.
\old Suddenly, a noise came from above.  This noise was strong like a wind.  People who
were in the house, everyone heard this noise in all parts.
\anc act.02:02
\tst Tst3:  How could this noise happen?  I dont know.  How can I know?  But if Jesus did
allow it to happen, it can.  Like when you have the windows or doors open, the wind can
enter - it is the same way, but this is God's noise that came."
\tst Tst3:  In retelling, lines 1-3 were retold as is.    
\ln 52.04
\bt Then God's {Spirit} came onto each of them and gave them
{power}.  
\anc act.02:04
\tst Tst2:  Why were they filled with God's Holy Spirit?  so that they have part of God in them
\tst Tst3:  How could God' Spirit come onto them?  God did all of this.  God sent the noise
into the house from above and God did this so God's Spirit could enter them.  So that
they could say, God did this.  So that God could save them.  God saved them, so He
could help them and they could listen and speak God's Words.
\tst Tst3:  Why did God's Spirit come onto them?  God said he would save them and then
give someone to help them (old version of Resurrection story), so he sent his Spirit
down on them, so they could say and understand God's words.
\ln 52.05
\bt With this power, the believers began speaking many other languages. 
These languages they had not spoken before.
\anc act.02:04 
\tst How were they speaking other languages?  Everybody understands them.  God's part
that is in them gave them the strength to do it.
\tst Tst2 How were they speaking?  After God's Spirit came down on them and entered them
they were speaking about that because it filled them with joy
\tst Tst2 Why were they speaking these other languages?  because the Holy Spirit was on
them and they have joy and they have to talk about it, God.
\tst Tst3;  Why were they speaking other languages?  Because the spirit came down and
they could speak the other languages.  Like me - I can speak Supyire, Bambara French,
you speak Supyire and English.  But they could speak the languages from all over the
world because it came to them from above.
\tst Tst3:  How were they able to do this?  God's Spirit came down on them and gave them
the other languages to speak.  It was giving them God's Words to speak in the other
languages.
\tst Tst3:  In retelling, he omits the phrase "These languages they had not spoken before";
however, based on previous craftings of this story, this phrase is important to retain
because otherwise it has been interpreted that they were simply speaking other
languages that they knew.  Maybe now that this testor has grasped and understood this
concept, he is not repeating it, but for first time hearers of this story, it needs to remain.
\ln 52.06
\bt Many people from all over the {world} were there.  When they came
and heard the words of the believers, they were {astonished}. 
{Why}?  Because each of them was hearing their father's language
from the believers, talking about God.
\old The people who left some other countries who were speaking their father languages
were all {astonished}.  {Why}?  Because all of them was hearing their language from
the believers talking about God.
\anc act.02:05 - 07 , act.02:11
\cn KH:  Their "father's languages" is the same idea as "mother tongue" or native language.
\tst Tst2 Why were they astonished?  because they didn't know how they were speaking
these things about God and how they could each understand
\tst Tst3:  Why were there people there from all over the world?  Because they came
together in one place.  They all came to be at God's Praying House so they could pray
together because it was good for them.  Why did the people come?  So that they could
know what was making the noise.  Because it was a great noise that had come from
above and everybody wanted to know where it came from and to ask who was there.
\tst Tst3:  How did they hear their language?  The people were speaking them and they
heard and understood.
\tst Tst3:  Why were they so astonished?  Because they didn't think anybody would know
their language - like when you come to my house - you speak Supyire, everybody is
surprised to hear it, surprised to hear their own language.    (NOTE, Since this testing,
Line 05 has been revised to include "that they had not learned" to make it clearer that
these were not learned languages)
\tst Tst3:  How could they each hear their own language when the speakers are not from
their country?  Because Jesus did this.  He wanted everybody to hear and understand. 
When God speaks to you he says it in English, but when God speaks to me, he says it in
Supyire or Bambara.  Because Jesus wants them to understand.
\tst Tst3:  Why were they talking "about God"?  Because God's Spirit came down on them.  It
came down on them so they could speak God's Words.  Why?  God's words were good
for them to speak about.  Like now, you speak God's Words and they are good for me.
\tst Tst3:  In retelling he states, "People that were in the village came. Each person was
hearing his father's language talking about God."  Based on this retelling, it should be
included  that "People from all over the world were there.  When they came and heard
the words of the believers, they were astonished.  Why?  Because all of them were
hearing their father's language from the believers talking about God"   Retold after
revising and retesting.
\ln 52.07
\bt When they were doing that, some began mocking them and said,
"They've drunk alcohol!"
\old When they were doing that some said, "Let's mock them, they drunk alcohol!"
\anc act.02:13
\cn KH:  "when they were doing that" is the bridge could also be said along the same lines
of, "at that time..."  this is the understanding.
\cn KH:  Most here do know what drinking alcohol is like and what it does to you.  Many
times we have seen it and seems our friends and family crack jokes and make fun of
those who are drunk.  This idea of "mocking the drunk" is something they can relate to.
\tst Why would they mock them?  Because they don't like the words they are saying
\tst Tst3:  Why were some mocking them?  They mocked them because the words they were
saying about God were not good for them.  God's Spirit came down on the believers and
gave them these words about God, but they said they were drinking alcohol because
they didn't like the words they were saying.
\ln 52.08

\anc act.02:14
\tst Tst3:  Why did the disciples get up?  They got up to say the truth because they wanted
the people to know that they were not drinking alcohol.
\tst Tst3:  Why did Peter take the speech?  He took the speech to tell the people that they
were understanding the other languages because of God's Spirit that came down on
them and not because of alcohol.
\tst Tst3:  Why would Peter tell them to "Open their ears and listen"?  Because when you
open your ears you can understand.  Peter wanted them to really understand the words
that he was telling them.
\ln 52.09
\bt They didn't drink alcohol, but it is God's Spirit that gave them this

\tst Tst3:  In retelling, he makes it explicit "It's God's Spirit that came down on them and
gave them the power to speak these other languages."  This would be a good change

\ln 52.10

\ln 52.11
\bt You know Jesus.  You killed him by nailing him to a tree.  
\anc act.02:23 - 24

\tst Tst3:  Why did they kill him by nailing him to a tree?  Because the words he said and

\ln 52.12

\ln 52.13
\bt Jesus is the Savior that we were waiting for {KT: Christ}.
\old Jesus is the Savior that we were waiting for {KT: Christ}.  Now, he has given us God's

\anc act.02:36
\tst Tst3: Why did he send God's Spirit to them?  Because he is like God, He sent him to do

\tst Tst3:  Line was retold as, "He said God's Spirit would come on them."  He had stated in

waiting for"  After retesting this revision, it was retold now.
\ln 52.14
\bt At the time they hear that, it burns their hearts.
\anc act.02:37
\cn KH:  Your heart or insides,  in Supyire culture are your emotions.  For something to burn
in their hearts it means it is something that makes them remember and think over it. 
(as explained by BK)  Is this a good thing?  If the words are true.
\tst What does it mean for the words to burn in your heart?  It means that the words are not
good for them
\tst tst2 They didn't like the words they heard, his words hurt them because their character
was bad and they had not turned from their bad ways
\tst Tst3:  Why did their hearts burn?  Their hearts burnt because of all the words they had
heard, these words were good for them now, they wanted to ask what they should do
now.
\tst Tst3:  Retold.
\ln 52.15
\bt Then they asked Peter and the other disciples, "What should we do?"
\anc act.02:37
\tst Tst3:  Why did they ask, "What should we do"?  Because they knew they had done bad
things.  They wanted to turn from their bad things and hear more of God's Words.
\tst Tst3:  Retold.   
\ln 52.16
\bt Then Peter answered, "Let your old {road} and take Jesus' road. 
Believe {KT: trust}  in Jesus and be baptized {KT: baptize}.
\old Then Peter answered, "You had better change your behavior and let your old habits that
are not right and baptized {KT: baptize}.  Why?  Because now, you {trust} in Jesus.
\anc act.02:38
\cn KH:  "turn your back on your bad habits" ... is the common way to say to stop doing
something.
\tst What does it mean to be baptized?  Your head enters water and its a sign you are
following God's road.  You turn your back on your sins.
\tst tst2 What does it mean to be baptized?  To turn your back on your bad things and take
God's road
\tst Tst3:  Why does Peter tell them to change their behavior?  Because they asked Peter
what they should do.  They should change their behavior because if they do and they
listen to God's Words, God will forgive their bad things.
\tst Tst3:  Why would you want to be baptized?  So that they can go to God's kingdom - so
they can understand God's Words and that God would forgive them.
\tst Tst3:  He struggled, but did say the "Let your old habits that are not right and be
baptized.  You believe in Jesus."  Based on previous stories and the difficulty in retelling
the phrase above, this will be changed to, "Leave your road and take Jesus' road. 
Believe in Jesus and be baptized.  God will forgive your sins.  God will send His Spirit to
you and give you power."  This was retested and retold well.
\ln 52.17
\bt God will {forgive} you.  Then, God will give his Spirit to you and give
you power."   
\old God will {forgive} your {sins} and God's Spirit will come onto you and give you power." 
\anc act.02:39
\tst Tst2 Who is God going to forgive?  Why?  God is going to forgive the people when they
do / follow God.  Why?  Because they have turned their backs on their sins and are
following him.
\tst Tst3:  Why will God forgive your sins?  Because they have listened to God and done his
good things.  They were baptized and let their bad things behind them, so God forgive
them.
\tst Tst3:  Why will God's Spirit come to them?  Because they were baptized because they
believe in Jesus.  Because they have listened to God's Words and done His work.  God's
Spirit will give them help and peace.
\tst Tst3:  In retelling, he states, "God will forgive you", but leaves off the second half.  See
unpacking of this above in line 16.
\ln 52.18
\bt This day many people were baptized thanks to Peter's words.  
\old This day many people was baptized thanks to Peter's words and the number of the
believers was increasing. 
\anc act.02:41
\tst Did the people listen to Peter?  Yes, they listened and gave God's words to their hearts,
then baptized and worked for God.
\tst How many is "many"?  there is no how many.  (They then started naming villages)
\tst Tst3:  Why were the people baptized?  Because of the words Peter was saying to them. 
Because Peter's words were the words that Jesus had given him.
\tst Tst3:  How did their numbers increase?  Because they were understanding God's Words. 
Some heard, then more came, then more came to understand.  They became a lot
because of these words of God.
\tst Tst3:  Line summarized to, "Many people accepted and were baptized thanks to Peter's
words."  Last part of this line can be deleted.  Deleted.
\ln 52.19
\bt The believers were listening to God's words together, they were
eating together in their houses, 
\anc act.02:42
\tst Tst3:  Why were they listening to God's Words?  Because they believed the words and
they were good for them.  
\tst Tst3:  Why did they eat together?  Because their work was one, their will was one.  So
they ate together.  Like you and your teammate (Warraba) - your work is one, you eat
together as one.
\ln 52.20
\bt they were praying {KT: pray} to God together and praising {KT:
praise} God together.  
\anc act.02:42 , act.02:47
\tst Tst3:  Why were they praying to God together?  So when you pray together God would
hear you, because of the work that they were doing, they were one.  They were praying
to God about the work.
\tst Tst3:  Why did they praise God?  Because Jesus praised God.  They wanted to be like
Jesus.  They praised God because he had given them peace.
\tst Tst3:  While testing respondent does retell lines 19 and 20, he tells them in a different
manner, "Believers ate as one in their houses.  They listened to God's words as one. 
They praised God as one."  The expression "as one" is simply a different manner of
saying "together".  It does not need to be changed.  The phrase "together" has been
repeated in previous stories and with this and other testors.
\ln 52.21
\bt God's Spirit was giving Jesus' disciples power to do {extraordinary}
things.  
\old Jesus' disciples were doing extraordinary things. Why?  Because God's Spirit was giving
them power.  
\anc act.02:43 , TN "God is the implied agent who was causing those many wonders and
miraculous signs to happen."
\tst Tst3:  How did he give them strength to do extraordinary things?  God put his strength
on them, so they could say his words, they could heal people and do the strange things
God wants them to do.  Why would they be doing strange things? Jesus did strange
things.  He healed people and opened eyes.  They are doing it so other people could
know and follow Jesus.
\tst Tst3:  How did the disciples do these extraordinary things?  Jesus did these things - so
they were working after him, they were healing people and doing strange things and
putting people on God's road.
\tst Tst3:  Line retold as, "Jesus gave power to his disciples and they were doing
extraordinary things."   In a previous retelling, he stated, "God gave power to Jesus'
disciples.  They were doing the extraordinary things of Jesus."  The phrasing could be
reordered, "God's Spirit gave Jesus' disciples power.  They were doing extraordinary
things."  The "Why?" phrase does not seem to fit here as this is not "Why" they were
doing these things, but "how".  We will emphasize that it is "God's Spirit" giving them
power.
\ln 52.22

\anc act.02:43

\tst Ts3:  Why were the people astonished?  Becaue the people were doing these strange

\tst Tst3:  How did it touch their hearts?  Because of the strange things, when it touched their

\dt 02/Jan/2009

\c 56
\t Philip and the African
\co Supyire
\p      
\co Redemptive theme:  There is access to God's victorious power and wisdom through
belief in Jesus.
\co Basic Biblical concepts:  Immediacy of baptism, Belief in Jesus as God's Son.   
\co Cohesion / Background:  Builds on the relationship between God and those who
follow Jesus as one of God's angel as well as His Spirit guide and direct Philip.  The
story continues to build the call to share God's Words with others and then to praise
God for what He has done.  The story cohesively ties the Isaiah passage here to the
Isaiah story.
\p
\co Story crafter's name or initials:  SS
\co Backtranslator's name or initials:  BK 
\p
\co Resources used in crafting:  Audio version of Supyire NT text, audio of Bambara text,
audio of French "Parole de Vie"
\p
\co Audio Last Revised 20Oct08
\co BT File Last Revised 21Oct08
\p
\tst General Testing Observations:  The testors have responded well to this story.  They take
this story and make it their own story of showing how God cares for them.  Why? 
Because even in the beginning, He wanted Africans to know him and sent messengers to
explain His Word to them.  It is one that is easy to retell and is simple to understand.
\tst Tst2:  Group of men in Gnirwani:  General Comments:  They were able to retell the
story very well.  The only line and portion they left out:  the details of the black man -
his job and the fact that he is a VIP.  They also simplified and said the black man was
reading from the Bible - omitting the reference to Isaiah.  They also struggled with the
exact text from Isaiah,  taking a few moments to think and having several people
interject the lines slowly.  However, the connection was clearly gotten and made
between Jesus and the words of Isaiah.
\tst Tst3:  Day Guard - The connection was made between Isaiah's book and Jesus.  Being
that this testing respondent has heard the stories chronologically and in a shorter time
duration than test 2, he had little troubles remembering Isaiah.  See comments below
with regard to retelling.
\tst Tst4:  Friend at Phone Booth  - Tested for retelling only.   Based on latest retellings, only
minor changes are required in the story text to make it more natural.
\p    
\ln 56.01
\bt This is something true that also happened.
\anc 2Ti.03:16 , Psa.119:142 (New Century Version) "...your teachings are true";
Psa.119:160 (NIV) "all your words are true"; Jhn.17:17 "your word is truth".
\ln 56.02a
\bt After Jesus went {above} to God, God's {Spirit} came onto Jesus'
{disciples} and gave them {power}.
\old Jesus went {above} and let God‚Äôs {Spirit} down to come and fill his {disciples} insides.  
\anc Act.02:23- 24, Act.02:32 - 33 , Act.02:04
\cn MM:  We reworked this introduction to make it a better transition from the Pentecost
stories.
\tst Tst3:  How did God's Spirit fill their insides?  It came down on them after Jesus had went
up.  It filled them and gave them God's Words to speak.
\tst Tst3:  In retelling, he states, "After Jesus went above to be with God, God's Spirit came
and filled his disciples.
\tst Tst4:  In retelling, she states, "... and let God's Spirit to come onto his disciples."
\tst Based on retellings, and on previous stories, the phrasing of this should be cohesive. 
Since the concept of "filling one's insides" may be a bit abstract, it may be best to
rephrase this line as, "After Jesus went above to be with God, God's Spirit came onto his
disciples and gave them power."  Revised.
\ln 56.02b
\bt After that, they were walking around telling about Jesus.
\old After Jesus went above, His disciples were walking and saying God's words.
\anc Act.04:33 , Act.08:01 , Act.08:04 , Act.08:40 , Act.13:1 -4 , Entire Book of Acts
\cn BK:  The phrase "walking and saying God's Words" means that they were delivering
God's Word from one place to another.  Even if you were on horse, bike, or donkey, you
would still use the phrase here for "walking".
\tst Why were Jesus' disciples walking?  To speak Jesus' words and do His work.  Why? Jesus
is strong and good.
\tst Tst2:  Why were Jesus' disciples walking?  To show people God's Words and speak God's
words.  Why?  Because they trusted God and wanted to do His work.
\tst Tst3:  Why were they walking and sharing God's Words?  Because they want the people
to know God's Words.  Like Jesus had taught them.
\ln 56.03

"Get up and go to the south."
\anc Luk.06:14 , Act.01:13 , Act.08:26

black man was coming and reading Isaiah's words.  God's Angel knew the one man was
coming.
\tst Tst2:  Why did God's Angel speak to Philip?  To tell him to go to the wagon.  Why did
God's Angel choose Philip?  Because Philip is God's good one.  He is good to God.
\tst Tst3:  Why did God's angel tell Philip to go to the south?  Because a horse cab was going
to come with a black man in it who can hear God's Words and will be baptized.
\tst Tst3:  In retelling, he omits "Get up" from this phrase.
\tst Tst4:  In retelling, she states this phrase as is.  It will remain.  
\ln 56.04

\tst Tst2:  Why did Philip go there?  The wagon was coming.  It was an extraordinary thing. 
The angel knew. 
\tst Tst3:  Why did Philip go where there is nobody?  He was going to the road to the south
that lead from Jerusalem.  The road didn't have anybody on it.  The road was hard.

\ln 56.05
\bt So Philip took the road.  While he was going, he found a black person
coming in a horse cab.  
\old So he was going and found a black person, who left Jerusalem in a horse cab.
\anc Act.08:27 - 28
\cn MM:  "See-pee-whorrow" = "Black-skinned person".  When asked in crafting and testing
and others how to say in Supyire, "A man who comes from Africa", this is the term
given.  In testing further, we discovered there is no problem or offensive nature to this
term.  They do not use this term in everyday speech here, because everyone is black
here, but in a mixed setting, you could say this.  We chose to go generic with "African"
because no one here knows where Ethiopia is, and we want this story to be most
relevant to them.  
\cn MM:  In testing, it was evident that this man is important because he is riding in a
cab/wagon pulled by horses.  The horse ‚Äì even today ‚Äì shows that person or that family
is a little richer than others.  Used to be used by king.  People say now that  the horse is
‚Äúblessed‚Äù animal and should not be used like a donkey ‚Äì for work.
\tst Why did Philip go?  Philip knew that what God's angel had told him was true.  Philip knew
God's angel was wise.  
\tst Tst2:  Who would you call a "see-poo-wo-ngy"?  Black skinned people.  All of us here,
except you.  When would someone use this word?  Not here in Mali because everyone
here is black.  But if you were in America, you would say it.  It's like when you are in
America - nobody calls you "American" or "White person".
\tst Tst2:  Why would someone drive a horse wagon?  If they were going long distances. 
There were no cars or motos in those days.  Long ago, kings and authorities would drive
a horse wagon.
\tst Tst3:  How did Philip "find" this black person?  Because he was going on a horse cab.  If
I was going to market on a horse cab, you would see me!
\tst Tst3:  Why was he in a horse cab?  Because he was a VIP - so he had horses. 
\tst Tst3:  He states, "So Philip went.  He saw a black man on a horse cab." 
\tst Tst4:  In retelling, she states, "So Philip was going and took that road and found a black
person who was in a horse cab. ..."
\tst Tst:  In both retellings they omit that he "left Jerusalem".  This can be rephrased to
state, "So Philip took that road.  While he was going, he saw a black person, coming in a
horse cab."  Revised.

\ln 56.13
\bt It said in that part, "They took him and went with him to be killed, like
they take a sheep to the killing place.  Then he lowered himself and let

\old It said in that part, "They took him and went with him, like they take a sheep to the

\anc Act.08:32
\cn MM:  he phrase "They catch him and went with him" in English more closely would be
translated as such, "They took him and led him away".
\cn BK:  The phrase "He lowered himself and let himself" implies a lack of a fight or
resistance.
\cn SS:  Here - He lowers himself to them, he became low - He was not an VIP anymore. 
He let himself to them and allowed them to take him.
\tst Tst3:  Who do you think the part about the sheep is talking about?  Jesus - it was about
Jesus, Jesus was like the sheep.
\tst Tst3:  Why would they catch him?  They caught him so they could take him and kill him.
\tst Tst3:  Why did they lead him like a sheep to the killing place?  Because when you take a
sheep, he doesn't talk - even when going to the killing place.  Jesus, he didn't talk when
they took him to kill him either.
\tst Tst3:  Why would he give himself to them?  He let them take him because he knew they
would kill him , but that after he would go to be with God.
\tst Tst3:  This line was retold as is, except for ... "They catch him and went with him to the

here means "allowed")
\tst Tst4:  In retelling, she does tell the last sentence as is "But he gave himself to them."

be killed, like a sheep is led to the killing place. "  Remainder stays the same.  Revised.

\ln 56.18
\bt Then the black person said, "Here is water.  Can I be baptized {KT:
baptize}?"
\anc Act.08:36
\tst Why does the black man want to be baptized?  Because he wants to follow the Jesus
