\tst Tst2:  Why does the man want to be baptized?  He studied the Bible.  He knows God's
character now.  He trusted Jesus and wants to be baptized now.
\tst Tst2:  When should people be baptized?  When they understand God's Words and trust
Him.  The story says that if you trust in Jesus, you can be baptized.
\tst Tst3:  Why does the black man say, "Here is water"?  Because he knew you have to
have water to be baptized and he wanted to be baptized.
\tst Tst3:  How does the black man know about baptism?  He knew that when you believe in
Jesus, you should be baptized to be forgiven from your sins.  He learned this from the
words they were speaking.
\ln 56.19
\bt Then Philip said, "If you believe {KT: trust} in Jesus, you can be
baptized."
\anc Act.08:37 , NKJ, NIV , TN
\anc In "TN" and in footnotes in the NIV it is explained that while this verse is most likely not
in the earliest manuscripts, " it does represent information some of which the text
implies. Also, the national language version for your language area may include this
verse."  It is also included in our Senufo Supyire draft of the NT.
\tst When should people get baptized?  When you trust Jesus, you should be baptized.  
\tst Tst3:  Why does he have to believe in Jesus to be baptized?  You have to believe in
Jesus to be baptized.  If you don't believe, you don't get baptized.  You have to believe
in Jesus to enter God's road.
\ln 56.20
\bt So the black person said, "I believe that Jesus is God's Son."
\anc Act.08:37 ,  NKJ , TN
\tst Why is Jesus called God's Son?  He has His Strength and is right/good.
\tst Tst2:  Why does the black man say Jesus is God's Son?  The words Philip said to the
man, he believed them and trusted Jesus and knew that Jesus is God's Son.
\tst Tst3:  How does he believe in Jesus?  Because Jesus had said God's Words to his
disciples.  Jesus was God's Son - He was God's Chosen One.  He believed this and
wanted to enter Jesus' road.
\tst Tst3:  How does he know that Jesus is God's Son?  Because Jesus had said His words to
his disciples.  They knew he was God's Son.  He said that God had sent him.  God's 
Spirit gave birth to him.  He was God's Son.  Why does this man believe this?  Because
Jesus had said God's Words and done God's things - so the believed him.
\ln 56.21
\bt So they went forward and stopped the cab.
\anc Act.08:38
\tst Tst3:  Why did they stop the cab?  Because he wanted to be baptized.  They stopped the
cab so they could get down and be baptized because he said he believed Jesus was
God's Son.
\ln 56.22
\bt They got out of it and Philip baptized him.
\anc Act.08:39
\tst Tst3:  How did Philip baptize him?  Philip baptized him like Jesus was baptized.  He
entered him into the water, brought him back out.
\ln 56.23
\bt Then, he left praising {KT: praise} God.  
\old Then, the black man left, praising God.  {KT: praise}
\old In that way, he went home and was saying God's good words.
\anc Act.08:39
\tst Tst2:  Why was the black man praising God?  He accepted and believed God and knew
God is the true God.  God is the Savior and has saved him.
\tst Tst3:  Why did the black man leave?  Because he was going to his home, his country,
where the queen was for him to work.
\tst Tst3:  Why was he praising God?  Because he had been praising God because he had
been baptized and knew about God's Words, so he was praising God.
\tst Tsts:  In both retellings, ending has been retold as is.  (Lines 16 - end)

\ln Further Comments from First Testing Group:
\tst What do you like about the story?  The part where Philip explains God's Words to the
man, the part where God's Spirit tells Philip to go near the wagon.
\tst What part of the story do you not like or find hard?  The part where the black man was
reading God's Words, but didn't understand it.  The part where Isaiah's words say that
he will be taken like a sheep and killed.

\ln Further Comments from Tst2:
\tst What do you like about the story?  The part where Jesus was explained to the black
man.  The part where the black man was baptized because he accepted/believed in
Jesus, the part where Jesus made himself like a sheep, lowering himself and allowing
himself to be killed, .. when the black man went home praising God
\tst What part did you not like?  When the black man was reading and he didn't understand. 
Supyire is difficult.  Everyone can't read.
\dt 02/Jan/2009

\c 58
\t Philippian Jailer Story
\co Supyire
\p
\co Redemptive Theme:  There can be a good relationship between God and people
through belief in Jesus.  How can one be saved?  Believe in Jesus.   Also, there is
access for the believers of Jesus to His victorious power over evil.  God acts
powerfully to provide for and save those in good relationship with Him.
\co Basic Biblical concepts:  Sharing the news of Jesus with others, baptism, God's
power over evil and over nature, persecution, praising God in midst of suffering,
power in prayer, fellowship of believers
\co Cohesion / Background:  Unpacks what Jesus' followers were doing when they were
"telling about Jesus" in cohesive terms relating to the way in which Jesus has
provided restored relationship with God.  Again, refers to those who follow Jesus as
"believers".  Ties in "those who take Jesus' road" with those who "trust" in Him.
\co Worldview/Selection:  Evil spirits are very much still present here in the everyday
world of the Senufo Supyire.  Therefore, this story importantly shows that there is a
way to have power over these evil spirits.
\p
\co Resources used in Crafting: Audio of Bambara scripture, audio of Supyire draft, audio
of French "Parole de Vie."
\co
\p Story crafter's name or initials: SS
\co Backtranslator's name or initials: BK
\p
\co Latest Audio Revision: 20Oct08
\co Latest BT File Revision: 21Oct08
\p
\tst General Comments from Initial Testing Session in Village:  The story is a long one, but
with much action and little dialogue.  This made it easy for them to retell.  They retold
the story well and understood the content of the story.
\p
\tst General Comments from Tst2:  Group of men in Gnir.  Amazing details were
remembered in the retelling of this story after hearing it only twice.  This is a lengthy
story, but based on the retelling, the depth of detail does not need to be reduced.
Outside of the items mentioned in the BT below, the story was retold well and was an
encouragement that the text of the story may not require much change.
\tst Tst3:  Day guard
\tst Tst4:  Friend at phone booth
\p                 
\ln 58.01a
\bt This is something true that also happened.
\anc 2Ti.03:16 , Psa.119:142 (New Century Version) "...your teachings are true";
Psa.119:160 (NIV) "all your words are true"; Jhn.17:17 "your word is truth".
\ln 58.01b
\old Jesus‚Äô {disciples} were walking around all over the {world} and telling the Good News.  
\anc Act.04:33 , Act.08:05 , Act.08:04 , Act.08:40 , Act.13:01 -4 , Entire Book of Acts
\tst Tst2:  What do you think Jesus' disciples were saying?  They were speaking God's words,
the words of God's messengers.  What are these words?  Words that are good for us,
words that tell us to have faith in God.
\tst Tst3:  What is the "Good News"?  It is God's Words, they were walking and telling people
about Jesus.  This is good news - God's Word is good news.  Why?  Because Jesus gave
God's Words to his disciples and they are to walk and share these words.  It's good
because it's from Jesus.
\tst Tst2: In the introduction, it was stated that Jesus' disciples were speaking God's Words
instead of saying "Good News".  Based on the fact that this is the only location in our
story set this is used and on the fact that it is unclear as to what they are saying, we will
remove this keyterm.  (What they were telling people, will be unpacked in line 02)
\tst Tst3:  In retelling, he omits this line and goes directly to the introduction of Paul and
Silas in line 02.  
\tst Tst4:  Also, in retelling, she goes directly into the introduction of Paul and Silas.  This line
will be deleted from story.  Deleted.
\ln 58.02
\bt Paul and Silas were some of Jesus' {disciples}.  They were walking
around villages telling about Jesus.
\anc Act.15:36 , Act.15:40 -41 , Act.16:01 , Act.16:04 - 12
\anc Anchor for the unpacking of "good news" - TW says this expression always has the
meaning in the NT of <the good news or joyful report that God has made a way of
salvation for sinful human beings>.
\tst Why were Paul and Silas walking around?  to speak God's Words.  What are God's
Words?  Jesus' Words.  What are Jesus' Words?  (There seems to be a bit of ambiguity
here.  A possible explanation somewhere along the story set of what "Good News" is or
what "Jesus' Words" means may be appropriate.)  We originally had they were walking
around speaking "Jesus' good words".  Because of this ambiguity we changed it to
"telling about Jesus".
\tst Tst2:  The fact that Paul and Silas were some of Jesus' disciples was not made explicit in
the retelling; however, this is the first time these two names are introduced and must
remain in the story.  He did remember their names in the retelling.
\tst Tst3:  In retelling, he introduces Paul and Silas as "Paul and Silas were two of Jesus'
disciples.  They were walking around villages saying "God's Words" so people would
enter God's road.
\tst Tst4:  In retelling, she states this line as in the original.  Either way seems acceptable
and natural.  The fact that they were "telling people about Jesus" will be unpacked here. 
It can be unpacked as, "... telling about Jesus.  They said that if they believe in Jesus,
there can be a good relationship between them and God."  Unpacked in line 02b below.
\ln 58.02b
\bt They said if you believe {KT: trust} in Jesus, there can be a good
{relationship} between you and God.
\anc Act.16:10
\anc Anchor for the unpacking of "good news" - TW says this expression always has the
meaning in the NT of <the good news or joyful report that God has made a way of

\ln 58.03
\bt They went to a village, the name of that village was Philippi.  They
spent a few days there.
\old They went to a village, the name of that village was Philippi.  As soon as they reached
Phlippi-village, they spent a few days there.
\anc Act.16:12
\tst Tst2:  The word here used for village, what do you think of when you hear this word?  It
is a place.  For example, it could be this village here (population 500).  It could be
Farakala (our town, slightly larger, of 1000).  It could be Sikasso (city closest to us) or it
could be Bamako (large capital city).  We do not know how big or how many people are
in Philippi.
\tst Tst3:  Why did they go to Philippi?  They went to Philippi because they were walking and
telling God's good news.  They were going from village to village and when they came to
Philippi they went to tell about God's Words.
\tst Tst3:  Why did they spend a few days there?  Because they went there to tell them God's
good news - so they stayed there so they could tell them.  They stayed there several
days to tell the whole village.
\tst Tst3:  In retelling, the phrase "As soon as they reached Philippi" was changed to "They
went into Philippi and stayed a few days there."  The phrase "As soon as they reached
Philipp - village" will be deleted.  Deleted.
\ln 58.04
\bt The day of rest, the went near the river bank.  They thought that they
were going to find people praying {KT: pray} to God there.
\old The day of rest, the went near the river bank.  They thought that they were going to find
people praising {KT: praise} God there.
\anc Act.16:13
\tst Why did they think people would be praising God there?  It is the day of rest.  Many
people praise God on the day of rest.  Our village ‚Äì day of rest is Monday.  Farakala
Christians day of rest is Sunday, others is Monday
\tst tst2:  Why did the women go to the riverbank to praise God there?  It's a place where
people would go to praise God.  The women like it there by the river.

\ln 58.07
\bt So they told her about Jesus and she accepted {KT: accept} Jesus. 
{Why?} Because God had opened her heart.
\old So they told Jesus‚Äô good words and Lydie accepted {KT:  accept}.  {Why}?  Because
God had opened her heart.
\anc Act.16:14
\tst Who is they?  Who told her Jesus' Good words?  Paul and Silas.
\tst Why did she accept these words?  God opened her heart and gave her intelligence.  He
"opened" her wisdom.  What does the word "accept" mean here?  It means that she
agreed with what they were saying.  It has the same meaning as "faith" or "believed"
here.
\tst Tst2:  How did God open Lydie's heart?  The words they said to her were good for her. 
God made the words good for her.  How does God open people's hearts?  Good things
that are done - they come to you.  (Implying God gives good things, like information,
blessings to you).
\tst Tst2:  Why does Lydie accept God?  Because she knows God will give peace and health
to her.  
\tst Tst2:  Again, line 07 is unclear as to exactly what they are telling Lydie.  In the retelling
it says they spoke "God's Words" to her.  We may make this more explicit.
\tst Tst3:  Here, in retelling, he stated, "They told God's words to her.  God opened her heart
and she accepted." 
\tst Tst4:  Also, in retelling, she states, "They told God's words to her.  And Lydie accepted. 
And she trusted in Jesus.  Why?  Because God had opened her heart."
\tst Tsts:  Based on testing and retellings, this line will be rephrased to "So they told her
about Jesus and she believed (trusted) in Jesus.  Why?  Because God had opened her
heart."
\ln 58.08
\bt So Lydie and the members of her family were baptized {KT: baptize}.  
\anc Act.16:15
\tst Tst3:  Why were Lydie and the members of her family baptized?  So God would forgive
their wrong doings because when you accept God's Words and are baptized God will
forgive you.
\ln 58.09
\bt Why?  Because they all believed in Jesus.  The moment Lydie and the
members of her family were baptized,  Lydie asked Paul and Silas to
spend some days in her home.  So they went there.
\old So they all accepted God.  The moment Lydie and the members of her family were

\anc Act.16:15
\tst Tst2:  How do they all accept God?  They are shown that He is good.  They like Him.  He
agrees to them - They accept/agree with Him. He gives them good things.  What do you
do to show that you have accepted God?  They are given peace.  They like the good
road.
\tst Tst3:  How did Lydie's family accept?  Lydie, her husband, her whole family accepted
God's words to be forgiven of their wrong doings.  They wanted to understand and learn
from God and Jesus.
\tst Tst3: Why did Lydie ask Paul and Silas to spend some days in her home?  Because Paul
and Silas had come and told them God's Words.  They believed and were baptized. 
They wanted Paul and Silas to come so they could hear God's Words and they could be
one.  (Their work could be one).
\tst Tst2:  From the original story, the retelling chronologically mixes up the order of her and
her family being baptized with them staying several days at her house.
\tst Tst3:  In retelling, the events were retold in the proper chronological order as, "Lydie
and all the members of her family were baptized.  They were baptized, why? because
they all accepted Jesus.  Then she asked them to stay some days with her and her
family."
\tst Tst4:  In retelling, she states, (Line 08-09), "Lydie was baptized and all the members of
her family were baptized.  Then, Lydie asked Paul and Silas to spend some days there.
So they went to Lydie's house"
\tst Tsts:  Based on the fact that chronologically this may be difficult to retell, the wording of
the phrase "So, they all accepted God..." will be changed to "Why?  Because they all
believed in Jesus."  Remainder of line will remain as is.  Revised.
\ln 58.10
\bt One day, when they were going to God‚Äôs praying place they met a
servant woman.  She was haunted by a demon {KT: demons}.  Her
demon made her tell the future.
\old One day, when they were going to God‚Äôs praying {house} they met a servant woman. 
She was haunted by a demon {KT: demons}.  Her demon made her tell the future.
\old One day, when they were going to God‚Äôs praising place they met a servant woman.  She
was haunted by a demon {KT: demons}.  Her demon made her tell the future.
\anc Act.16:16
\cn MM:  The phrase "haunted by a demon" is literally stated in Supyire as "a demon was in
her".  This is the phrased used in the Supyire NT draft.
\tst Tst2:  The fact that Paul and Silas were going to "God's praising place" was not retold in
the same fashion. In tst3, he retold this naturally as "God's praying house".
\tst Tst3:  How was the servant haunted by a demon?  She was haunted by a demon and
said the future because she did not know Jesus and God's Words, so the demon went in
her.
\tst Tst3:  How did it make her tell the future?  The demons are not one, they are many. 
They knew what was going to happen.  Like, they knew Paul and Silas were coming and
could tell the way to be saved.  They knew but the demons could not take Paul and Silas
and the people who follow Jesus.  Demons cannot take these people.
\tst Tst4:  In retelling, she states, "While they were going (omits "God's praising place", they
met a servant woman.  The servant woman had a demon in her.  Her demon made her
tell the future."  "God's praising place" will be changed to "God's praying house" to match
keyterm.  Revised.
\ln 58.11
\bt She used to get a lot of money from her fortune-telling, that she gave
to her chief.
\anc Act.16:16
\tst How did the servant girl get money?  She knows certain things about the future.  She
sells this service. What does the word for "chief" here mean?  It means "patron",
employer or owner.
\tst Tst3:  Why did she give the money to her chief?  Because she was the worker.  When
you are the worker, you give or do as your chief says.
\tst Tsts:  Line retold as original.  
\ln 58.12
\bt So she followed them by saying, "These are God's workers, Those who

\old So she followed them by saying, "These are God's workers, Those who are showing us

\anc Act.16:17
\tst Why was she saying this to Paul and Silas?  They are God's workers and are showing
people how to be saved.  She knows that Paul and Silas are good.
\tst Tst2:  How are Paul and Silas showing people the way to be saved?  The girl had a
demon and she didn't know what she was saying.  God put the words in her.
\tst Tst2:  In the retelling, the exact words that the demon girl was shouting to Paul were not
remembered.  He also mistakenly said she was saying, "These are the saviors."  We will
relook at this section, possibly using repetition to make it clearer and more memorable. 
Or cohesively use what is used in line 01 to describe Good News as what the

\tst Tst3:  In retelling, he does state, "These are God's workers", but states, "They are our

\tst Tst4:  In retelling, she says, "These are God's messengers, doing His work."

\ln 58.13
\bt By saying that continually, it hurt Paul.  
\anc Act.16:18
\tst How does "it hurt Paul" mean?  Provide example.  Example:  There is sickness
everywhere in our family here.  The sickness "hurts" us.  When the heat from hot season
is upon us, the heat "hurts" us.  It was further explained that this is the equivalent of
something "tiring" us, "fatigue" in French.
\tst Tst2:  How does this hurt Paul?  She was saying it all the time, all the time, all the time.
\ln 58.14
\bt Then Paul said to the demon, "In the {name} of Jesus, with the
{power} of Jesus, I demand you to leave that woman."  And the
demon left.
\old Then Paul said to the demon, "In the {name} of Jesus, leave that woman."  And the

\anc Act.16:18
\tst How does Paul get the demon to leave?  He begs [prays to] God and the spirit leaves.  
\tst Tst3:  Why does Paul say, "In the name of Jesus"?  Because Jesus is their boss and
teacher.  He taught them so now they work in his name.  What does saying "In the name
of Jesus" do?  Because they work for Jesus, in his name.  If they had just said, "Demons
leave" they would not have left the woman but because they said "In Jesus name" the
demons knew who they were working for and left them.  How did the demons know Paul
and Silas worked for Jesus?  The people of Philippi knew because Paul and Silas had
come to tell them the words about Jesus.  They all knew that Paul and Silas were for
Jesus.
\tst Tst2:  In line 14, the phrase "In the name of Jesus" was omitted in retelling.
\tst Tst3:  In retelling he states, "He said to the demon, "leave this woman, in the name of
Jesus."
\tst Tst4:  In retelling, she states, "In the name of Jesus, demon, leave that woman."  And
the demon left the servant woman."
\tst Tsts:  While testing respondents 3 and 4 did retell "in the name of Jesus", this is the first
usage of the phrase "in the name of Jesus" in the story set.  It will be unpacked to say,
"in the name of Jesus, and with the power of Jesus, I demand you to leave that
woman."  Revised.
\ln 58.15

\ln 58.16a

\ln 58.16b

\anc Act.16:20 -21
\cn BK:  The phrase "to make disorder" means that they were causing trouble in the village. 
It was further explained that the people can not follow Paul and Silas.  They should not
accept the words they are saying or the things they are doing.
\tst Why do they arrest Paul and Silas?  The girl can't tell the future anymore.  She can't find

\tst How do the girl's patrons explain why they are arresting them?  Paul and Silas' words
are not good.  They want to mix-up their village.
\tst Tst2:  Why are these people angry at Paul and Silas?  The workers work is now bad. 
The demon has left and there is no more work.  They can't get money anymore.  The
words/future left her.
\tst Tst3:  How did they make disorder?  Because they had made the demon leave the
woman and this wasn't good for her chief.  So he went and made disorder with the
village leaders.  He says they made the disorder because it wasn't good for him.
\tst Tst: Lines 15-16 are retold as is (Tst3 and Tst4) and will not be changed.  
\ln 58.17
\bt At the {moment} they said that, the authorities took Paul and Silas'

\old At the moment they said that, the authorities asked them to take Paul and Silas' clothes

\anc Act.16:22 - 23

\ln 58.18
\old So they took Paul and Silas' clothes off, beat them, and put them in jail.
\anc Act.16:23
\tst Tst3:  Why did they beat them and put them in jail?  Because they had said God's Words

village - Paul and Silas made this disorder, so they went to the village leaders becaues
they wanted them to be beat.  So the took them and beat them.  Here, the other day,
when I went to eat lunch, I got to my house and a man had come to rob my neighbor -
they had him tied up.  They were going to beat him and put him in jail.  You don't cause
disorder here.
\tst Tst2:  There is a bit of repetition in line 17 and 18 that was not in the retelling.  This
could potentially be shortened.  In line 18, the location of the "small room" was not in the
retelling and could be omitted as it's importance in the story is not great.

\tst Tst4:  In retelling, repetition was omitted.  Lines 17-18 retold as, "The authorities

\ln 58.19
\bt The authorities warned the guardian of the prison to take care of them
seriously.
\anc Act.16:23
\cn BK:  Here the phrase "take care" better means "guard".  In this context, the phrase
"take care of" is not in the "good" sense of the term, but to prevent them from fleeing
away.
\tst Tst3:  Why did the authorities tell the guardian to "guard them seriously"?  So that they
could not escape and go to another village.  They beat them and put them in the small
room in the other rooms of the prison to guard them seriously, so they could not leave.
\tst Tst3:  In retelling this line was rephrased to, "And they told the guard of the jail to take
them."
\tst Tst4:  In retelling, the line was rephrased to , "They gave them to the guard of the jail." 
In tst2, this was retold as is, and will remain in the story to place emphasize that the
authorities gave the task of guarding the prisoners to the guardian.
\ln 58.20

\anc Act.16:24

\tst Tst3:  Why did the guardian put them in a room behind the other rooms?  Because if
they were out, they would of run off.  
\tst Tst3:  Line retold as is.  
\tst Tst4:  Line retold as is.  
\ln 58.21
\bt At the moment the earth was cold, Paul and Silas started praying to
God {KT: pray}, praising God, and singing.  Then all the prisoners were
listening to them.
\anc Act.16:25
\cn MM:  The phrase "the moment the earth was cold" is the exact same phrase used in the
Supyire translation.  When asked about it, it was explained that this is the late hour of
the night in which everyone is asleep.  There is no noise and no one is walking around. 
They told me it may be between the hours of 1 am and 3 am.
\tst Why were Paul and Silas praying and singing?  They want God to help them.  God will
grant strength to them.  
\tst Tst2:  Why were Paul and Silas praying and praising God?  They wanted God to help
them and give them peace.  They weren't at peace in that place.  They wanted God to
give life back to them and take them out.
\tst Tst3:  Why were the other prisoners listening to Paul and Silas?  Because they were
praying to God  and praising him.  The others could not leave and they did not believe
them.  But they were scared because they were in prison.  So they listened a lot to
them.
\ln 58.22
\bt Later on, the earth shakes and all the prison walls started shaking
also.
\anc Act.16:26
\tst Tst2:  How did the earth shake?  As God makes it thunder in the sky, as He makes the
sky shake, He shakes the ground.
\tst Tst2:  In retelling, instead of saying the "earth shook and the prison walls shook", in the
retelling he said "the house shook".
\tst Tst3:  in retelling, he states, "Then, the earth shakes."  He omitted the "prison walls
started shaking also." and went straight to "And the doors of the prison opened."
\tst Tst4:  In retelling she also states, "Then, all the earth shook.  And the doors of the
prison opened."  In both of these latest retellings, the "prison walls started shaking also"
was not retold and can be deleted.  Maintained as it was retold in final recordings.  This
phrase was retold in Tst2 (BT as "the house shook")
\ln 58.23
\bt The door of the prison opened.  All the chains used to tie the prisoners
cut.
\anc Act.16:26
\tst Tst2:  How were the chains cut?  As the sky shakes, as the ground shakes, God's

\tst Tst3:  How did the prison doors open?  They were praying  to God and praising him when
the earth and the building shook.  That is what opened the doors.
\tst Tst3:  Line retold as original.  "Chains" and "cut" are same wording as original.  
\tst Tst4:  Also, retold as original.  
\ln 58.24
\bt When the guardian of the prison awaked and saw the doors open, he

\anc Act.16:27
\cn BK:  Here the word "left" means that he thought the prisoners "escaped".  
\tst Why did the guard want to kill himself?  He woke up and saw the prison doors open and

\tst Tst2:  Why did the guard take the knife?  He was scared, the doors were opened.  He

\tst Tst3:  Why was the guard afraid?  Because he thought that everybody had left and his
chief would then kill him, like me, when I sleep here and Zanga (his chief) yells at me,
it's not good.
\tst Tst4:  In retelling, she states, "The guardian of the prison woke and found the doors

\tst Tst3:  In retelling, this line was retold as is and will not be changed.

\tst Why did he ask them this?  He knew Paul and Silas knew God's road.  He wanted to be

\tst Tst2:  Why does the guard want to be released from his sins?  The things he's done

\tst Tst3:  Why would the guard want to be released from his sin?  Because he knew that

\ln Futher Comments from Back-Translation Session
\tst What do you think people will understand from the story?  If the villagers listen to the
story, to my understanding, it will show them that the judgment here on earth is inferior
to God‚Äôs ones. Why?  Because if you take the case of Paul and Silas, they sent them to
jail and with God‚Äôs help, the earth starts shaking and all the doors open.  Why?  Because
God was following what Paul and Silas were doing.  It means they were right, but for
human beings they were wrong.  But God was the one who released them from the
hands of the unbelievers ‚Äì the guardian and the chiefs.  In sum, only God we should
trust.  He is the best judge.

\dt 02/Jan/2009

\c 60
\t Return
\co Supyire
\p
\co Redemptive Theme:  It is through belief in Jesus that one is on God's road and is
saved.  Those who believe in Jesus, God will save.  They will go above and be with
God forever because of the good relationship that Jesus has placed between them
and God.  God's power and ultimate provision are seen in giving man access to God's
power over death, providing man with everlasting life with God.
\co Basic Biblical concepts: persecution of believers, coming day of judgment , Jesus'
return, resurrection of the body, eternal life with God.
\co Cohesion / Background:  Jesus' followers continue sharing about Jesus.  There is still
evil in this world - presence of jealousy, evil spirits, the enemy Satan.  Reminder
that Jesus was the "Savior they were waiting for".
\co Worldview/Selection:  Based on the often synchronizing of religious beliefs and the
possibility of persecution and suffering from family and others, there is emphasis on
the words of Paul to the believers that they "turned their back on their fetishes" and
have believed in Jesus, not leaving His road even in suffering.
\p
\co Story Craftor:  SS
\co Story Backtranslator:  BK
\p
\co Resources Used in crafting:  Audio of French Bible- Parole de Vie, Bambara Bible,
Supyire NT draft
\p
\co Audio Last Revised: 20Oct08
\co BT file Last Revised: 21Oct08  
\p

with the level of detail maintained.  Discrepancy in retelling have been noted below as
Tst3 (retest) comments.

\ln 60.25
\bt You have turned your {backs} to your fetishes {KT: fetish} and

\anc 1th.01:06 , 1th.03:03 - 08 , 
\anc TN 1th.03:03, The phrase, "by these trials": "This phrase refers to the persecutions that
the Thessalonian believers were suffering. The same Greek word was translated
‚Äúsuffering‚Äù.  TN 03:06 states, "good news about your faith: This refers to the good news
that the Thessalonians were still continuing to believe strongly in Christ."
\anc TN 1Th.03:07-08 states, "Because of that which Timothy has told us , brothers, even
though we suffer much because people are persecuting us, we were encouraged about
you because of your faith. we have become encouraged about you, because we heard
that you are still trusting in Christ.
\tst Why are they following the Lord? because they know that God's road is the only good

is in this story.
\ln 60.28

\ln 60.29
\bt Those who died that were on his road, he will {rise} them from
death.  
\old He is going to raise {KT: rise} the dead from death.
\anc 1th.04:16 , TW says in TN, "Most English versions understand this to refer to those who
believed in Christ before they died, that is, ‚Äúbelievers who have died‚Äù will rise first: This
means that the believers who have already died will become alive again, before those
who are still living go to meet Christ in the air. It does not mean that those who have
died will rise into the air before those who are still living."
\tst How is he going to raise the dead from death?  Because God is going to give him the
power to do it
\tst Tst3:  Why would the dead rise from death?  Because he did not die and stay dead.  So
when he comes, he will do the same for his disciples.  How?  He is God's Son.  He will
pray, "God bring up my disciples from death" and they will come because God agrees
with (accepts) His Son.
\tst Tst3:  In retelling he stated, "He will come, he will come and let death, he left death."
\tst tst4:  In retelling he stated, "and raise the dead
\tst I suggest changing this to, "He will come and raise the dead who had walked on his
road."  See Revised Line.
\tst Tst3(retest):  Here in retelling, he continued to say "those who believed in Jesus";
however, there are many ways to say this, and the road analogy is easy to understand
and has been retold in previous stories.  Also, this testor had recently heard previous
versions of the story and may have still had this previous version in mind.

\tst How will all of them be with him above?   Because of his power and because he saved us

\tst Tst2:  Why will Jesus take those alive who are for him above?  If they like Jesus, they
get to go with him and if the do not, they stay here.
\tst Tst3:  Why will he take those who are for him above?  Because they believe in him, they
will be with Jesus in God's kingdom forever.
\tst tst3:  In retelling he stated, "The disciples who have died will get up.  These people will

\tst Tst4:  She retold this line as is.

\ln 60.31

\old and be with him in God's {kingdom} forever."
\anc 1th.04:17

we will be with him
\tst Tst3:  How can they be with him in God's Kingdom forever?  Because Jesus is like God. 
When he brings us up, we will be with him forever.  We will not die.
\tst Tst3:  Why would you want to be in God's Kingdom forever?  Because I can understand
and know God's Words.  I will not be tired or suffer.  I can be there forever.  We will not
suffer in God's Kingdom because there is nothing bad there.  No badness there, only the

\ln 60.32
\bt This day, those who believe in Jesus, God will save {KT: Savior} them
from his anger.  
\old This day, those who believe in Jesus, God will save {KT: Savior} them from the fire that
cannot be extinguished.  
\anc Anchor for "when this day comes" - 1th.05:02
\anc 1th.05:09 , TN states, "Paul meant that God deliberately chose (or destined) to save
those who have trusted in Jesus, rather than to punish them as he will punish the
unbelievers.
\anc TW, Index of Implicit Information, 1Th.05:09, "destine us for God's future punishment of
unrepentant sinners"
\cn MM:  Here again, the Supyire word for "anger" is expressed in terms of a "raised
heart".  
\tst Tst3 (retest):  How can we be saved from the fire that cannot be extinguished?  When
we do not believe in Jesus, we are put in the fire.  But when we believe in Jesus, he goes
to God and tells God that we have believed in him and then God does not put us in the
fire.  This is because Jesus is our Savior.
\ln 60.33
\bt Why?  Because those who believe in Jesus are on God's road.  There
will be a good {relationship} between them and God.
\old Why?  Because Jesus has put back together a good {relationship} between us and God.  
\anc 1th.05:09 -10
\anc TN 1th.05:09, "On the contrary, he destined us to be saved from being punished by
means of what our Lord Jesus Christ has done for us.
\anc NIV Study Bible 1th.05:10, In reference to "with Him" , "To be Christ's, is to have
entered a relationship that nothing can destroy."
\tst Tst3 (retest):  How can we have a good relationship with God?  Because we believe in
Jesus.  Because we believe in him, God forgives us for our bad things.  We have a good
relationship with God because then we are one.  We now work as one with God.
\tst TSt3 (retest):  How can having a good relationship with God save us from the fire? 
Because we believe in Jesus, God saves us.
\tst Tst3 (retest):  How does Jesus put back together the relationship between us and God? 
Because we believe in him, he goes to God and says - God they believe in me, forgive
them, do not put them in the fire - so Jesus is the one who puts our relationship back
together.
\tst Tst3 (retest):  Why is it good for us to have a good relationship with God?  Because
when we do have a good relationship, God helps us, we work as one - that is good for
us.  God will not put us in the fire to be burned.
\tst Tst3 (retest):  Why only the people who believe in Jesus will he save from the fire? 
Because they believe in Jesus, he will save them.  Those who believe in the fetishes will
find the fire.  Those who believe in Jesus will be with him and not in the fire, but all those
who do not believe in him will be in the fire that cannot be extinguished.
\tst ***Tst3 (retest):  In retelling, he states, "Why?  Because there is now a good
relationship between us and God."  As this is the only place in the story set where the
concept of "putting back together" is used, we will rephrase this to say in more natural
words, "Why?  Because those who believe in Jesus and take his road, have a good
relationship with God."  This cohesively ties the redemptive theme of belief in Jesus, to
being on Jesus' road, to being saved by God from His judgment, and gaining life forever
with God.  Also, in researching the concept of "restored" relationship within the NT draft,
it does not appear to use this word used above for "put back together" in the context of
relationship.  However, the draft simply states that is is because of Jesus, that there is
now a good relationship..."  See relationship in L&C Notes.

\c 97
\t ONESTORY TOOLBOX HELPS
\co TO ADD A NEW STORY RECORD: 
\co2 1. place the cursor in the story BT window, click on Database / Insert Record. 
\co2 2. It will ask you for the Record you want to insert--so you should write a new chapter
number (be sure to insert a zero before single digit numbers)--try to estimate where the
story will come in your story set.
\co2 3. Click ok. 
\co2 4. A new record will open and you can begin to key in the story and anchors. 
\co2 4. The template will automatically give you 30 linenumbers. You can change them from
"02.xx" to whatever chapter number you gave, by using Edit / Replace. Make sure that
you leave the period after the number.
\co2 5. Choose the "replace all" button. Hit "ok".

\co TO SEE YOUR WHOLE LIST OF STORIES
\co2 1. If you want to see titles as well as chapter numbers, click on View / Browse Fields.  A
window will open up with a list of all available fields. Highlight "t" and click "last" to move
it to the right.
\co2 2. Click "ok"
\co2 3. Click on the three-column icon above to see an index of your stories -- both chapter
numbers and titles.

\co TO ADD A FIELD:  
\co2 1. Click on Enter, and then "\"-- this brings up a list of Standard Format markers that this
window can use.
\co2 2. Click on the marker you want, hit space and your cursor will be back in the window
you can write in.

\co TO DELETE A RECORD:  
\co2 1. VERY IMPORTANT:  Click in the window of the record you want to delete.  
\co2 2. Click on Database / Delete record
\co2 3. Select "yes"

\co TO ARRANGE YOUR WINDOWS:  
\co2 1. Click on Window
\co2 2. Choose the type of arrangement you want for your windows (cascade, tile, tile side by
side) -- OR just drag each window to where you want it, and then resize it to fit.

\co TO SEND A BACKTRANSLATION RECORD TO A CONSULTANT:  
\co2 1. Click in the back-translation window 
\co2 2. Click on File / Export - select "standard format" and select "show properties dialog box
on export"
\co2 3. Click on the "export" button - another window will open.  If the "consistent changes"
field has anything in it, make it blank.
\co2 4. Hit the "browse" button on the "output file" field - another window will open 
\co2 5. Give your file a name with a ".txt" extension and hit save. 
\co2 6. Go to your email program and create a new email to your consultant.  Attach the file
that you just exported from Toolbox.

\co TO ADD A RECORD FROM A CONSULTANT:  
\co2 1. Save the text file to your project folder.
\co2 2. In your Toolbox project click on File / Open, and select the file from your consultant,
click Open.
\co2 3. In the dialogue box that opens, (if the file is a Consultant Notes file) touch the little
down arrow in the middle selection box, and select StoryNotes.
\co2 4. Click Ok
\co2 5. With the curson in the window that opens, click on Database / Copy Record.
\co2 6. Choose the ConNotes (or whatever your Consultant Notes database is called).
\co2 7. Click Ok.

\co OR
\co2 1. Double-click on e-mail attachment to open it.  
\co2 2. Select all the text in the document.  
\co2 3. Copy the highlighted text. 
\co2 4. Click in the Consultant Notes window in Toolbox 
\co2 5. Go to the record number that you are working with - highlight the entire record. 
\co2 6. Paste to replace the old copy of the file with the new updated one.

\co TO SEND A CONSULTANT NOTES FILE BACK TO THE CONSULTANT (with your
answers in it)
\co2 1. Click in the ConNotes window
\co2 2. Hit "file", then "export" - select "standard format" and select "show properties dialog
box on export"
\co2 3. Hit the "export" button - another window will open.  Make the "consistent changes"
field blank.
\co2 4. Hit the "browse" button on the "output file" field - another window will open 
\co2 6. Go to your email program and create a new email to your consultant.  Attach the file
that you just exported from Toolbox.

\ln line number--this should match the line number in the ConNotes file, use the
format xx.xx
\ln To JUMP from the \ln field in this window to the equivalent \ln field in the
ConNotes window, rightclick on the number.
\bt backtranslation (keep your lines fairly short)
\bt to JUMP: From this line you can jump to records you have made in the
keyterms database. For example, if this line had the word "God" in it,
and if you have made a keyterm record called "God", then a rightclick
on the word "God" will immediately bring up the record in the
keyterms database.
\anc anchor ref -- If you are working with a language for which there is translated scripture
with a backtraslation, it would be helpful to your consultant for you to paste the BT of the
appropriate vss.
\anc to JUMP from anc to NETBIBLE rightclick on the reference here (eg. Gen.01:01) and your
cursor will immediately bring up the verse in the Netbible window
\cn Crafting note -- put cultural info here, or reasons why you crafted the story in a certain
way, or information about this line from your testing groups.
\cn to JUMP: From this line you can also reference records you have made of Cultural
observations. For example, if this line of the story is about the Wedding at Cana, and
you have made observations about weddings in the group you work with, A rightclick on
the word Wedding will jump to the "Wedding" record in the Cultural notes database.
(Note that in order for the jump to work, the Cultural Notes database needs to be sorted
by \r)
\tst testing question -- prepare testing questions ahead of time.  Then put the response here
also.
\old A preivous version of this line of this line of the story.  As you proceed through testing
and editing of the story you occasionally decide to delete a line or to make major
changes. If you do that, we'd like for you to keep old versions of each line--especially if
there have been consultant comments about it.
\dt 07/Dec/2008

\t LINE NUMBERS TEMPLATE
\co use the following numbers to paste into the records (there are 99, hopefully you
won't need all of them--just select the ones you will use), then in the Menu above,
click on Edit/Replace (be sure to set the "Field" to "ln Line number" click on "current
record only". In the "text to find" type "99.", and in the "replace with" type in the
appropriate chapter number followed by a dot, then click "replace".

\c 99
\t SAMPLE STORY (Title goes in this line) 
\co (Language name or code goes here) 
\co Reason for having this story in the set

\ln 01.01
\bt After David became king and was settled in his palace,  
\anc 2Sa.07:01
\ln 01.02
\bt one day he was with his spiritual advisor, Nathan, and he said to him: 
Look!  Here I am living in this beautiful palace, but the place of
worshipping and the holy case for consulting God is out in a tent.
\anc 2Sa.07:02 
\ln 01.03
\bt Nathan said to him:  "Well, go ahead and do what you have in mind,
because God is with you. 
\anc 2Sa.07:03 
\ln 01.04
\bt But that night Nathan perceived from God that he was guiding him a
different way. 
\anc 2Sa.07:04 
\ln 01.05
\bt And he went back to David and said to him:
\anc 2Sa.07:17  
\ln 01.06
\bt <<Here is a message from God for you:  Who are you to build ME a
house? 
\anc 2Sa.07:05 (NLT) ìGo and tell my servant David, ëThis is what the Lord says: Are you the
one to build me a temple to live in?
\ln 01.07
\bt I chose you when you were just a shepherd boy taking care of your
sheep out in the pasture, and raised you up to be king of your people,
the Israelites.
\anc 2Sa.07:08 
\bt And I have gotten rid of your enemies. 
\anc 2Sa.07:09 
\ln 01.08
\bt Now  instead of you making ME a house, I am going to make YOU a
house, a royal "house" of David, a dynasty of kings that will go on for
all time.
\anc 2Sa.07:11 (the Lord will build his "house")
\anc 2Sa.07:16 (his dynasty will be permanent)
\ln 01.09
\bt You will have a son, and he will build my house, a temple where
people can worship me. And the line of his descendants will go on
being kings forever.>>
\anc 2Sa.07:12 -13
\cn Temple recurs in various stories.
\ln 01.10
\bt When David heard this, he went to the tent of worship, sat down in
God's presence, and prayed.  He said:  "Oh all-powerful God, Who am I
that you have brought me this far?
\anc 2Sa.07:18 
\cn NOTE: re. "went in to the tent" -- HBK says: The fact that he entered into the tent where
the ark was housed (see 6.17; 7.2) is implied in the expression "before the Lord"
\ln 01.11
\bt And now you are talking about the kingdom and rule of my
descendents going on forever.   
\anc 2Sa.07.19  
\ln 01.12 
\bt So may it happen just like you have promised.  
\anc 2Sa.07.25 
\ln 01.13 
\bt Because when you speak, it is the truth. And this is what you have
promised to me, your SERVANT.
\anc 2Sa.07.28  
\cn Servant becomes a sub-theme in this panorama, first with David referring to himself as
God's servant, then referring to the Messiah, and then with believers calling themselves
servants of God.
\dt 07/Dec/2008
